But if you are pool loungers - its perfect!My fiance became ill while we where there and we called the hotel doctor. He was there in 15 minutes! And since we didn't rent a car and it was at night, the head of security himself went to Walgreen's to drop off and pick up my fiance's prescriptions for us! The staff was wonderful!We did end up renting a car the next to last day we were there to drive into Old San Juan for the day. Everything is at the hotel. Car Rentals, excursions, an incidentals and souvenier shop, a small casino and outdoor and indoor event space (saw a wedding, birthdays and a Quincinera). The food was very good, but there really wasn't a large variety - only 2 restaurants (one Italian) and the other either Asian Fusion or Habatchi (one restaurant with two sides). No buffet in the evening - only for breakfast. There was also just the pool bar or restaurant for lunch. We are late eaters, so if you tend to eat late - make sure you get there no later than 9 pm. However, the staff was very gracious when we arrived 15 minutes before they closed for the evening. The bar and lounge is beautiful and large - they have live dancing/music and then a DJ.The only downsides we experienced was the room smelled a bit musty, but it wasn't anything we couldn't deal with. And we were a bit concerned that the person who checked us in didn't explain the extent of their meal plans when we purchased. I.e., there were restrictions to certain plans that we didn't know exsisted until we met and started chatting with another couple there. Again, not a huge deal for us, but if you are drinkers - make sure they clarify at what times the meal plan includes alcoholic beverages.Otherwise get to the Gran Melia - they have a lot going on and lots more going on for them in the future too (Trump bought the golf course and its one of his now. <Author>Moochanator
<Content>Held Hostage at the Gran Melia My wife and I stayed at the Gran Melia as part of a conference. We've stayed in many nice resorts and hotels but we've never stayed in a resort that went so far out of it's way to take advantage of the guests. The illusion of luxury is little more than an overwrought resort experience lacquered over modern-day resort piracy.You begin your sentence with a $35/person shuttle to the resort. You can rent a car in San Juan but they charge you about $15-20 a day to park it. Each group's calculus may differ but we should have rented a car in San Juan. The Avis agency in the actual resort charged me a little over $70 to rent their subcompact for the day. In the end, the resort does everything they can to keep there, preferably running up your bar tab.The food was outrageously overpriced and not very good. Your dinner options include an Asian Fusion, Italian, and a sort of Caribbean themed Cafe. (During our stay one was closed each night) The portions were very small and the dishes, while very artistically plated, were substandard. I asked to see a wine list but was dismayed when A) half the wines were not actually available and B) the rest cost almost as much as my airfare. There's also atmosphere problems- you're not close enough to the ocean, the napkins are disposable, and since there's no casual (or cheaper) place for dinner, half the guests look like bums. Olive Garden or Red Lobster would have been a substantial improvement. The waitstaff was polite, but not very charismatic, helpful, knowledgeable, or experienced.While Gran Melia's grounds get high marks for being immaculate, it has atmosphere problems, too. No actual sand was harmed in the making of the beach. It's rocky, silty, and not great for swimming. A walk at dusk on the beach led us to discover hundreds of tiny hermit crabs which was enough to make my inner naturalist jump for joy.  The pool is enormous, which is great, but there's no shade. After seeing the pool at the Rio Mar resort I realized how disappointing the Melia's sun-baked pool was. A hot tub/spa is available for those guests that wish to spend $28 for a one-day spa membership. Gran Melia's lodging sprawls across 16 different multi-room bungalows and a handful of more expensive villas. The rooms themselves are exquisite with marble tile and nice fixtures. The compounds are connected by paths that are adorned by tropical plants, immaculate bermudagrass, and endemic iguanas. (My wife and I found the large iguanas endearing but other guests were a little put off) I liked walking the paths but I grew weary of the golf carts that the staff used, buzzing through and roaring like B-29s while I dove for the bushes. The rooms were nice but there weren't bathrobes or sandals or any of the other sundries you might expect from true luxury establishments. Our unit's air conditioner only worked 50% of the time but I'm not a real A/C-o-phile so it didn't bother me that much. I imagine that it was a problem with our room and not with every room.The Casino was a little anemic-.a Casino without craps is like a prom date without a corsage- in bluejeans.Puerto Rico has SO MANY awesome things to do close together that I don't know why I would stay in a resort that penalized you for wanting to get out and see them on your own.Pros: Beautiful Grounds, RoomsCons: Food, Location, Beach, just about everything else.

We ate Asian one night, not that expensive,Italian another night, not that expensive, (NY prices) The cafe which serves breakfast, lunch and dinner cost more. They have buffets for breakfast and dinner. Breakfast was $15. for continental, which included anything cold, and the regular buffet was $22.00. Not worth it unless you had a very big appetite. We ate one night at Riches, which was a restaurant that would come and pick you up and bring you back. They had a mixture Puerto Rican or American food, so you could enjoy anything you wanted. The view was magnifcent.Bring your camera. If you have a car and want to experience some real PR cuisine, go left on Rt. 3 towards Luquillo. You will see a sign that says Kiosks. Exit on the right and make a left turn under the highway and then another left turn and go into where the Kiosks are. There are numerous food establishments that sell local food. The first place was really good. Well, that is all I can say. The hotel was great, even the casino. We won, but then put it back, but the odds were better here than in the other casinos we played at. <Author>rkl1130
<Content>Beautiful Gounds and Service but Far My husband and I decided to stay at the Gran Melia despite mixed reviews because it looked nice and we were not disappointed. The grounds are impeccable, staff friendly, everything clean and rooms spacious and everything gorgeous. The hotel has a beautiful 24 hour pool with a swim up bar and grill. They also have a beach with chairs set out that is great and you can rent kayaks and paddle boats on.I did, however, have a few negative things. The property has few dining selections--some of which were not open everyday. This hotel is far from everything so without a car, you are stuck and the prices are fairly high. There is also no authentic Puerto Rican restaurant on site, which is highly disappointing because when traveling we like to eat local. Again, the property is far and there isn't much to do and they don't provide free shuttles. In addition, I felt like they charged for every single thing which was annoying.Despite that, we still enjoyed our stay but would recommend that you rent a car because it will be pricey to go out.

<Author>YogiTravels
<Content>Starving and trapped at the Gran Melia I have no complaints for the property or the hospitality. My main issues were the lack of Puerto Rican food in a hotel in Puerto Rico!!! There are only three restaurants on the resort and they were all pretty pricey. I don't know about anybody else but when I go to any place new I like to sample the local cuisine. No such luck at the Gran Melia, your only options were Japanese, Italian and a buffet style restaurant that was closed the first two days I was there. There was a pool bar but it closed at 6:00 and I arrived the first night at 6:30. Of course I had the option of room service but that was ridiculously overpriced. There was a food cart that another patron recommend to me for breakfast. The cart had bagels and things like that, and I was able to get something once, but then the cart was closed during the remainder of my stay. So much for the cheap breakfast. I did speak to several of the staff about the lack of local cuisine and they told me a lot of the hotel guests had complained about the same thing, but management deemed the guests would prefer the type of restaurants that were more tourist friendly. Listen if I wanted Japanese or Italian I would have stayed home. So my advice is to pack lots of snacks, or stop in San Juan for food on your way to the hotel.My other recommendation for future travelers to this establishment is for you to make sure that you rent a car if you stay here. It is so far from everything and there is no other affordable means of transportation. I asked about transport to San Juan and was told it would be $80 one way by taxi. So needless to say I was stuck on the hotel grounds for the duration of my stay.I thought the staff was very nice and very helpful and the grounds were absolutely gorgeous, but I would not stay there again based on my experience.

<Author>gipsy61
<Content>Fabulous My Husband and I and another couple spent 5 nights (Sept 14-19) at the Gran Melia and we all had a great time from start to end. We had considered other hotels (Inter-Continental, Ritz-Carlton, Rio Mar, Marriott, and El Conquistador) but in the end we decided we didn't want to stay in San Juan, we didn't want a large property, and we wanted to be close to El Yunque.I read all the reviews as I always do when we travel and I know that you can't always please everyone. I myself am hard to please and can usually find something that isn't up to par however, not this time. Roundtrip airport transportation was included in our package and we were met by a very nice young lady (sorry I misplaced her name) as soon as we came down the escalator by baggage claim and we were at the hotel within 25 minutes courtesy of our driver Cesar. We were introduced to our Butler Hector who told us not worry about anything anymore and we were led to the Royal Service Lounge for check-in and offered cold drinks.Check-in went smoothly thanks to the ladies of the RS lounge, Veronica, Omyra, Sara, and Angelica (I know I've forgotten one or two more names...sorry!) who were always friendly, gracious and helpful. We arrived early and our rooms weren't quite ready so we went to lunch and by 2:30PM, Hector was giving us a tour of the resort on the way to Bungalow #18, when he left he gave us his cell# and said to call if we needed anything!We both reserved Ocean Front Royal Service Junior Suite rooms and although we thought a ground level room would be good either Omyra or Veronica suggested the second level for more privacy with the Jacuzzi on the balcony and we were so glad they did! Our room was exactly as pictured on the website with the canopy over the bed, large bathroom (huge shower with great water pressure and drainage) with plenty of towels and bath amenities, big balcony with 2 person Jacuzzi and a fabulous view of the ocean.Before dinner we had a few drinks in the RS lounge (our rooms were really warm but the RS staff said they would take care of it and by the time we returned to our room that night our rooms were much cooler and we never had another problem with the air). We had dinner at Nami, the Asian restaurant, and we all had a delicious meal and was surprised when the bill came considering some reviews stating that it was expensive, we thought it was quite reasonably! Nami is actually like 4 restautants in one; Hibachi, Sushi. Teppanyaki, and then outdoor dining over the water, we ate there a few times and it felt like a different place each time. We also ate at Tempo and loved it (also reasonably priced). The resorts open-air lobby is beautiful with floral arrangements everywhere, lots of comfortable sitting areas, and a really cool bar, The Avenue, with lounges and palapas. Very relaxing, exotic music is played all day and night, and at night candles are lit everywhere, the grounds are beautiful and are constantly being tended to by the staff. The main pool is huge with lounge chairs partially submerged in the water, a swim-up bar, jacuzzi's in the middle of the pool, plenty of lounge chairs, and palapas (Bali beds) that can be had for the day for a fee.The casino is on the small side but that wasn't an issue with any of us. One afternoon while the guys went kayaking, we went to the Spa, our Butler Manuel made the arrangements. I had the Rain Forest Body Glow Scrub with Yadira, followed by more down time in the spa jacuzzi and pool, it was fabulous!Continental breakfast was included as part of the RS package however, if you wanted the full buffet breakfast it was just an additional $7, we thought it was well worth it. The restaurant's host - Angel, was always friendly and helpful, the staff were attentive and always smiling, and Gregorio the Chef prepared the best waffles, cheesey potatoes, and various Puerto Rican specialties each morning. When we go on vacation I always try to get a deep soaking tub to bubble bath in, my daily life is so busy I rarely have the time to luxuriate in a bathtub so I was really looking forward to our balcony jacuzzi. You can't imagine how thrilled I was when we came back after dinner that first night and my husband called me out on the balcony, it was the best bubble bath/jacuzzi I ever had for no less than 5 reasons . I could describe it but I would rather you go and be surprised yourself, many thanks to our fabulous Butler Mario who made me a wonderful jacuzzi almost night!We loved the RS pool which is exclusively for RS guests (no kids). The pool has it's own bar, is surrounded by palapas, and played soothing music, we loved it so much we stayed all day even having lunch there. Sergio and Leslie were perfect and took great care of us: we loved the cold, scented towels, they were so refreshing, it was heaven!One day we rented a car (thanks Gina, hope your Mom is well!) and went to El Yunque, the light house in Fajardo, and Luquillo. We had a great time, the rain forest was beautiful, went to the tower, hiked to the waterfall and swam in the pool underneath it! The beach at Luquillo was very nice but we thought the beach at the Hotel was just as good. Yes- it was rocky, yes there was grass in the water but it didn't matter, we loved the beach and we found a lot of beautiful shells there (just be sure there aren't any hermit crabs in them).Many thanks also to our Butlers Angel and Marco you made us feel special while we were your guests! Also the Housekeeping staff were great, our room was always clean and taken care of in a timely manner. I think you really have to know what you want or can reasonable expect, in order to be happy with what you get. We loved the two story bungalows, the beautiful grounds, friendly staff, delicious food, relaxing atmosphere, and the RS treatment was so worth it, I would never book this hotel group again without it ! I have recommended Gran Melia to everyone and will definitely stay there when in PR!.

<Author>ladausa
<Content>Not as bad as some reviews make you believe After booking our stay at Gran Melia, I started reading all the bad reviews posted here, and got a bit worried. However, it's definitely not as bad as others have mentioned. One caveat - we were there during the low season, and the resort was virtually empty. A rental car is an absolute must if you're staying there - there's nothing within walking distance but a golf course. Location: The resort is located about 20 miles east of the airport, on a little peninsula. The location is great if you want to go to San Juan (30 min), rain forest (15 min), Fajardo (30 min) - as long as you have a car.Finding the hotel: It's so new, GPS (or Google Maps) does not have it's street address, however, as you take Route 3 east from San Juan, there's a huge sign pointing to the hotel. Parking:Parking is not free, and on weekend night there are a lot of locals who come to the casino, but we never had problems finding a spot (or parking right alongside the drive if there were no spots).Check-in:There were two employees checking people in, and it took us all of 5 minutes to check in. The do put a hold of $150 a night on your credit card as a safety deposit - never seen this anywhere else. We asked for a room close to the main area and parking, and were placed in bungalow 16 - a 100 yard walk from the pool and very close to the main area and parking.The room: Very nice - roomy, marble floors, nice furniture and art, decently comfortable beds. All rooms have private balconies or patios (depending on the floor). The only issue was the towels - it seemed that every day we had one less than before, and they did not replace the hand towels at all - just took the dirty ones away... Resort amenities: The only amenities we used were the pool - nice and clean, the gym - it's super hot in there - no A/C it seems, the casino - has an ok selection of machines from 5c to $1 and several tables, and the beach - full of seaweed as it is a nature preserve... Food: Restaurants at the resort are expensive as many reviewers have pointed out, so we had to fend for ourselves. For breakfast and lunch - go to Coco Sweets Bakery - it's at the intersection of the road that leads to the resort and Route 3. Wonderful staff, 70 cents for a cup of excellent coffee, $4 sandwiches, and great pastries. For dinner - if you want real Puerto Rican food and ambiance - go to Liquillo Beach - you can see a long strip of shops along Route 3 a few miles east of the resort - these are all bars/restaurants. They may not look like much, but the food is out of this world and it's cheap. Go to the last one (#60) for the best seafood on the island - try their whole red snapper.Staff: Most of them were very nice and friendly - especially security guards by the bungalo area - their job is so boring, they like to chat with guests - they are a great source of local info. The guest concierge desk staff were also helpful - they have info and directions for most local attractions.Conclusion:A nice hotel if little things don't bother you. We had a good time exploring the surroundings since there's not much to do at the resort itself.

<Content>the good, the bad and the ugly Suggestions:!)Rent a car! It's an American territory - most signs are english or easy spanish, roads nothing different than lots of other places.2)Get used to the idea of bugs - there are even cockroaches-it's the tropics! Bring some Deet -ingredient bug juice if the biting ones particularly like you!3) Appreciate that this is a travel experience, it's not going to be what you have at home - or else, why travel?We are a family of four - with two late-teen daughters. We were celebrating our 20th anniversary and a daughter going off to college. We looked forward to a place away from the Waikiki of San Juan party environment. We found that the resort is lovely - and although far away from most everything - we enjoyed the peaceful, lovely atmosphere. TRANSPORTATION We had rented a car, because 1) in doing the research, including these reviews, the fees for the transportation to and from the resort to the airport were as much - or more than - renting a car for a week!! This was a great decision , EXCEPT that the DAILY FEES for parking were NOT DISCLOSED TO US IN ADVANCE ,by the resort or Travelocity, and this added an unpleasant surprise of an unbudgeted expense for a week! (unless we had used AVIS - they have an office at the resort -and rental charges probably include those fees) 2) Also, the car allowed us to explore on our own; the east end of the island offers quite alot of activities! (the rainforest is great and so close, the luminescent kayak trip is work but SO worth it, and several swimming beaches close by) and we could get our own food - good  cheap restaurants nearby on the hiway or in other towns - instead of paying the exorbitant prices at the resort! And we could go into San Juan when we wanted (*take the toll road - for $1.50 TOLL it saves MANY slow miles of stop light travel)We did eat one dinner at the resort @Asian restaurant $20.00 - 45.00 pp range, very good and 'gourmet -type (small delicious portions)but very $$$$! Also the breakfast buffet there $25.00 pp / $16.00 for continental(=no hot food)ROOMS: The resort was not particularly busy the last 2 weeks of August, but we still were relegated to the units farthest away from everything (bungalow 7) we figured it had to do with booking through a discount broker, although they denied it. The rooms were great; the musty, tropical air is what you find in the caribbean- it's very much expected. AND bugs of all kinds are also tropical, I doubt there were bed bugs(claimed by another reviewer) -because I didn't get bit, but my husband did- and he always gets bit wherever we are) more likely it was no-see-ums that are everywhere in the tropics in the late summer !If you want exterminated and sanitized accomodations - stay in the 30th floor of a high rise american hotel!I did object to the fridge- apparently electronically controlled (ie: they know when you pick something up) filled to the brim with outrageously priced waters  booze ( no room for your stuff) and the candy tray -out on top -with equally exhorbitant prices $5.00 for a .75 cent candy bar.The walk was pleasant when we did walk to the main pool, sometimes hot if it was a muggy day, but sometimes breezy!The golf cart transportation was fairly regular and the staff running the carts were very attentive - or possibly it had more to do with having two cute blonde young ladies with us! The pool was great -almost too warm- and since we live in Calif, we were not looking for A Beach like we have, (again, we read the reviews) we were satisfied with the wonderful snorkle beach they have and the many colorful fish we saw!! All in all we enjoyed our stay and did not want to leave as soon as we had to..The Parker familyCamarillo, CA

<Author>lifeexperiencer
<Content>Awesome/Beautiful Vacation--just a little in the boonies We stayed at the Gran Melia for a week vacation, and we had a wonderful stay. We were a little worried after reading reviews, but we like to keep an open mind and experience it ourselves, and I am so glad we did! Some people must just want to find something wrong with everything or have impossibly high standards. It was a great place!!! The resort is amazing, totally beautiful, with lots of amenities. SERVICE: We did NOT get the royal service, and didn't notice a problem with a regular room. It was perfect for us. All of the staff is soooooo friendly. I will say though that service is NOT always fast. We checked in super late at night, when everyone was sleeping. When we got to our room we had absolutely NO towels, we called, and they said they would be sent right up, yet it took over an hour to get them. That was a bummer because we just wanted to go to sleep. That also happened one other night, but that night took 2+ hours. Just make sure if you need something you call the front desk at least 2-3 hours in advance. That was our only problem. SECURITY: There are security guards everywhere! You have to go through two gates and 13 huge speed bumps to get on premises. Everyone is very friendly and helpful. LINES: We were there when it was really busy, yet the check-in and check-out lines were fine. You can also call the night before you check-out to do the express check out. If you do self-parking, you have to validate your parking every time you leave. It is kind of annoying, but it only takes a minute. It would be nice to have a parking pass instead for however long you are there. ROOMS: The rooms are spacious and comfortable. The beds and pillows are amazingly comfy and lush. Everything you need. VERY nice! POOL: The pool is the most incredible pool I have ever seen, and it is open 24/7. There is something for everyone in the pool area. We were there when the resort was booked solid, yet the pool never seemed overcrowded. Night swims are beautiful with all the lights. BEACH: The beach on the resort grounds is NOT good for swimming. Not a whole lot of sand. No waves at all. BUT we did go snorkeling there, and that was fun. The water is incredibly warm, and you can see some cool tropical fish if you snorkel. Great beach chairs, fun to lay out at night and see stars. RESTAURANTS: We ate at two of the hotels restaurants. We had lunch at the Wet bar near the beach area and pool (it is also a swim up bar). They had great food and reasonable prices. The service is slow though, so make sure you are not in a hurry. We also ate supper at Nami (their Asian/Latin blend restaurant) one night. It is pretty pricey, but great food. They will ask you if you want rice, like it is included in the meal, but it is actually an additional $7. Try the desserts there.... totally amazing. We got our food pretty quickly there. TENNIS: They have 3 tennis courts (but only 2 actually had nets), and they were really nice. They have lights, so you can play anytime of the day or night. They also have awnings on each court for shade from the sun with a bench and cooler of drinking water underneath. PARKING: Parking was $16.05 per day for self-parking. Parking there is crazy... I will say that. One night they had us park under a construction crane. It is always really full at night. Also, make sure your car is locked. We had about $10 stolen one night when we forgot to lock one door. CAR RENTAL: If you want to experience more of PR, I would definitely rent a car. The Gran Melia is definitely in the middle of nowhere. We were so glad we had a car. Eating all meals at the resort could get expensive. We rented a car near the airport, not at the resort. Charlie's Car Rental is great, friendly, and inexpensive. LIZARDS  ANTS: As far as the pestering animal life that I read about in others' reviews, I would say there was no problems. There are some really cool iguanas near the man-made lakes early in the day, but there are definitely not lizards everywhere. You see them sometimes, but they are not bothersome. There were a few really tiny ants in our room, but only in the bathroom, so be careful what you set on the bathroom counters and floors. They don't bite and are probably harmless. OFF-SITE DINING: If you want to save some money or try authentic PR food, here are some great nearby options. There is a great bakery (Sweet Coco Bakery) at the beginning of the entry road. They have amazing donuts and awesome sandwiches, all with great prices. Down the road is a Church's Chicken. They have an amazing dessert for only $2.99. The Vulcan de Chocolate. Down the road the other way is Madre Tierra's. This restaurant has amazing food with great prices and great service. ONLY ANNOYANCES: 1. Any service up to your room (towels, etc) is very slow. 2. I don't know if we were just worried after reading reviews, but we weren't always sure what was off limits to people without Royal Service (like the lounges, internet use, etc). Just make sure to ask right away when you get there. 3. The beach does not have waves at all and is not great for swimming. The water is extremely warm though, and it is fun to snorkel there. 4. The location is kind of a bummer, you are way away from everything. We struggled finding sites and places to see for the first few days. There are no brochures or signs for anything anywhere. I would recommend planning and booking everything (all extra excursions) before leaving on your trip. Vieques Airport has good brochures. You can also pick up tourist info at Madre Tierra's restaurant.One more thing... we got home and checked our credit card. We had an additional charge from the Gran Melia to our credit card. The charge was quadruple what we thought we were going to pay. We knew this must be a HUGE misunderstanding. Turns out Travelocity charged us but didn鈥檛 pay the Resort. The Gran Melia was a little hard to get a hold of, but both companies were very cooperative and kind. It took several weeks to figure everything out. Pretty sure Travelocity was in the wrong, not the Gran Melia. Just make sure to check your credit card when you get back.Overall, this was an amazing place to stay. We would definitely stay there again. It was beautiful, friendly, and had everything we could want and more.EXTRAS: Here are a few sites and attractions to see in PR:1. El Morro in Old San Juan (it closes at 5:00 though--we didn't know that). 2. El Yunque Rainforest. It is free if you bypass the visitor center. Hiking to the very top has the same lookouts as below, but is pretty. 3. La Playa Azul is an amazing beach (right down from Luquillo beach). So sandy and fun waves. Not populated at all. 3. Bio Bay in Vieques. WOW! That was totally amazing and totally worth flying over for. Unbelievable! 4. Flamenco Beach on Culebra. I have never seen such a beautiful beach in my life. Awesome! Must see! Great sand and very blue water. 5. Chartering a small flight verses the ferry. We were hoping to take the ferry to Vieques and Culebra, but lines started at 1 am the night before, and were always full. We chartered flights to both. Definitely more expensive, but less hassle. Plus, if you have reservations on the islands, the ferry is not a guaranteed mode of transportation.I would definitely recommend this trip to anyone! It was great!

Even the car rental desk charges twice what the rest of Puerto Rico does. Gran Melia also makes extra money by letting non guests pay to use the pool, so the place is crawling with kids during the day. We really felt like they went to great lengths to squeeze every last dollar out of us, but made no effort at all to deliver even passable service. We travel a lot and don't mind paying for something nice, but this place charges 5 star prices and gives you half star service. They nearly ruined our honeymoon. Puerto Rico is great, but stay away from Gran Melia!

<Author>Brianh898
<Content>Absolutely Beautiful!! Let me start by saying I'm a 30 year old guy and I'm not one of these people that have never traveled before and then come straight home to write a review about how wonderful there vacation was, because lets face it, first time in the Carribean, how could it be bad? I've been all over the world, and have stayed in many 5 star resorts. The Gran Melia is world class. The staff was amazingly helpful, the restaurants were some of the best I've ever been to in my life ANYWHERE!! The rooms were absolutely perfect. Even the beds were top notch with plush pillow top mattresses, down comforters and large down pillows. If you need to get out and roam, this is not the resort for you, as you are miles away from anything, however there is so much to do right there at the resort I can't imagine why you would need to go anywhere. If you want to rent a car, rent it at the airport, not the resort! They wanted over $300 for 4 days, and we ended up renting at Enterprise for about $125 insurance included ( after driving in Puerto Rico I highly recommend taking there insurance). Taxi fares are not cheap! To get from the resort to the airport was about 30 miles and cost $80 dollars each way, but remember, you're still basically in the United States. Wages are the same, and cost of living is very high here unlike most destinations in the Carribean, so don't expect to come here and rack up on some over priced brand name purses, because everything is priced basically the same as in the states. Through the resort you can contact a guy named Angel for some of the best scuba diving I have ever done in my life. All day tour for about $175 per person, lunch and beer included! Great value, great guy! Oh yeah, Donald Trump is building a couple hundred condos on the same property as the resort (Don't worry, you don't even know the construction is going on, this place encompasses over 2000 acres), and Trump also has two 18 hole golf courses (PGA tour 2008-2011) on the property. As I said I would recommend this resort to anyone wanting to relax, be totally pampered, and enjoy some of the benefits of the good life. By the way, I read somewhere that the place was overcrowded with locals paying only a small daily fee to get in. This is somewhat true, but undestand that these people are paying abut $50 dollars per person for only the use of the swimming pool and a few of the other pleasures of the resort. A family of 4 cost about $200, so your not dealing with a bunch of out of control kids running around with one adult trying to wrangle them, these people are paying very good money for the day use only of these things, and are not a problem at all. Oh yeah, the casino is very nice, and drinks thre are always free (Hold'em tournament every Saturday Night)

<Content>Fabulous Nothing short of perfect. A small piece of paradise. Girls trip, we stayed 5 nights, 6 days. The people were incredibly friendly and always wanting to help. Instead of paying for the tours we rented a car and went on our own. We got around easily and were able to do and see a lot on our own time frame. We spent a day in Old San Juan, saw the Fort Castillo San Cristobal-El Morro, shopping, lunch and dinner and even the Baccardi rum facility. Another day we went to the El Yunque Rainforest and loved having our own car to get around, (hint, wear your bathing suit and a cover-up and walking shoes) after leaving the rainforest we enjoyed the nearby Luquillo beach. There is an Avis car rental on site at the Gran Melia and Gina who works there is wonderful. She used to be a tour guide. One day she sent us on a scenic route to Ponce, south west/central, carribean side of the island. It was beautiful. Saw the eastern exterior, beachs and the interior mountains. We toured a coffee plantation just outside Ponce, (we got the 2 hour tour because they only harvest in October, which is when they offer the 4 hour tour) then we went into the city and toured the Serralles Castle, a beautiful mansion that sits high above the city with an awesome view of the caribbean and city of Ponce. Visited the town square (the trolly's end at 4:00 so we were to late to take a trolly) but after that we went to the boardwalk, five minutes from the city square. We had dinner at El Paladar Bar  Grill right on the boardwalk, very obscure but we had the the freshest, most delicious, seafood meals. We took the interstate back to San Juan and on to the Gran Melia within 2 hours. This day away really made us feel like we had experienced Puerto Rico, because we saw so much outside of the commercial and resort area. One of our favorite memories will be the Coco Sweet Bakery. It sits at the red light entering the road to the Gran Melia. Every morning we had breakfast here. Fresh island coffee was 70 cents, 3 scrabbled eggs with vegtables and fresh baked bread was $3.00. Cuban style, egg, bacon, cheese sandwich was $3.25 (great to go). It opens at 5:30a.m. and closes at 10:00p.m. Donuts were superb. We sun bathed Sunday afternoon, Tuesday after the rainforest, all day Thursday and Friday morning before heading out to the airport. It was truly a great trip and yes I would return and visit the north west side of the island and the caves. I will always stay at a Gran Melia hotel when it is available for future travels. It was a very hospitable and welcoming experience.

I stayed in the Royal Service part of the hotel, so you have a dedicated check-in desk away from the masses, although they don't tell you that (I waited in line for about 15 minutes before I was shuttled over there).My room was spacious, marble-laden, and luxurious. I appreciated the private pool and cabanas that are reserved for the Royal Service clientele. The restaurants were very good, and the sea bass at Nami, for $22, was a relative bargain and outstanding.I had a late flight, and they accommodated me with a 3 p.m. late check out, even though the hotel was completely sold out that day. I'd stay here again in a heartbeat, especially if you can get a deal.

<Content>Don't believe the reviews My wife and I stayed here from 29 Jun - 5 Jul. First of all, as I have learned from many reviews off Trip Advisor, don't believe everything you read. Yes, the room had a bit of a musty smell, but it wasn't due to the lack of cleanliness. A candle fixed that. We even had an extra fridge in our suite so we were able to keep our own supplies readily cold in our room for consumption. Property was awesome. We were in villa 924 with ocean view and yes, it was a bit of a walk to the main resort and pool, but that was how we liked it. We enjoyed our daily walk to and from the pool/resort. The scenery was amazing so we enjoyed taking in all of it during the walk.There was never a time that as we walked to and from our room, a staffer with a golf cart stop to offer a ride. Never ate in any of the restaraunts since we had a rental and wanted to experience Puerto Rican food while in Puerto Rico rather than Japanese or Italian. We ate daily at the pool grill for lunch and it was decently priced. C'mon folks, a $9 Cheeseburger with fries is the norm. If you want a value meal, then stay close to a McDonald's. Same goes for the drinks. I don't know where some of the reviewers normally go, but where I am from and where I have been $5-$10 for a drink is norm. Bartenders took care of us and never skimped on alcohol content. Try to stay during the week if possible. Service is different when the volume increases, but that's to expect anywhere. One thing I was frustrated by was the parking situation on the weekend. There was so many guests and so many people visiting guests, parking was non-existent beginning on Thursday and no one in the hotel seemed to care whether you found a spot or not. We ended parking on the other side of the resort. A small discrepany, but definitely something that needs attention. That Friday we had a problem at the pool grill too. The servers didn't have a grip (nor cared) on who had what tables so several families waited for some time to even get to order a drink. A couple next to us called management and to their credit the grill was swarmed with management and additional staffers within minutes. They personally stopped by our tables, took orders, and comp'd drinks and food for the inconvenience. Every resort working on that scale is likely to have problems. It's how they react and attempt to wrong the rights it is what counts!There it is. Don't let such a great place/deal be overlooked because some people expect way too much even though they got a great deal. We thoroughly enjoyed it and because a few good reviews, we were prepared and it made our vacation so much better.

<Author>SusanfromSoCal
<Content>Exceedingly poor service and mildewed rooms mars otherwise decent enough resort We just got back from a trip around Puerto Rico in which we had the misfortune of staying at La Gran Melia Resort in Rio Grande on two occasions over the course of two weeks. The combination of over-the-top ostentatiousness, exceedingly inefficient service (with the exception of that which is offered to Royalty Service patrons), mildewed rooms (we stayed in 3 of them, all of which had the same problem to differing degrees) and being nickel-and-dimed for everything (including hi-speed internet access - they give you the dial up for free) made for an overall unpleasant stay in what would have otherwise been a decent enough place.Check-in (we arrived at 4:00) took several hours - there were no rooms available with 2 beds and we are a family of 3. At 6:30 we were finally given a room that reeked of mildew. The delay in check-in meant that we were unable to make it out to Fajardo to go to the bioluminescent bay as we had planned. I complained to management the next day an we were upgraded to one of the Royalty Service rooms, which was a significant improvement (in fact, I would never stay there again unless I were to have Royalty Service (which is how *all* of the guests should treated - not just those who fork over the extra $$). The grounds are fairly spread out, which was a huge problem fore me as I have limited mobility due to a disability. We were told that carts circled the property regularly or that all we had to do was call and someone in a cart would come to pick me up whenever we needed transportation. The only carts circling the property regularly were security/landscaping/housekeeping. I called to request a cart on THREE separate occasions and no-one came after more than 20 minutes of waiting!! (The night before we were leaving I even arranged in advance to have a cart pick us up in the morning and it never came!! (In addition to the prior arrangement I made the night before I called in the morning to make sure they would send it to no avail). I should point out, however, this was not the case when we stayed in the Royalty Service quarters, as they have butlers available for transport, etc. at all times. Again, this is the treatment that should be offered to *all* of the patrons, not just those in Royalty Service.The inefficiency with which the place is run is staggering!! In addition to the outrageously long wait for check-in, each time you leave during your stay you have to get your parking ticket validated (for which there was generally a line). On our check-in for the second visit (a week after the first), we requested that express checkout paperwork be sent to our room to avoid the interminable and unavoidable line. The paperwork was never sent.The tendency to nickel-and-dime the patrons for everything from lying on the canopyed beds by the pool to using the high speed internet was rather annoying. Another *huge* problem for me were the polished marble floors all over the place (very slippery when wet (and it rains a lot in Puerto Rico) - I fell on two occasions).I would not stay there again unless I were in Royalty Service (and even then, I'd have to think twice about it).

Monday and Tuesday the pool was very quiet. Our room was nice, always cleaned promptly, very comfy bed, great flat screen tv with all the american channels. We found service very friendly and willing to help. We did not like the beach at the property (full of rocks, like the pictures show) but we took our rental car a few miles down the road to Luquillo Beach which was beautiful, easy to find and almost empty on a Monday. Highly recommend that.Overall, I would recommend this hotel to families much more than singles and also I cannot say enough about having a car to leave the property. There is a lot to see in Puerto Rico. The Gran Melia served as a perfect suitable home base but the beach on property and lack of diverse restaurant options made our rental car worth 10x what we paid for it.

<Author>CTtravelgirl
<Content>The good, the bad and the ugly Just got back from a 5 day stay and in retrospect, I really should've paid better attention to the not-so-hot reviews on Trip Advisor. I booked it because the resort looked beautiful online and I got what I thought was a really good deal. But unfortunately, I can only give the experience a 2 out of 5 rating. The Good: The grounds of the resort are undeniably beautiful. Large, lush and quite romantic...and it's easy to find a quiet little spot as long as you're away from the pool. That's about the extent of the good... The Bad: The food was WAY overpriced for mediocre quality. I'm always prepared to pay a lot for resort food on vacation- but this was ridiculous, especially considering that it wasn't even very good. The pool was loud and crowded. The beach was pretty much non-existent...it's certainly quiet there, but too much sea grass to swim. The rooms were just ok with myriad problems (ants in the room, safe didn't work, clogged tub drain, sink stop broken, etc). The kinds of things a nicer resort would ensure were all in working order BEFORE check in. Also, the golf carts that were supposed to shuttle you around the resort seemed to never be around...we ended up walking everywhere and it takes a good 15 minutes to get from your room to your car. The parking is another nightmare. Hard to find a spot, very tight, overpriced, far away and a pain to have to get your card validated everytime you leave.The Ugly: The service was AWFUL!! The hotel lost our reservation...even after I had confirmed 3 days prior to arrival! After an hour of arguing with the front desk, we finally got a room...but the price was nowhere near the rate/package I had booked online. It was a nightmare...and the front desk reception was the rudest, most difficult staff I've ever had to deal with. Consider yourselves warned...In conclusion, I would not recommend this hotel to anyone. It was ok...but given the rate I ended up paying...I would've been better off at the Ritz, Marriott, Intercontinental...anywhere but here.

<Author>cdd64
<Content>Beautiful Getaway I'm just really shocked of all the bad reviews and pettiness I've read prior to and after our visit to Gran Melia. Granted, there were some issues, but not major enough to complain about. We are people who realize nothing in life is ever perfect. We were not looking for the mistakes or mishaps during our stay as it seemed many who read these reviews and traveled there did. My husband and I travel quite a bit and have stayed in some wonderful places and we consider Gran Melia one of them. The resort is beautiful and very relaxing. We did not have a problem with the food. We ate both at the resort restaurants and outside of the resort. Yes, prices overall at Gran Melia were quite expensive, but I agree with the other reviewer that it's due to the importing of items. You have to pay for convenience. The staff was very helpful and friendly. Particularly Miguel from the concierge desk. He was very consistent in making sure our visit was comfortable. I do recommend that you rent a car because it's a great convenience to be able to explore towns and local restaurants outside of the resort. Miguel had recommended Pasion Por El Fogon in Fajardo (www.pasionporelfogon.net). It was excellent! In fact, we ate there 2 nights in a row. He also recommended Richies's in Rio Grande. Can't see how the one reviewer talked badly about it because it has a great view, menu and Ritchie was nothing but friendly and accommodating. Gina from the Avis desk was also a wonderful person and very helpful. My husband had mentioned it was my birthday and we were going to drive into Old San Juan for dinner. We talked about finding some good paella and she recommended Rosa de Triana, a place that she frequented often in Old San Juan. It's a great casual local restaurant which also has a Flamingo show. When we arrived, Gina was there dining and had arranged for the Flamingo dancers to sing happy birthday to me. Very special and sweet of her to do that for me. Gina was right, the paella was excellent. As far as the pool being too cold. Well, I don't know about you, but while I'm sun bathing in the hot tropical sun, I want a cool refreshing pool to step into, not a warm pool. The activity and towel center staff were also very accommodating. As far as the distance of the rooms and everything else in the resort鈥?we didn't mind the walking. There were carts to use but we found the walking a plus after having such wonderful and filling meals. Good advice as far as signing up as a Sol Melia member (which is free). It's gets you a 2 for 1 breakfast, as well as a discount off your restaurant tab. The drive into and out of the resort didn't bother us. Yes, there is construction near the resort itself, but that didn't take away from the beauty. We didn't use the Royal Service package and felt we really didn't need to. Our room had a partial ocean view and sat behind the Royal Service Pool, which was just fine. Very spacious and clean room. We never encountered any bugs, bites or attitudes and had a very pleasant stay. So, rest assure that you will enjoy yourself at this resort, unless, of course, you are one of those people who look for problems.

<Author>ced2108
<Content>Amazing in every way! I can not believe what some people will complain about!  This place was amazing! I booked my destination wedding there without ever visiting and I was extremely nervous about it once I read the reviews! I had 20 guests in 10 rooms and not one of them had a complaint! They kept telling me how friendly everyone was (grounds crew, service staff...every one) and I agree! The food at the pool bar as good and reasonably priced for a resort...obviously people think they are going to Mexico where everything will be dirt cheap but this is America people and the prices are comparable..except remember it is an island so things have to be imported so they are more expensive. Stick to what is native, RUM, FISH, Plantains...etc and you will be ok.Yes, there were a few minor things that happened, such as my brothers room kept blowing a fuse with the AC but it was quickly fixed. You can't expect perfection but you can hope that any issue is resolved quickly and efficiently, and it was. As for people complaining about musty odors or a lack of shopping should go to the mall for vacation. It is an island, surrounded by water and guess what?...things get humid and damp. Try to remember you're on vacation and have to be a little less stressed and go with the flow. Rent a car and explore the island if you don't want to stay at the resort the whole time...it's not like they advertise being in the shopping district..stay in San Juan if that is what you are looking for...or go 7 minutes down the road and the is an entire outlet center!A few notes on other things: BEACH: natural wild life preserve, excellent for shelling and we did some fun snorkeling too. We found starfish, a living Conch, and sea urchnants. Don't plan on riding the waves...because there are none....if you have water shoes bring them, but enjoy the beach none the less! FOOD: we ate in all 3 restaurants and l liked them all. The Habachi was very fun and delicious, Italian, very good and The dinner buffet (Cafe Solie)- ok for adults but excellent for kids. We had two 10 year olds, a 6 year old and a 4 year old and they all ate well that night! For breakfast I skipped the buffet and just grabbed something from the Cart (Kisok)...it was a small wagon with juices, muffins, breads and eggs and coffee. All we needed.Pool BAR/GRILL - any one who complains about this has issues. There are lots of people and they serve you as quickly as they possibly can. You can see the guy cooking behind the bar so it's not like they are being lazy...just busy. And the drinks are about $10 but any one who has been to a resort knows this is the going rate! And they were strong and good. I recommend sticking with the Mojitos!!!!!!!!!! (rum, fresh mint, club soda and sugar)If you can, go with the Royal Service (but if you have kids you will probably stick to the main pool and thus not enjoy all of the benefits) but the special lounge, pool and little extras were really nice. My guests didn't have the Royal Service and they all still LOVED the place and all said they would return.Over all this place was beautiful, the staff extremely friendly, Very helpful (if treated respectfully!) and we had a great time.

<Author>LovetoVacationAlways
<Content>Nice Enough but there were issues... My husband and I just returned from Puerto Rico last week (2/23-2/27) and we were quite concerned with the Gran Melia after booking with CheapCarribean.com with some of the postings on this site. We were expecting the worse, but we had a great time nonetheless! Here are some of our experiences: The Good: - Beautiful property and friendly staff. Although, it was peak season in PR, the property was pretty empty so we enjoyed the resort immensely. - The Room: Although, they couldn't give us an upgrade since the resort was at capacity - the front desk agent was nice enough to put us in a room with a living room and kitchen! It was one of the nicer rooms we had stayed in for a while. We really enjoyed having the extra space and fridge to stock our snacks and refreshments.- The pool: Really nice and clean! Unlike other resorts we've been to, we didn't have to get to the pool extra early to fight for a chair. There were plenty of lounge chairs around the pool. The not so good: - The Food: We only had dinner one night at the Asian restaurant (we had Hibatchi) and were utterly disappointed. We had reservations at 8:00pm and didn't get seated until 9:15pm. We understand that the prices were going to be expensive considering we're at somewhat at a luxury resort, but the quality fo the food was just plain bad. Our hibachi chef smothered everything (we had steak and seafood hibachi) with butter and terayaki sauce. Our dinner for 2 people came out to around $110 including tip (not bad IF the food was decent). Word of advice - don't EAT in the resort. The other nights we ate in Old San Juan and Fajardo and had much better luck! - The Beach: All the complaints about the beach are TOTALLY warranted. There is NO BEACH. The sand is rocky and you can't really swim in the water since it's so shallow. My husband and took several day trips out to Luquillo Beach and Culebra - totally worth it. - The drive into the Resort: Waaaay too long. It will literally take you a full 15 minutes to drive from the entrance of the resort to the highway. Plus the ticket validation process is really annoying.All in All we had a great time! The resort served it's purpose as a place to sleep and chill out, since we were not at the resort most of the time. Renting a CAR is a MUST in PR (however DO NOT rent from THRIFT - we had a miserable experience with them when we left PR and they charged me 2x on my credit card).

<Author>mi48301
<Content>Nice Get Away I would say that just about every reviewer has this right. It all depends on why you are going here. You would probably hate this place if you are looking for night life and high energy. You would think it was pretty bad if you just wanted a beach to swim in. But if you are looking for a beautiful or romantic place to relax, you may have found a gem. I took my fiance for a long weekend, and it was a lovely experience.THE GOOD: We had an ocean front suite with the jacuzzi tub. The main area of the hotel is very beautiful, lots of marble, candles lit every night, open air, fountains everywhere. The royal service pool was perfectly quiet, we had an amazing bed looking out at the pool and the ocean just beyond. We enjoyed the fact that the pool workers weren't coming over every 15 minutes asking for another drink order. When we wanted something it was a short walk or an armwave. We ate at the Asian restaurant and watched the cook on the grille in front of us. Fun to watch, fun to meet people, and the food was just fine. Cafe Soliel had a great breakfast buffet that would tide you over until dinner if you ate around 11:00. The grounds are nice, above average but not like a Ritz or Four Seasons.The service was acceptable, nothing special but certainly not to the point of complaining. When we wanted to go off site for a local dinner, our butler, Marcos, recommended TACO RICO, which is just east of the resort road on 3, past the shell station about 2 blocks. You will probably pass it the first time, but it is worth the trip! We were the only non-locals and the owner is the only one who speaks english. They do not serve alcohol, but if you want a beer or wine, the owner will go to the bar down the street and get it for you. The food is awesome...let the owner set you up with appetizers and your meal! You won't regret it! The BAD and UGLY: While the beach is very picturesque, everything you have read on previous posts is true. It looks great! But what is pictured is like a hard clay with lots of rocks and coral that they groom in the morning so it looks a little like sand. Gorgeously landscaped, with chairs and hammocks but not very friendly to bare feet. There is a line of rocks that separates this clay beach from the sand beach. The sand is very coarse and is more like broken shells than sand. If you have water shoes or plastic flip flops, this is a nice beach to walk, and you can go pretty far. We were with people who saw an octopus, an eel, and a manta ray in the water from walking on the beach. I think you could have some fun and see some fish snorkelling here as long as you don't need the water to be really deep and sandy, but unfortunately the one day we tried, the water was too cloudy.The only other complaint is that the road into the resort is long and with a lot of construction. It detracts from the beauty of the resort to see all the dirt and mud and the lack of landscaping. Overall we had a super relaxing experience. Went to the rain forest and walked to see mina falls and tall tree trail. Saw Luquillo beach where people were surfing on giagantic waves, and spend a lot of time reading books and enjoying the sounds of the surf at the resort. And enjoyed some sunsets over the tree line to the west. Finding the information about the $250.00 food credit on the puerto rico forum pages made the food taste even better, since most of it was free! :)  
<Date>Jan 29, 2008

<Author>pforgebobby
<Content>Not Worth The Price My wife and I stayed for five days in November, 2007. We were part of a conference booking, so that may have made our experience above that of the non-conference guest.The room was well below standards for the price. It was clean. The rooms are in separate buildings and are pretty far removed from the front desk. They have golf cart type vehicles that circle the sidewalks. They run on an irregular basis. We rode one to the room and walked the rest of the time.The hotel was probably less than 50% occupancy while we were there. The pool always had sufficient chairs/towels. The beach is very small. The part of it adjoining the pool is not wider than ten feet and has rough shells/rocks. The part of the beach down toward the more expensive rooms is wider and more sandy. There was plenty of room there in November. We had the beach to ourselves (the whole area) for most of one afternoon.BUGS! Thankfully none in the room. But the conference had a cocktail party on the grassy area between the beach and pool one evening and no-see-ums ate exposed skin. Take insect repellant with you! The store on property ran out and it was only available at the front desk at $10 a can. Don't expose too much skin -- that will help, too. The bugs were there during the day but not nearly as bad.The food IS expensive. We rate it 6 out of 10 overall.There was major golf course construction going on during our stay and the earth moving equipment ran all day long in sight of our room. They were trying to get ready for a major golf event. The pool gets an 8 out of 10. It was dirty near the swim-up bar -- an area that seems to attract debri.We would never stay there again. The bug bites were the biggest reason. My wife was sick for a week after our return.

<Author>Traveller99_8
<Content>A cruel $7000.00 joke! I brought my 21 year old daughter for a week of relaxing, good food and sun, so she could recharge her batteries before returning to her final semester in college. The Royal Service plan is a joke. One morning, I came in to the Royal Service lounge to find a young family grazing over the buffet of breakfast foods, eating while food dropped from the dad's mouth into the tray of food which was to be consumed by other guests. The cheeses were slimey and much of the cold food suffered time and temperature abuses galore! We were afraid to eat some of this. Without giving the details of each day, I will say this: Never go to this resort. You will be extremely disappointed with the service, food, and inconsistencies! The final slap in the face was the bill. Our week was consumed with stressing over what we would be able to eat. OH! And don't ask for the wine list. The staff provided basic treatments, which were represented as much more than they really were. The skincare products were absolute crap. The special anti aging facial was $190.00 and was the most uncomfortable 80 minutes of my life, with a nervous gentleman administering the treatment, after not washing his very cold hands. Also, the spa hours are from 10 to 8, but try to book a treatment during the early morning or late afternoon and forget it. All the appointment times seemed to be between 11 and 3, which is prime pool time!We knew there would be no beach. The Royal Service Pool was nice. The only beer we had that was served COLD, was here. Leslie was the best pool guy in the bunch. Our butler, Manuel, was awesome too. But you just knew he couldn't right all of the wrongs at that place. So why complain to him?The Royal Service people (Veronica and Tamary) were helpful in negotiating our complaints with management. From the conversations we overheard at the pool and in the restaurants, many guests were flatly disgusted with what they had paid and the quality of what they received, if they received it at all! It was to the point where, each morning, we would say EXPECT NOTHING. Then, when something good happens, we will be happy!  We took a taxi to a seafood restaurant on the last night just to have edible food. The taxi was $120.00 and the meal as much. If you are a vegetarian, you will be miserable here. We do eat fish, but that is it as far as animal products. Ask for veggies and rice, and be prepared to take a potent diuretic the next day, as the use of salt was extreme.Most of the staff was friendly, but they seriously lacked communication, just forgot things, and were generally inconsistent with respect to the rules. The Royal Service Pool was to be restricted to children, no matter what. Yet, every day, someone would have a child under 16 there. This is an example of what I mean by inconsistent. I could go on and on about this.Basically, if you don't have enough frustration and stress in your life, come to Gran Melia Puerto Rico. By the end of your stay, your life will be completely full of it.The resort itself was beautiful. I will give credit where it is due. Our room had a funky yeasty, moldy scent, too. If I were given a free week here, I would return. That is the only way I would ever come back.

<Author>Nana_KB
<Content>A fabulous place We just returned from Puerto Rico and had a great stay at the Gran Melia. The lobby area is beautiful, in the evening they light hundreds of candles making it an enchanted place. Our suite was wonderful, the bed was very comfortable our only complaint was that our tub would not close, so only showers for us. The beach may not be what people expect, but the breakfront is a long way from the shore, so you can easily swim and enjoy the water without fighting the surf. There are areas of seaweed close to the shore, just swim out a ways to get passed it. The pool is great and goes on forever, we rented a cabana for $35 for the entire day, this was a great shady place to relax and watch all the activity. The pool attendant was very nice and attentive. The service in the pool bar was pretty poor, they don't seem to be able to handle a crowd, but I think the worst part was that they don't seem to enjoy what they are doing and were not at all friendly. This same attitude extended to the bar in the lobby, the bartenders can make or break someone's attitude about a place, so this is where they really need to improve. The breakfast buffet was pretty extensive, but the food was somewhat mediocre. The only bright spot was the omelet and waffle stations where you could get freshly made items. But there are lots of choices, so there should be something for everyone. It is a little pricey at $20 per person. The only choice we ever had for lunch was at the pool bar, good burger, but otherwise not great and again pretty overpriced. $13 for shrimp cocktail which only had 5 small shrimp on a bed of lettuce with fried plantains. This is a resort, so you should expect resort prices, go with the expectation that you are going to be paying for the atmosphere and enjoy it. My recommendation is that you rent a car and get off the property to enjoy all the attractions in the area. El Yunque is just minutes away, there is a beautiful beach at Luquillo ( there is a $3 entry fee). Go to the biobay in Fajardo, this shouldn't be missed. There are lots of alternative places to eat away from the resort, so get out and get the flavor of Puerto Rico. The parking is $15 daily for self park, but you will save that in just a few meals. Inspite of the few complaints we had, we had a wonderful time at the Gran Melia, it is a beautiful place to stay.

<Author>zcooltraveller
<Content>Beautiful grounds, but still adjusting My wife and I are seasoned travelers to the Caribbean. Many visitors to the Grand Melia don鈥檛 understand the economy of tourism, especially in poorer areas and have set too high expectations. In short, if you have a Wal-Mart budget 鈥?stay home. Several reviewers were accurate with their assessments and I will echo their advice.The Melia just took over from the Paradisus this year, which was an all-inclusive family style resort. My impression was the employees are still adjusting to different hotel policy. Loungers and towels still had the old name on them. We had a great time because we did our homework, and you will too. Below is my advice for this resort.1. Transport: Rent a car. For the whole trip. From the airport. We got 5 days with full insurance and prepaid gas for $235. Not hostage to shuttles, or schedules (blah), or the onsite Avi$$. Yes parking fees are charged, but so does every other hotel in PR. There are two lots inside the gate, right is closer, left is the remote lot. Nearby is El Yunque, Luquillo beach, Fajardo.2. Royal Service: premium 鈥渃lub style鈥?service. Basically an upgrade in room, attention and treatment, running from $75 鈥?00 more per night. You have your own lounge with complimentary hors鈥?douerves all day, free Internet and a comp bar from 7-9 PM every night. Plus any room or activity issues you go through them, and not other departments. Use of the Royal service pool. It鈥檚 a better class of service. Highly suggest.3. Meal Plans: The Melia needs to rethink their AP and MAP plans, way overpriced. We prepaid our breakfasts (at $20 pp over 4 days). The buffet style breakfasts were plentiful, with omelet鈥檚, waffles made to order. For dinner, slow service meant long waits at TEMPO. Decent food, I give it 3 stars out of 5. At the Palm, Puerto Rican Paella was excellent. Reservations are not taken, its FCFS. Kids will be everywhere. Not too many fine dining options near the hotel, we ate out one evening at the Rio Mar, about 5 mi down Route 3.4. Food and Beverage: Pricey. Prices are as other reviewers stated. On Route 3 make a left out of the access road 录 mile on left is a strip mall with a BK, a KFC, a Subway and AMIGO 鈥?their version of a Shop Rite.. Soda  beer at supermarket prices. A good way to keep the lunch and beverage costs down.5. Rooms and grounds. Beautiful. Rooms look freshly painted. Gardens are full, lots of color. Main pool is enormous, with plenty of lounge chairs (could use more umbrellas). Beach: a disappointment. Rocky, red sand. Sea grass. Good for sailing, not for snorkeling. Calm. If you want surf 鈥?go to Luquillo, about 10 miles away. There is a kids club, and there are games, bikes for the young ones.6. Main building. Open air. Lots of chaise lounges  sofas. Gardens  fountains everywhere. Clean. Live music at the bar every night. Small casino, but some slots are broken, they don鈥檛 take bills, or bar code vouchers.7. Tipping. I am amazed at how cheap people get on vacation. A little goes a long way. We tipped, and got great attention. Yes the service is slower, but it鈥檚 the Caribbean. Overall: a good hotel, that can be superb if they make some adjustments. Be patient, ask lots of questions, and tip a few bucks if someone goes out of their way for you. You鈥檒l be amazed at how far a smile, and a 鈥淏uenos dias鈥?will get you.

<Author>0RyGuy0
<Content>Great place, not price My wife and I went to the Gran Melia for our honeymoon. We had read the reviews on Trip advisor so we were a bit wary but had a nice time overall. So, here are the categories I'll use: be aware of, the good, and the bad.First of all, be aware that...- When you fly in to San Juan, you'll need to arrange your own transportation from the airport to the hotel. I tried to book a separate travel company but to no avail but it actually worked out OK because we were able to take a taxi to the resort for about $75 for both of us and our luggage plus tip. Our taxi driver was very nice and gave us an orange and a travel guide for Puerto Rico. You may want to call the concierge desk at Gran Melia because I think they can arrange transportation for you at around $60 for two people. We took a Gran Melia shuttle to the airport when we left the resort.- If you choose to rent your own car, parking at the resort will be $10 a day so add that to your cost of renting a car for a week.- There is an Avis rental booth at the resort, if you don't want a car for the whole week but may want to take a day trip.- The resort has several options for day trips so don't plan with any outside source (e.g., through Orbitz like we did) because they might not pick you up at your resort (we learned this only after purchasing the non-refundable day-trip vouchers).- There are not surfable waves, if you know what I mean. It is a beautiful natural beach and the waves break on a reef about 200m off of the shore. - The resort is secluded: you drive past a golf course and through a gated entrance so you can't just walk off of the resort unless you want to walk about a mile or so.- Because the resort is somewhat secluded (which we enjoyed), food at the resort is expensive ($80 for fillet mignon and strip steak with 2 sides, $50-$60 for 2 buffet-style meals).- An Ocean View room means that you will be facing the ocean but may not be able to see it. We could see the ocean from our room but others may not have been able to.The Good:- The rooms were beautiful, air condition worked great, room service did a good job.- The location of the rooms were nice as well, a short walk away so they were away from any noise coming from the pool or resort.- The beach was relatively unused. We had a great time taking walks along the natural beach.- Although a bit pricey, the food was relatively good.- Mostly couples and families so it was a good atmosphere.- Beautiful pool, even when during popular swim time, it was easy to find a place in the pool where you didn't feel surrounded and crowded (also nice at night).- Employees were friendly if you are friendly to them. It's good to tip but not in a manipulative way. Basically, if you treat people decently, you will be treated decently.- Live entertainment at night.- Close to El Yunque Rainforest.The Bad- A bit pricey for what you get.- Hard to get off of the resort without shelling out some cash. Either you need to rent a car for the whole week and pay $10 extra (probably the best option if you're feeling adventurous), rent a car for a day (about $70), or get a taxi or shuttle somewhere (price varies depending on distance).- Some restaurants are closed depending on the night.Advice:- Eat lunches at the pool-side bar, it's pretty reasonable there.- For breakfast, borrow bread from the night before, if you want to save some dough (pun intended). - Use lots of sunscreen, you will still tan quite well with SPF 50.- Stay hydrated: lots of water.- Eat your fill at the buffet meals to get your money's worth.- There was an all-inclusive plan available but I didn't check it out so it may be cheaper that way.- If you're not intimidated by driving in PR, rent a car for a week. It would make it easier to see many of the sites around PR and much less expensive in the long-run.Synopsis: all-in-all, a good place. Our only concerns were the price and the difficulty of leaving the hotel and not paying a lot extra for it. But, seeing as we were on our honeymoon, we didn't worry too much about leaving the resort.This kind of place is good for a relaxing, quieter getaway with a few friends, spouse, or family. If you're looking for a great place to get drunk cheaply and not remember your vacation, this is not the place. If you're looking for a party-atmosphere or night-life, this is also not the place.Basically, we were happy with our trip but could have just as well gone somewhere else and been happy there too.

<Author>Jazcutey
<Content>They didn't advertise the possible bed bugs! Well, from the website I was expecting to have a nice relaxing girls weekend with a friend of mine, however, this hotel did not live up to our expectations. From the time when we first arrived and until we left there were little experiences that added up to up to us both making the determination we would not come back, nor recommend this place to friends. Arriving from the airport the cab dropped us off at the wrong hotel, we were left at the golf resort, which is on the same grounds, but about a mile away from the Gran Melia. My friend and I knew our adventure had begun! Arriving at the Gran Melia the welcome was nice and the the hotel looked very inviting. Check in was good and our bags were brought to our rooms. We had a handicap accessible room, although neither of us is handicapped. We just assumed this was the only room they had with two double beds. The room was nice, however it was missing little things you would expect out of a four star hotel, a mini-bar, note pads and pens, a do not disturb sign, a guide book that discusses the hotel, the amenities, local attractions, etc. Not having these things did not dampen our experience, but I would expect a four star hotel to have these things at a minimum. The beach - well I always heard about the beautiful beaches of Puerto Rico, but the Gran Melia is not on one of those beaches. The path to the beach was filled with rocks, which in bare feet is somewhat of a challenge to walk and water and beach itself were also filled with rocks. You could not lay out on the beach with a beach chair because there was not enough space, not b/c there were tons of people, but because the beach was more like a small patch of grassy area. The water was beautiful once you got past the rocks and the non-beach area, but the Melia cannot take credit for that. Beach experience - Grade CBefore laying on upper level of the beach (grassy area near pool) we asked the pool bar/restaurant for food and drinks. The wait staff did not seem eager to assist us. Several staff just stood around talking while we were standing at the bar and the waitress who finally assisted us seemed like she would have preferred to do something else with our time. We eventually got our food and drinks, which were okay, however, that was the only contact we had with the beach staff. One would expect (or at least we did!) that someone would come up and take out plates and cups, no one did, one would also expect that they would ask if we wanted anything else, no one did. We were on our own! If I am staying at a four star beach resort I would like someone to come and see about me, but we came to the conclusion that attention to customers was not their strong point. Another slightly annoying fact is that we couldn't pay for anything in cash, we had to charge eveyrthing to the room. Beach and Beach Service - Grade CRestaurants - well there really weren't any choices b/c only one restaurant was open! The restaurant was fine dining and the food was okay, but again for a four star place, why only one eating option??!! I would suspect that on a beach vacation most people would want to grab a burger or something non-fine dining, however, there was no type place to go to. Now we were told that there was room service, which there was, but since we did not have a book in our room with a menu we called to the front desk. What was give to us was a paper print out of the menu, again, not very four star like! The food took 45 - 60 minutes to arrive and when it arrived it was a bit cold, and the order was wrong! I definitely think there were some language barriers to ordering. Breakfast was okay at the buffet. Food and Restaurants - Grade CTransportation - now I mentioned above the cab from the airport dropped us off at the wrong location, which wasn't a huge problem b/c the shuttle from the Gran Melia came and picked us up. However, my friend and I wanted to leave the resort and go into town (15 minutes away from the hotel) and the cab ride cost us an arm and a leg! Considering it takes about 5 - 8 minutes to get off of the resort grounds, $30 for a 10 minute ride seems excessive! However, the ride into town was worth the meal we received at a restaurant called Sandy's. Great food and a great waitress! That meal was the best meal of the whole trip but the only meal eaten outside of the hotel. We had to hire the same cab to take us back that brought us to town, for some reason only certain cabs are allowed on the property - a round trip fare for a twenty minute ride $60. I think that is waaaaaay too much! Transportation - Grade CGuest Services - well, the people who drive around in the golf carts were attentive in asking me if I needed a ride anywhere, but short of that there was little to no customer attention. All of the staff had the same don't bother me attitude. When you asked for something they got it (or tried to) but other than that they seemd like they didn't care about your stay. Guest Services Grade - DI could go on and on about the averageness of this place or the lack of things a standard four star hotel should have but I will leave you with this. My first night in the hotel room I kept waking up thinking there was a mosquito in the room. I checked the bed, pulled the sheets off, looked at the mattress, but didn't find anything. But each night I felt the same way, but could never find anything. But each morning I woke up with more and more red marks on my arms and legs. These marks are not mosquito bites, and after some investigation they may be bed bugs. Psychologically I don't feel ilke leaving my house for people staring at the marks on my arms and legs! I should not be stressed out after vacation about whether I am bringing bed bugs into my house!!!! Thankfully my roommate didn't get any bite marks, but I did see a few other people at the hotel with the same bites on their arms and legs. Bed Bugs - Grade F After all I mention above this is not a place I would go back to or recommend to my friends. Overall Stay - D
