<Author>montymon113
<Content>Look Before You Book The Gran Melia Puerto RicoResort  VillasPicture yourself surrounded by beautiful palm trees and clean, comfortable rooms. A large pool with built in lounge chairs and tables to place the tropical drink you just got from the swim up bar.Shuttle cars leave regularly from the open-air lobby to transport youto and from your room. Four elegant, high-priced restaurants cater toyour dining needs and a buffet breakfast stocks more food than you could possibly sample.Now imagine you want to leave the resort and experience the culture of Puerto Rico. You want to hike the waterfalls of El Yunque, the only rain forest within the U.S. National Forest system. You want to swim at Luquillo beach. Then you discover the customer鈥檚 dilemma: theresort is so far off the beaten path and the prices to leave it so high that you can鈥檛 afford to leave. However, with the prices incurred on the resort, you can鈥檛 afford to stay either.You soon learn that everywhere you turn another guest has a horror story to share. They are commiserating in paradise, over delicious strawberry daiquiris, about slow customer service, long check in lines, false promises, and exorbitant costs. Since the Gran Melia used to be the Paradisus, an all-inclusive resort, the clientele was mixed when we were there. Adding to the tropical flair are the bali-beds, draped in canopies with soft cushions. A romantic dream that can be rented for $30.00 per day. You can frolic in the pool or on the beach on a $15.00 per day raft. Towels are free in exchange for your room number, but don鈥檛 loose them or you will be charged, from what we heard the priceper towel ranges from $75.00-$100.00.We chose to have breakfast included in our vacation package. A smart move considering it was the only meal of the day that was guaranteed us. The first three days they gave us a check and we had to take the time to explain we had the breakfast package. We ate a few dinners at the resort restaurants. Here are a few examples of the food options taken right from the menu:Romantico (a fine dining experience in elegant surroundings with excellent service) Salmon Alumando appetizer $13.00Cordero a la Narranja $37.00Nami (Hibachi-style dining with a Japanese flare) Teppanyaki Dinner Table $39.00Caf茅 Soleil (considered a steak house)Seabass fillet $27.008 oz Rib eye $30.00Side dish (e.g. baked potato) $7.00Dessert $7.00 ($8.00 for the Key Lime pie)The other restaurant, an Italian option, wasn鈥檛 open while we were there.Lunch at the pool-side bar will set you back $12.00 for a hamburger. Now imagine yourself there with children. Many people I spoke to with families rented a $65.00 mid-sized car from the on-site Avis dealer for $117 per day (that鈥檚 including tax, insurance, and other hidden fees) and headed to the grocery store down the street. We soonrented a car ourselves; a compact car for two days got us off the resort for $138.00. It鈥檚 a good thing my friend was comfortable with city driving, because a cab to San Juan was $80.00 each way, per person. We took the car to El Yunque and after paying $3.00 at the visitor鈥檚 center we saw the beauty and spendor of the rain forest, a short, 10-15 minute drive from the resort. The same excursion from the Gran Melia, advertised as a Rainforest Hike to Waterfall Swim (3.5 hours) will run you $97.00 per person.Since getting around was a key frustration for us, I do have to mention that I asked about Sunday services. I noticed a Catholic church on Coco Beach Road, the road the resort is on. I inquired about Mass times and how to get there. Once I found out it was $20.00 each way, per person, I decided that God would understand if I missed mass this week.A side note about renting a car: There is also a $15.00 per day parking fee that you are not informed of. We learned, however, from one of the other hotel guests that the parking ticket can be validated in the Casino with minimal gambling.Short of the canned hotel information, I felt uninformed about how to enjoy my vacation. I felt as if the staff at the Gran Melia did not want me to leave the resort except by the means they provided. By the time I figured out how to have the vacation I wanted, my time was up. I wish the staff was forthcoming and told me to go enjoy a dinner in Old San Juan or to take the car to Fajardo for the experience of a life time. There was very little in the way of entertainment and thus, the nights were boring and rainy day proved long and uneventful. I may have been looking for the experience I had at the Divi in Aruba last year where dancing and shows were provided every night. Music in the lobby and one show with dancers (that we found by chance) did not do it for me.I can overlook the mistakes that happened to us: 鈥he hotel transfer was not communicated properly. Once we found where to go our luggage took one bus and we took another. We were even asked to get off of the first bus because it was a private group.鈥ur room not being ready (even though we made the reservations well in advance and specifically requested two double beds). A hospitalityroom was offered to us where we changed and stayed by the pool. My friend asked for a complimentary drink at the lobby bar for our troubles, which was granted by the front desk, but not the bar tender. A manager was summoned. After a few hours we were placed in a room that was first offered us (unacceptable due to the travel party). We did not get in our proper room until 10:00 that night (check-in was at 3:00, our first room was promised to us by 5:00).鈥ur luggage was sent from the hospitality room to the first incorrect room (the one that was describe during check in that we specified would not work for our party). Some clothes were lost in transit, but then later found and returned. My friend requested a complimentary dinner for our troubles which was granted by the front desk. No one in the restaurants had known about it. We did finally get it.鈥 party at the resort (not for hotel guests, but sponsored by Budweiser) was not well thought out. We took our rental car into Old San Juan returning about 10:00 p.m. It took us 32 minutes from Old San Juan and 40 minutes waiting in a line of traffic to get into the Gran Melia. No accommodations were made for hotel guests. To add insult to injury when we got to the front of the line the 鈥渓ot closed鈥?sign went up. We explained that we are hotel guests and were redirected to the Avis lot that was already filled with cars from the Budweiser party. We did not have the option of attending the Budweiser party.鈥hey tried to charge us for our breakfast included in the vacation package for the first few days.The Gran Melia traps you in an overpriced paradise on the wrong side of the island (if you are there to experience beautiful beaches. We did not see anyone swimming, nor did the beach water look inviting to us.) The staff will try to make you feel as if you are the most important entity to them, while they never follow through with promises. The right hand doesn鈥檛 know what the left hand is doing is an extreme understatement. As far as I can see there are two choices at the Gran Melia; stay on the resort and pay for overpriced meals and excursions (but then you miss the real local flavor of Puerto Rico), or rent an overpriced car and get out and live the culture with the locals. <Author>Pedro727
<Content>Some changes would make it great... My parents, who live in Puerto Rico, enjoy spending one weekend during the summer at one of the resorts throughout the island every year (and they like to treat their kids and their spouses). After 2 years staying at the El Conquistador, we decided to give the Gran Melia Puerto Rico a chance. My parents had stayed here before (when it was the All Inclusive Paradisus). However, my wife and I had not. Structurally, from the outside, the hotel doesn't look like much. However, once you enter the lobby area, it's a beautiful resort and nicely decorated. The pool area is the main focal point and it's also very nice. The rooms are some of the largest and nicest I've come across (with large bathrooms, large balconies, and marble throughout). Instead of one large high rise building, the hotel is spread out with one main building housing the lobby, casino, shops and restaurants, and several bungalows where all the rooms are located. These are spread out throughout the property. We were in bungalow 10, and even though it wasn't the farthest one from the main building, it was still a 1/4 mile walk.(distances are marked along the paths). Golf carts are constantly going by taking guests from building to building, but don't hold your breath for one. During the 3 days and 2 nights we were there, I was only able to ride them once. This hotel became a Melia resort a few months ago, and unfortunately, the transition seems to be hurting them some. I hope that they can iron the problems because it's the only way that it can truly be a 5 star resort. We encountered some problems, which could've ruined our vacation, however, we tried to make the most of it:- CHECK IN: Veeeery slow. We arrived at 6:00pm. Our reservation was nowhere to be found and they tried to convince us that we had only reserved one room and the hotel was full to capacity (I was not planning on spending my vacation sharing a room with my wife along with my parents!). I asked the lady to allow me to look up my email account where I had saved my confirmation which obviously stated two rooms. Magically, the second room appeared. FINALLY, one hour and 10 minutes after arriving at the hotel, we were on our way to our rooms. The golf carts were nowhere to be found, and after waiting some more, we decided to walk the 1/4 mile to our bungalow. Unfortunately the luggage didn't arrive until 9:00pm (3 hours after we first arrived)! We kept calling, and calling and they kept saying that they were very busy (and apparently the front desk team was also understaffed).- THE ROOM: As mentioned before, it was one of the nicest rooms I've ever had at any resort. The only negative was that there were three phones, but the only one that worked was the one in the bathroom by the toilet! - HOUSEKEEPING: We left our room at 7:00am and returned at 4:00pm only to find out that the room had not been cleaned. We called for clean towels which were delivered promptly. The maid knocked on our door around 5:00pm, but by then, we didn't care about having our bed made so we thanked her but told her not to worry. Once again, I believe their housekeeping team was also understaffed.- FOOD: The only place to eat something without getting raped with the prices is the grill by the pool. Even though $13.50 for a burger is insulting, we expected these prices since this was a resort. The breakfast buffet was $23 per person. Dinner at the Tepanyaki restaurant was $39 per person. Even though the food is obviously overpriced, it was very good. We did feel sorry about our waiter at the restaurant for dinner. Usually, at resorts, and in order to maintain the service that is expected, you would expect several people serving you at once. Our poor waiter was doing an excellent job, but he was all by himself, running like crazy between 2 tepanyaki tables with 10 people at each one, cleaning, bussing, taking orders, serving drinks, cleaning again, serving desserts, and still managed to keep a smile. Dinner was a 2 hour affair, mostly waiting and watching our waiter run from one table to another, but the food was very good. Once again, the problem here seemed to be with staffing.-ENTERTAINMENT: We went to the bar area after dinner, where they had live music, featuring traditional and fun music from the island. It was definitely very entertaining. After that, we went to the casino which is terribly small, but we aren't big gamblers so we didn't care much. After that, we returned to our room where we attempted to get a movie on pay per view, only to find out that we couldn't order because the hotel reservation system didn't show anybody checked in to our room (??). They promised to fix it, but after waiting for 20 minutes, we decided to give up on that idea.FACILITIES: Very nice, but some construction going on as part of the transition. It didn't bother us too much, but there was some jack-hammering during the day which didn't mix too well with the serene atmosphere of a beach resort. Overall this resort will be great once all of the problems mostly caused by understaffing and renovations are addressed, but the experience we had was somewhat dissapointing.The rate was great, but after staying there, we understood why this resort was mysteriously priced substantially lower than all the other resorts in the island....

<Author>talb
<Content>Not very user friendly I didn't much care for the place but after reading the other reviews it appears that it has improved from its low point in the spring. The room, for example, did not smell musty and was clean, although the shower took a long time to drain. However, it still has a ways to go, and some things can't be fixed. For example, unlike every other resort I've ever seen, the pool, nice as it is, isn't in the center of the resort but off to one end, a VERY long distance from the rooms. During our stay the shuttle ran fairly often until a convention came and most of the shuttles were reserved only for attendees. The beach is narrow and the water not very inviting, although one employee said that will be fixed when the hotel convinces the government that they should be allowed to blow up the reef!Renting a car is a must, considering the cost of the hotel shuttle and on site restaurants. I never saw a taxi at the property. Unfortunately, the hotel charges $10 a day to park, even though its in the middle of nowhere. And the system for paying couldn't be more annoying and inefficient. Every time you enter the property you must take a ticket. When you leave you have to have the ticket validated at the parking office at the opposite end of the hotel from the rooms. Apparently they never heard of a parking pass. The 15 unnecessary speed bumps on the way out to the main road manage to make the experience even more annoying.We never ate at the hotel, instead we bought pastries and drinks at the very good but inexpensive bakery on the main road and kept them in the small refrigerator in the room. We had lunch several times at the bakery near the Wyndham Rio Mar, which had great inexpensive sandwiches made to order. There were lots of restaurants within a few miles, probably better than those at the hotel and certainly much cheaper.

<Author>claudster22
<Content>Beautiful but has problems. We stayed at the Gran Melia PR from May 29-June 4, 2007 for our honeymoon. First off, the hotel is beautiful. The grounds are gorgeous, the pool is awesome and without a doubt the best thing about this hotel. The beach although not very swimable is very prettyas well. The lounge chairs everywhere are relaxing and the cabanas surrounding the pool area are great to lay down, relax and take a good nap. The room was spacious and beautiful as well. Very high celings with a very large marble bathroom. However.................there were many drawbacks. The food and drinks are extremely overpriced and too expensive to really be able to enjoy. We were on a budget, but even if we weren't still think prices are too high. We ate only at the Avocado once for breakfast. All the restaurants are buffet or a la carte. The breakfast at the Avocado although they had a great variety, was mediocre. We payed $48 just for my husband and I and it was not worth it! All the food was cold, the eggs rubbery, the bagels stale an dry. I even spotted a few flies flying around the cold cuts. Pretty gross! Needless to say at those prices we did not eat at the hotel again. The pool swim up bar closes at 6pm! Not much fun if you are on vacation. We could not enjoy the swim up bar either because they charged us $20 for a Long Island Iced Tea and a substitue for a Mojito (they ran out of mint and mix)! The drinks were practically non-alcoholic too. Very weak. Beers cost $8-9 dollars a piece! From then on we went to a loca supermarket, stocked up on beers and wine, bought a foam cooler and kept it in our room. They don't let you walk around with glass bottles or glasess though, so make sure you get some plastic cups too. The Mirador Grill one of the other restaurants by the pool was closedthe whole time we were there. Apparently they will re-open again, butwhat a shame we could not even try that one out. It's an outdoor restaurant with views of the ocean. You are not allowed to eat outside at any of the other restaurants even though they have chairs and tables set up outside.The biggest issue with this hotel is the parking. What an incovenience and mess! Not only do you have to pay $15 a day to park your car, but they do not even have enough spots to accomodate all the people staying there. During the week not as bad, but on the weekends they have a lot of proms, graduation parties, weddings, etc.On two separate occassions we came back from the beaches outside and could not find parking anywhere. We had to valet park. It was an unorganized mess. The worst part was that later on that night when we tried to go out of the hotel for dinner, they could not find our car. They had lost the keys to our car and it took them an hour to find it! Needless to say we lost our dinner resrvations and by the time we got to the restaurant it was closed. They need a better parking system and more parking spaces. It seems they cater more to their weekend party people than their guests. Another thing, the hotel is located in an area that is far and isolated from the highway(Rt. 3). Just to get out of the hotel we had to drive 5 min. and go over 15 speed bumps (yes, I counted). What a hassle! It makes you not want to go anywhere, which is probably what they want. Aside from those problems, the service was pretty good. People and staff were nice and friendly. Jose at the front desk was very helpful and accomodating when we checked out. After telling him our problems he was kind enough to knock off some of the parking fees and a discount on our whole bill.This is a good place to stay only if you plan on being in the pool all day and spending all your money there and nowhere else. If you are the type of people who like to explore and experience being in another country, this is not for you. We ate at Amadeus in Old San Juan once, it was delicious. There are also 2 restaurants off of Route 3 East, one called El Meson next to a Suzuki dealership and one near entrance to Whyndham Rio Mar called Antojitos. Both were very good and reasonably priced.

<Author>milk41358
<Content>Very nice, but not worth $500 per night First of all -- this place was STUPID EXPENSIVE. I didn't have much choice though. I was a cheapo for our honeymoon, and I have been paying for it ever since. I was told by our travel agent that we were getting the Royal Service for no extra charge, which may or may not be true. And, I think if not, then not, our agent was only relaying what she saw on her screen. Anyway, we got a beach-front room even though we were told we were only getting a garden-view room. Maybe it was a mistake. Whatever. I didn't complain about it. It was a great room.Food -- Pretty good! I think almost everything there was good, but I was told by many that the sushi was lousy. We ate at every restaurant, and I had no complaints except that maybe the AC was a little intense at Toscano. I had filet mignon every night, except for the night I had a ribeye. Ahhhh.We were on the all-inclusive plan. (More about that later.) I cannot imagine what it would cost for a meal. I think the bills for our meals would have been around $150 for dinner alone each night (meal, appetizers, deserts, drinks and wine ). Trust me, if we had not been on all-inclusive, we wouldn't have gotten such extravagant meals. We are simple, humble folk.Remember, money really wasn't an issue. I would have spent most anything to provide my wife with a relaxing vacation. Trust me -- she deserved it.The Royal Service was DEFINITELY the way to go. I loved the Royal Service lounge. Anytime I wanted, I could pop in to use the computer or get a drink without having to wait at the bar. The computer was very nice, and I was able to take care of a little business at home while I was away. Snacks were also provided in the lounge. The Royal Service pool was nice, but small.SERVICE -- People like to talk about the laid back atmosphere of the Caribbean. Yeah, that's great except for when you're paying $500 per day for your room, and time really is money -- a lot of money. You will spend a lot of time (and money) waiting if you don't raise your voice. Some people call it rudeness. I call it ASSERTIVENESS, and sometimes your level of ASSERTIVENESS must rise to meet the hosts' LEVEL OF APATHY. If someone on the staff is being dismissive or slow to act, SPEAK UP. It's your money. (More about that later.)Remember, YOU DESERVE GOOD SERVICE. if you demand good service, you will get it. If you are o.k. with someone wasting your heard-earned money, then by all means, keep quiet. This is rated as a 5-Start Hotel, and you SHOULD EXPECT BETTER. The SPA: My wife loved it. She had a massage, and some of that other stuff. It was o.k. with me, but I don't really get into spas. I had a massage by a very pretty young lady, and I wasn't sure how to deal with that. I mean, if I'm enjoying it, am I being unfaithful? But, isn't the point of the massage to enjoy it? Every time, I started to relax, I thought Oh, this feels too good. Then, I would think, hmmm, better not enjoy it too much, right? Oh, too much confusion. Too many questions. And, no booze at the spa. Apparently, drinking prior to getting into a hot tub is dangerous.The ROOM: Very nice -- just like the website photos, but the floor was marble and very slippery. The TV was great. I looked through the pay-per-views movies. There must have been 50 ADULT movies. Geez, how many dirty movies can one person watch in a week? It seemed like overkill. The bed was o.k. The AC was great. Bathroom was nice also. We had a no-so-private hot tub on our porch facing the ocean. It was o.k., but we learned one night that it's REAL easy to lock yourself out. Someone had to come and open the door for us. We also learned that the secondary lock was useless. (It's kinda like a door chain but steel bar instead of chain.) They have been bent open to disable them. The maintenance guy just unlocked the door came right in even though we had the lock on that is supposed to be opened only from the inside. Also, I liked the in-room safe. It opens with a code rather than a key.ROOM SERVICE: LOUSY, LOUSY, LOUSY even though we supposedly had Royal Service. And, when you check in, CARRY YOUR OWN BAGS TO YOUR ROOM. We waited HOURS to get our bags. I had to berate the front deck baggage man just to get our clothing. We wanted to get to the pool, but they were holding out luggage hostage. It was at this point that we started learning about that laid back attitude that we could come to loathe. We could have easily carried the luggage the five-minute walk to the room, but they insisted so we relented. We didn't make that same mistake when we checked out. POOL: Fantastic, just like in the website photos.BEACH: Not so great. There's a lot of muck and plants in to water, but another person told me that once you get past that the snorkeling wasn't so bad. EXCURSIONS: We went snorkeling with the on-site company. It was just o.k. The water was choppy and deep. It also took forever just to get there, and I was glad when it was over. We used a rental car to explore Old San Juan and the forts -- definitely worth seeing -- as well as El Yunque Rain Forest. El Yunque was o.k., but it looked pretty much like the mountains of NC, which I can see anytime. The only difference were the Coqui frogs. There's a hike they tell you to take to a waterfall -- not worth it, in my opinion unless you LOVE waterfalls and you plan to swim. And, AVOID THE CEMETERY AREA IN SAN JUAN. Just don't go there or to the tiny ocean-side neighborhood next to it. These are DANGEROUS areas.RENTAL CAR: After waiting in line for two hours, I learned that our RENTAL CAR WAS NOT AVAILABLE when we went to pick it up at the on-site HERTZ desk. Our reservation was apparently not a reservation. Instead, your reservation is merely the right to reserve a reservation. There was no car available for our first day, and nothing would change that. After much of my yelling, which regrettably made the HERTZ lady cry, we got a Pontiac Aztec at a very low rate. But, we only got it for one day. The next day we got a Cadillac. The Hertz lady was very nice, but she was constrained by the lack on a computer on-site. She said she didn't know what she would get each day. If you plan to rent, see the Hertz lady a day ahead to get everything sorted out. They most likely will NOT have what you reserved so be prepared to be disappointed. ALL-INCLUSIVE: Better than paying every time, and with the prices like the were -- $8 for a drink, $100 for dinner -- it worked better for us. I'll gladly pay extra to avoid extra hassles. Some people didn't get the all-inclusive plan. There was some kind of an electrician's convention, and one of the wives was begging for drinks at the bar. She didn't have an all-inclusive wrist band on. She claimed she couldn't get the bartender's attention, and wanted me to order for her. It was annoying. I knew what she was doing so I said, I will order a drink and swim away. If it's not here when I get back, I'll just assume it got poured out. Luckily, the bartender never came back to me. He was too busy taking care of the people who were tipping.TIPPING: In spite of the all-inclusive talk, TIPPING STILL MATTERS. I found that I got much more attention when I gave the bartender a few dollars. We tipped one guy really well, and he spent the evening coming with new drinks for us and a couple we went snorkeling with. One was on fire. I also taught the bartender a new drink. MUCHO DRINKO. MUCHO HANGOVERO. SUMMARY:Pool - A Beach - CFood - A Service - C- (But F if you consider that this is rated a 5-star hotel.) Accommodations - B+ Rental Car - D Old San Juan / Forts - A It was 70/30, but the poor service brought everything else down. I will not return, and I can recommend it only with a warning to BE ASSERTIVE so that you will get what you paid for.

<Author>chicagotvd
<Content>Felt like prison Gran Melia was once an all-inclusive which would have been great, except they changed two days prior to our arrival. Positives:Beautiful resort, great pool, okay service.Negatives:Way too expensive...Corona's were $7.00. An 8 ounce draft of local beer was $6.00. Food was TERRIBLE. The hotel is 3.5 miles from the main drag which limits any walking that you want to do. Gran Melia is an all-inclusive type hotel minus the all-inclusiveness. Suggestions:Rent a car at the airport. Transfers to the Hotel are $60.00 per person for a round trip ($120.00 for my wife and I). Do the math, you can rent a car for a week on that money. My wife and I ended up renting from the Avis at the hotel (at least $20.00 more than at the airport) and drove ourselfs around the island just to get away from the resort which didn't have much to offer except the sun.If you want to enjoy a cocktail or two during the day...go to the local grocery store, buy a six or twelve pack and bring it in. Or, buy some rum and mixers and bring it in. You'll save yourself a bunch of money.This hotel/resort is great if you have a lot of money to spend and want to sit by a pool all day. But, if you want to experience a true Puerto Rican environment and get bored laying out, rent a car, drive to the east side of the island, find a remote beach, and hang out in the many beach side cities. I WOULD NOT RECOMMEND THIS PLACE FOR ANYONE WHO WANTS TO DO MORE THEN LAY DOWN ALL DAY.

<Author>USAlawyer
<Content>A terrific resort Our family stayed at the Paradisus - Puerto Rico for a week in mid April 2007, and had a wonderful time. The grounds are lovely - beautifully landscaped and well maintained. The rooms are spacious and nicely furnished. (The bathroom is large with marble floors and countertops, large mirror and terrific water pressure). The AC works well - actually a bit too strong for my taste - so the ceiling fan was fine. There was a musty odor when we first got to the room - which seems to emanate from the AC unit. As soon as we turned it off, and used the fan, the odor was eliminated.Negative comments about the staff should simply be disregarded. From the reservation desk, to the poolside bar to the activities center - all of the staff with whom we interacted were friendly and helpful. Everyone we encountered greeted us warmly and with a smile. As long as you are friendly and courteous, you will receive the same in return.The beach is not what most envision for the Caribbean - it is rocky with seaweed patches. But all you would need are aqua shoes and you are set to go. The water is warm and clear - actually warmer than the pool on some days! There are kayaks and boats to use or just a long stretch of coast to walk and find shells.During our trip, the Paradisus was still an all-inclusive. The choice of restaurants was fine. We had breakfast each day at Caribeno - a wonderful assortment (eggs, fresh omelettes, pancakes, bacon, oatmeal, fresh fruit, blintzes, muffins, bagels, juices, and Puerto Rican specialties etc.). It also has a lunch buffet that was great. We had lunch at Mirador grill since it was closest to the pool. The lunch there is average, but one could always find something to satisfy the appetite. The dinner choices (beyond Mirador Grill) were Romantico (adult only, so since we have a teenager and 8-year-old we did not try it); Bamboo (a Japanese hibatchi-style restaurant - very nice, tasty - John Carlo was our chef and was terrific); Avocado (typical steakhouse - make sure to have the shrimp at the buffet - they are large and delicious); Toscano (rather pedestrian Italian fare). All in all, the selections were numerous, the entrees were well presented, and the staff at each restaurant was attentive and pleasant. Keep in mind, this is not a resort know for gourmet food. However, there is something for everyone, and in general, the food was above average.A few tips - check-out is at noon. Be sure to check out at 8:30 to avoid the rush. You can then leave your bags in a locked room near the front entrance, enjoy the remainder of your stay at the pool and then shower and change in a fully-equipped salon next to where you leave your bags. Don't book trips to El Yunque rainforest or Old San Juan through the hotel. The costs are exhorbitant. Instead, rent a car from the Avis representative at the hotel (Gina was ours - she was great). We rented a car for a day ($70) and went to the rainforest (20 minutes away), Luquillo Beach (another 10 minutes away) and then drove back west to Old San Juan. If we had booked the tour through the hotel, this would have cost more than $500 for the 4 of us. We'd go back to Paradisus tomorrow. It was wonderful.  
<Date>May 4, 2007

The handicapped person did not receive the requested handicapped room. The second couple did not receive the requested king bed. We returned to the registration desk to seek correction. Believe it or not it took almost one hour of confusion to check in.We were informed that dinner reservations had closed at 4:30 and we could present ourselves to any of the several restaurants for seating without a reservation. Nothing could be farther from the truth as we arrived at first restaurant and we were informed that we could not be seated until 9:00, a little late after a long day of travel from the states. I sought the help of the night manager who obtained us a table at the Bamboo Restaurant. For a 5-star resort we were shocked by the brusque service. It was as if we were intruding on the staff's routine. The food was expensive and unsavory. Duck in wrap was cooked so hard that we could not eat it. We were much relieved to finally get to bed. The next morning the breakfast buffet was fabulous as it was each morning. Breakfast was the best meal of the day. Trying to get food at the pool was another matter. There is none. You must go into the restaurant for lunch. I asked the receptionist if I could take some food to the pool. She explained that it was not allowed but that I could wrap up some food in a napkin and take it out. That I did each day. We had two excellent meals at Avocado and Romantique. The resort is in the process of renaming the restaurants. Avocado food was superb but the service was about 2 star if that. The waitress insisted upon delivering our check before our dinner was complete. Since we had the same annoying experience the evening before I pointed the oversight out to her , and she insisted that was what management required. I explained to her that the check should not be presented until the guest asks for it particularly so if dessert or coffee is likely to be requested. My comments did not make any impression, instead she argued with me. Apparently there must be guest walk-outs without signing or paying the restaurant bills. On several occasions we were asked when leaving the restaurant if we had signed. Rude? Yes?The best meal was at Romantique and the worst at the the Bamboo and the Mexican restaurant whose name I cannot recall. The service at Romantique was impeccable. I asked the waiter why so much difference between the service at the various restaurants. Training and experience was the answer. And, of course management.Our handicapped friend and his wife were locked out of their bungalow after dinner one evening during a heavy rain. The electronic keys had failed. Repeated calls to the front desk did not bring help. Luckily a staff person happened by and opened the door after 30 minutes. I complained to the night manager and was informed that mobile phones will deactivate the door keys. The inconvenience of being locked out was compounded by the long distance to the bungalow. It is not merely an elevator ride to the lobby to reactivate the key. I suggested that the locked out guests should be compensated. I thought it unusual when the night manger asked how. I said at the least a bottle of wine to the unconvinced guests. The next evening a nice bottle of wine and cheese was provided to our friends. Paradisus is beautiful. A swimming beach is non-existent. However the pool is beautiful with a swim-up bar with pleasant bartenders. To obtain a cabana you must get up early and occupy your site. No towels are laid out for you. My impression of the hotel is that it lacks knowledgeable management. Maybe it is the Caribbean attitude. It is certainly not the attitude and service we have experienced at other Spanish owned hotels. At a so-called 5-star resort I would expect more concern for guests.

<Author>cmc2275
<Content>Beautiful resort and great food but customer service lacking I just returned from a 5 day trip to the Paradisus. We upgraded to Royal Service. Our review is mixed: we had a wonderful, relaxing time but the customer service is REALLY lacking.  First, the Royal Service turned out to be a good thing for checking-in (we were able to bypass the front desk) and for making dinner reservations and also for reserving the huts with beds at the Royal Service pool. The Royal Service pool was great---not crowded and quiet. No children are permitted. There is also a separate bar at the Royal Service pool. That is the only upside to Royal Service but highly recommend it since we couldn't imagine what the service would have been like if we didn't have it.The food at the resort was excellent. We tried all the restaurants except the Italian. Order the filet mignon where you can. The Asian Fusion restaurant was ok but the menu was limited and again, the service was lacking. Breakfast and lunch are buffets but don't be scared---the food was great and varied. The lunch buffet had fresh fish, sandwiches, hot foods, gourmet salads, etc.The rooms were clean and spacious. Each room has a balcony with chairs. We had no bedbugs as earlier reviews reported (believe me, we checked). We thought the beach was beautfiul. Very natural setting but it is not a beach where you swim in the water so we did hear that people were disapponted in that. You could take beach chairs down to the water but most people were by the pool (which had a great view of the ocean). There is no snorkeling.The problem we had was the service. We have been to a few all-inclusives and the staff would do anything to make your stay comfortable. We were used to the friendly, enthusiastic and proactive service of the staff at the resorts in Mexico and the Dominican Republic. But here, it always seemed like we were bothering the staff when asking for a drink or even checking in at the hostess station and EVEN at the Royal Servie lounge! We found ourselves standing in front of a hostess or at the bar and we would sense this attitude of We will get to you when we are ready. There was no acknowledgment of We will be with you in a second. This attitude was pervasive and it wasn't any better at the Royal Service pool. At points on the trip, it felt like we were on a 'Seinfeld' or 'Curb your Enthusiasm' episode. We would be the only people in line for say, lunch. The restaurant was just opening and there were only 4 people standing there to get in (and NO ONE was in the restaurant). They would not acknowledge that you were standing there until they were ready (we almost thought they were faking busy) and then they would take our names and tell us that it would be a few minutes. This was funny in itself since the restaurant was open and no one was inside. Then seconds later--with still only 4 people standing there--the hostess would seriously yell out our name like she had no idea where we were. We were like, we're right here, you just took our names 5 seconds ago. If we hadn't spoken up, I was convinced she would have just crossed our name off the list. It became comical. And it didn't matter if you tipped every bartender or server (which we did). Another scenario was when we would request a refill of water or request a utensil or napkin. We would both have empty water glasses and only the person that asked for the water, got a refill. We had to stop the server from walking away so they could refill the other glass. At the buffet, they take away your plate each time you go back up, so usually your fork would be missing when you got back. It was getting so hard to get someone to come to the table that we saw the drawer where they were getting the forks and would just help ourselves. Thank god the food and the resort were excellent or we would have not enjoyed ourselves as much as we did. We did have 2 excellent servers: Harry at the Romantico restaurant and Diana at the Avocado Restaurant. Very friendly and proactive. Glasses were refilled with water and wine and they would check-in with you to make sure you had everything you needed (and if you needed something, they would actually come back to give it to you within a 15 minute period.)So, in summary: despite our frustration with the serivce, if you are booked for the all-inclusive in the next month (the hotel changes hands May 1st--no all inclusive after that point), I would say that you will love the resort and the food. It is a great place to unwind and relax. Just be forewarned that the staff has a laissez-faire attitude.

<Author>HudsonValleyMama
<Content>A pleasant surprise I never write reviews, although I do pay attention to them. I read a lot of bad reviews before going to Paradisus this March and was a bit nervous. I'm happy to report that after a week with my husband and 2 grown sons, we all had a wonderful experience. Check-in was a breeze. We took our luggage to our room so delivery of baggage wasn't an issue. We had Royale Service, which I highly recommend. The room (ocean view) was very nice, clean and well appointed. Maid service was excellent .The Royale Service pool was fabulous. We reserved a private palapa each day with no problem. The bartenders and attendants were extremely efficient and friendly. (When a gentleman dropped a piece of fruit poolside a nearby bartender quickly picked it up, washed it, and returned it to the man's lounge chair. ) Our private butler introduced himself to us the first day. And although we never used his services, he saw my husband 3 days later and spoke to him by name! (very impressive)The grounds are beautiful and extremely well kept up and clean. No surprise....the beach was not great - can't really walk it or swim. But the kayaking was fun.We didn't expect gourmet food and didn't get it. (This is the reason I'm not giving this resort a 5* rating) The breakfast and lunch buffets were terrific (But avoid the Mirador Grill - ugh! opt for the Carribean instead) Romantico is over rated. We enjoyed Avocado and Tuscano better. Bamboo is your typical hibachi place.(Avocado has great beef) Overall we found that the beef was much better than the fish -fine for my sons but my husband and I prefer seafood. The snacks that were always set up in the Royale Service Lounge were great.There was a problem with a restaurant booking one night. When the RS manager called to explain we couldn't get the time we reserved at our chosen restaurant, we didn't make a big deal about it. He quickly got us a table at another restaurant. Fifteen minutes later he, along with a waiter, arrived at our room with a bottle of wine and a plate of hors d'oeuvres to make ammends for the mistake. Now that's great PR!!! I cannot stress the cleanliness enough - everywhere! Especially the bathrooms. EVERYONE (maids, shuttle drivers, bartenders, waitstaff, gardeners, watersports staff, etc. etc) was extremely warm and friendly, and always quick to greet us.Certainly everyone cannot expect to have as good an experience as we had. But I do recommend it highly and hope that some people will take advantage of this great all-inclusive resort before it no longer is all-inclusive as of May 1.

<Author>SkiKat
<Content>Pretty Darned Good Having been to Puerto Rico several times before, we were able to avoid some of the potential hassles and overall had a really nice time. Hopefully, some of these tips can help you. The hotels in PR tend to be pricy - Paradisus included. However, Paradisus serves decent food in the buffets, very good food in the reservations required places and has top shelf drinks included - the value is not bad as compared to other places. Paradisus has nice, large rooms with balconies. The beach is OK, not great. But the pools are wonderful and the place is large - i.e. not crowded. The service staff is primarily younger folks (this is not their career unlike what you find in many other Carribean destinations) - you see many of the things that can come with that - service is not always rapid fire or accurate - but it is generally very good. The hotel is well outside of San Juan. If you want to do excursions with a tour company, you get stuck with the inevitable waits you see anywhere in the world. (I abhor waits and shuttles) Here's some advice - if you are going to leave the resort and tour or partake in excursions, rent a car. Driving in PR is easy, rental cars are cheap, picking them up at the airport is fast and easy, self park is close to the rooms. A lot of cool stuff can be done on your own, you don't need a tour company. Or, hook up with the tour company at the destination rather than waiting on a shuttle. There are a lot of people from the North East. They, generally, have a more brusque approach to things - if that really bothers you, don't go to PR because it is a big destination for New Yorkers.

<Author>p20nch
<Content>A week in paradise I felt I needed to add a review to this website after using it in preparation for our family's trip. I read through many reviews ranging from this place is hell on earth, to greatest destination I have ever been. After the reviews I did not know what to expect, but I trusted my family's decision and could not wait to get away. Our party included 18 people ranging in age from my grandparents to young cousins. I am a 29 year old male. I should note here that our last family trip to an all-inclusive resort was a disaster. Stay away from Playa Naco in the Dominican Republic at all costs. Paradisus was head and shoulders above our last experience. The trip to and from the airport was about 40 minutes by van and not bad at all. Our first order of business was an upgrade to royal service. I recommend this move if your budget allows. It provided access to a few extra ammenities including a separate royal service pool (ask for the mojitos), and some upgrades in rooms and dining. The all inclusive food and drink worked out very well for our party. It was great to be able to eat or get a drink at any time, day or night. My uncle was able to force me into a shot of tequila and a beer as I stepped out of breakfast one morning. The quality of the food was very good over all. This included the breakfast (good omelettes) and lunch buffets, and all of the different restaurants on sight. The only negatives here were the slow service at one or two of the restaurants, and some confusion over reservations. Not bad over all. Room service (try the quesadilla) and butlers were also free with royal service. The main pool in the center of the resort was a lot of fun for all including water basketball and other sports. I should note here, if you are a looking for a beach-front resort, paradisus is not for you. The pools were great and there was a beach volleyball court. The sand and beach area were not great. The staff and service was very competent and friendly over all, including one woman with beautiful eyes that my brother is still talking about. Some slow service in the restaurants but we had a party of 18 to serve each night. We were lucky enough to have great weather for most of the week. A little overcast and rain at times. The resort did get buggy at night and my feet and ankles were pretty bitten up all week. On our last night we were fortunate enough to catch the white party. A dance party where guests and staff (yes she was there) showed up wearing white and we danced and drank until the wee hours of the morning. A great way to end the week. My family's review was very positive over all. We all had a great time and I would recommend the resort. My major complaints were the lack of a great beach area and the bugs. I think I covered the important points and I hope you find the review helpful. Bring your sunblock and bug spray and enjoy the trip. Have a mojito for me.

If you travel a great deal, you know- tip when appropriate-yes it is an all inclusive and no you shouldn't have to give extra but if it makes life easier to part with a few singles here and there, why not? Youwill be amazed how much better attitudes become. Royal service also provides a separate, adult pool that is only for royal service guests. It is a smaller pool but definitely more quiet and allows personalized attention. A word of advice, try to get poolside before 10:00 to insure your own cabana for the day. As other travelers stated, the beach is nothing to be in awe of and swimming there is not ideal. But it still makes for a nice stroll and to dip your toes in. They do have paddle boats and catamarans to enjoy.The 5 star element here is undoubtedly the grounds. Paradisus is a breathtaking place to behold and the attention to its decor is amazing. If only they placed remotely close attention to their food. There is nothing 5 star about it. I have been told that all inclusives almost never have gourmet food. Everyone was right.The food here is fine if you do not expect stellar chef delicacies. We ate at every restaurant except Toscano. Romantico was more upscale and other travelers said it was the best pick.My boyfriend had a delicious lamb entree but my seafood entree was inedible and I had to return it to the kitchen only to be told it would take another hour AGAIN to bring me something. I left hungry and couldn't believe the mis management with that one. I would have opted for room service when we got back but the room service menu is extremely limited.The casino is definitely larger than a closet as another trip advisor member stated. It's actually a decent size and staffed with friendly employees.The spa is also nice although small. We had a couples massage which was delightful although quite expensive even for 80 minutes.I began the trip to Paradisus filled with trepidation due to so many negative reviews but the stay here was lovely, with not a bed bug in sight, thank god!I think perhaps if Paradisus lowers it's star rating, expectations will not be so high. Based on my personal experience as well as that of my boyfriend, I can tell you that if you do stay here, you can expect a wonderfully, relaxing time. It was a little taste of heaven for us. How could it not be when you are lounging poolside and the most energy asked of you is to lift your head up to ask for another drink? Just remember, heaven doesn't come cheap!

<Author>petulia
<Content>Total Rip Off - Not as All-Inclusive as You Would think. There was only one family ahead of us but it took us 45 minutes to get checked in. However, most of the restaurants offer buffet-style appetizer dining and in my book, no classy restaurant makes you run around and serve yourself. in addition to which the different cuisines that they offer (french, italian, carribean, etc) offer largely the same array of dishes for the appetizers, which is very disappointing. The presentation and quality of the food also very disappointing. A japanese restaurant with no chopsticks, for example, is just weird. The all-day dining room service menu stinks too. They offer sandwiches, BLT's, hamburgers, for the most part. The fanciest offerings are a shrimp ceviche and beef carpaccio, but they are mediocre at best. And you are restricted to 2 beers per room per night. What the hell is that?Spa - They tell you it is included, and that the massage/facial treatments are not included, but in fact the use of the spa is only included if you have a facial/massage appointment that day. Those treaments cost between $80-$165 and the spa itself (we had a look) is pretty meager. The spa in my gym at home is set up better than what they have there. In order to even use the spa by itself, you have to pay $28, which makes it in fact NOT inclusive at all as part of the package. We were so annoyed by this that we canceled our appointment at the spa since we just had a feeling that it would not be a very good experience in the end. Beach - The nice part of the beach is that it is never overcrowded since it only serves those staying in this hotel. The problem is that it is completely rocky and you cannot really walk on it without shoes on. there really is no sand to speak of, more like gravelly pebbles, which smart quite a bit on the feet. Not surfable for sure, at least not while i have been here.The Hotel Building - Really beautiful, very photogenic, it really is a sprawling complex that is great and not over crowded and well-decorated. Conclusions - I just think that this is the very problem with this hotel which is that it looks good but tastes like crap. The fact that the food is so mediocre is a really big problem because the least that they can do is offer excellent food and it is just too disappointing in the end and there is no excuse for it given how much money people have to spend here. And honestly, if you just want to relax and have a beautiful time and eat good food and not feel ripped off, then don't go here.

<Author>jaypatent
<Content>There are better options . . . . Unfortunately, while the property was lovely, enough lapses occurred that I cannot recommend vacationing here. We stayed just before Christmas 2006 in a Royal Service Oceanfront Junior Suite. We found our room musty and poorly ventilated. The beach was for walking only, and not for swimming--we had to hire a driver to take us to a nearby beach for that purpose. The enormous pool is gorgeous, but not heated. Two restaurants were open for breakfast and lunch. One, the Mirador, was infested with a number of black birds. Several of them landed on the bread line of the buffet and picked away while we were seated there. The remaining quickly circled our table. The staff did nothing, so we left promptly. We ate the rest of our breakfasts and lunches at the other restaurant, which typically opened 5-10 minutes late.We found the Royal Service not particularly helpful in making reservations. Rather than arrange travel or tennis for us, for example, we were simply directed to queue up at the front desk, concierge, or travel desk. Royal Service did provide a prompt check in and check out, however, and also gave us access to the charming Royal Service Suite as a base of operations. The suite was far less musty than our room, and featured a TV, Internet access, drinks, and a small buffet.Although the hotel boasts that tennis lessons are available at certain times, in fact the staff will simply call local tennis pros to see if one will visit on-site. Nobody was available during our stay, so my daughter didn't receive a lesson.The hotel cancelled one of our restaurant reservations (at Bamboo) just a few hours before we had arranged to arrive. Other restaurants were closed for one or more nights during our stay. I found the food on whole rather undistinguished, with the exception of the fine meal served by the Romantica. The decor of each of the restaurants is quite spartan, and all but the Romantica have what is essentially the same buffet as your appetizer. As buffets go, they are probably above average, but the food was at times underheated. Given the Rain Forest nearby, it was not surprising that the weather was overcast for much of the trip. Scattered showers during the day are apparently very common here. Finally, there was no shortage of mosquitos on site.Overall, not bad, but at this price point superior accommodations are available in this part of the world.

<Content>Loved it . . . My wife and I had never been to an all inclusive resort before, so we weren't sure what to expect. The resort is beautiful, the room was very nice. Again, the resort wasn't crowded while we were there, so your results may differ.All in all, it's a nice facility and we were treated well. They market themselves as a five star resort, and I would say that's a stretch. However, I would place them solidly amongst the 4 star resorts I've stayed at before, and I'm no pushover.

We found plenty of kids running around the pool and a bit noisy than we expected. Overall, we would like to go back for our 1 year anniversary.!

<Author>susandances
<Content>One of the BEST! We just returned from a long weekend at the Paradisus (July 21 - 24) and had a spectacular time! Do Not believe the negative reviews! The resort is absolutely beautiful, from the grounds to the rooms. My husband and I paid for the Royal Service and I would highly recommend that you pay the extra for it. We did not wait long at all to check in (there was one person ahead of us). I will say that the line was extremely long for regular check-in and we met a family that waited 2 hours to check in. Therefore, do the Royal Service if you can. Upon arrival, our butler (Manuel) drove us to the Royal Service pool, reserved a Palapas (wonderful hut w/mattress and pillows) for us for our entire stay, got us drinks and booked us reservations for dinner for our stay. You definitely need to book dinner reservations when you arrive. We found that they tend to say that the non-buffet restaurants are booked, but if you insist or just show-up you most likely will get in. We ate at Romantico twice and really enjoyed it. The food was very good and the service was excellent. The other night we ate at Avacado which was quite good, too, though not as good as Romantico. We ate breakfast and lunch at Mirador and contrary to what others have written, my husband and I enjoyed our meals there. It is not gourmet food and a lot of it is their local cuisine, but the food is perfectly good. It is an open-air restuarant and views of the ocean are wonderful. Every morning we asked them if they would cut us a fresh mango and they never had a problem with it. We has excellent service there, too!The Royal Service pool is quiet and our bartenders (Pedro and Leslie) were excellent! They would check on us quite often and bring us drinks. Both bartenders made great rum drinks!If you are truly a beach person then this may not be for you. The beach is very rocky and there is a lot of seaweed and what not at the shore. We did take a kayak out one day and we were able to get out of it and swim in the water further out. The ocean water is warmer than the pool! We never really ventured over to the main pool. It was very crowded while we were there (there were 2 conventions). There were many activities going on every day (salsa lessons, water aerobics, karaoke, etc). My husband and I were there for relaxation and that is exactly what we got! I did get a massage at the spa and it was wonderful! If you have the time and the money, I would recommend it!All in all, this was one of the best vacations we have been on. We have been to Puerto Rico before and have stayed at what was once the Hyatt Cerromar and this was much better! The Paradisus is a beautiful resort with lovely accomodations, good food and just a really wonderful time!

<Author>scottnic
<Content>Had a decent time, but not 5 star quality!!! We just came back from our stay at the Paradisus this past week, July 15-19. It was my husband, me and my 2 year old. We had a good time, but there were definitely some negatives which the hotel needs to address. The whole reservations thing for dinner is absolutely ridiculous for an all-inclusive resort. I've never heard that anywhere else. We were able to get reservations every night, but the timing was terrible, especially with a two year old. Our earliest dinner was at 8:15, and we even had one at 9:45 one night. Yes, we could have eaten at the outdoor buffet from 3:30 - 5:30, but why pay the outrageous price on all-inclusive and get mediocre food. The Bamboo was the best, and the Caribeno was great for breakfast and lunch. The Mirador food was not so good. After the first day, we never went back. We knew about the beach from reading all the reviews, so that wasn't much of a surprise. They do try to make up for it by providing paddle boats, kayaks, and wind surfing on the beach, I thought that was nice. The pool was nice, and we mostly spend our entire vacation there. The next biggest hassle were waiting for the golf carts to go to the restaurants and pools every day. Although it's not a great length, when you have a two year old and are expecting another, the walk is not nice. I am not a very hard pleaser, but when you shell out the kind of money for an all-inclusive 5 star hotel, you expect certain amenities along with comfort and relaxation. We own a time share in the Mayan Riviera and stayed at an all inclusive for our honeymoon. I could say hands down that the Aventura Spa Palace there, which was also all-inclusive, was by far more relaxing and accomodating to a vacationer's needs (i.e. no charge for room service, mini-fridge stocked with food, chocolate, cookies, drinks of all sorts, no reservation needed for dinner). Overall, the place was nice and we had a good time, but there were things here and there that just seemed so tricky or penny pinching about the resort, that I couldn't give it a full thumbs up (The room service menu stated that they couldn't bring up a carton of milk for the baby, we had to take it from breakfast or lunch every day and keep it in the fridge). We stayed at the regular villas, and it seems like those with rave reviews all had the royal service, maybe that is much nicer. We would probably not go back.

<Author>Beachlover888
<Content>Some flaws .... but overall very nice We (2 adults) just returned from a week at the Paradisus. For months I read the comments on the tripadvisor and had very mixed feelings about the resort. Well, overall I have to say that we enjoyed our stay very much. Service was very good, friendly and helpful. We got all the dinner reservations we desired and the times we wanted. On the first evening, since we arrived around 6 PM, the concierge desk was already closed. But we went to the Toscana restaurant and were welcomed and seated within minutes. The buffet style Italian food was very good and offered a nice variety and the wait staff was excellent. That was a promising beginning!!!The front desk could not honor our request for a king-size bed room (reason was never explained), but offered us a room with two double beds pushed together (which was acceptable) in the Royal section without the royal service. (The rooms are basically the same in the royal and non-royal section). Yes, the beach is nothing, also the water is clear and warm, but the coral and coarse sand and rocks are not nice. I brought my aqua shoes and spent every day a bit of time wading knee deep in the water, seeing quite a few fish. The pool is large and busy the whole day long. We found an umbrella shaded area (bed) every day, since we were at the pool around 7:30AM. I am a bit puzzled about the remarks of another tripadvisor writer in relation to the pool bar. We usually requested our last drink at the pool around 4:30PM and never had a problem with it not being honored or even having to wait. We never ordered drinks while in the water. Like I said, the staff was great everywhere.We were able to eat in all restaurants and the food was excellent. Bamboo: great Japanese tepanyaki....the day we went, two seats on our table were empty.La Romantica: great food, a lovely ambience and an attentive wait staffAvocado: steak and fish dishes were excellent, service very efficient even on a day when there were a lot of large tables (convention) who required so much extra work.Carabena: breakfast and lunch buffets were always presented very well with lots of things to choose from. Fresh fruit every day, great salads and cold cuts (salmon and prociutto crudo) and a friendly wait staff to refill your water or drinks. I tried the scambled eggs and they were very good, not at all rubbery and dry as some reviewers indicated. Mirador: this was a bit disappointing, especially the evening meal there. It is buffet style and there is no Mexican ambience and the wait staff is the slowest. I would not recommend the Mirador for dinner. Unfortunately, the resort creates some of the problems with insisting of stationing a hostess at the door for breakfast and lunch buffets. One has to constantly wait for the hostess, because she is off seating people, and that creates a backup.We were at the Paradisus when there was a convention with 250 people and it tended to be crowded and loud during breakfast and lunch. Not 5star quality!!!One remark from a previous writer about no food available after 3PM until dinner time, is not correct. The Mirador, which is the outdoor restaurant close to the pool, serves snack food between 3:30 and 5:30PM. We went ithere once and were offered chips and dips, pizza, chicken nuggets and a few other things. So, there is always something to eat.We used the resort shuttle bus for transportation to and from the airport and it was efficient and quick. No problems other than upon arrival at San Juan airport the driver neglected to hold up a sign for Paradisus, but had only a sign for travelocity. When we could not locate the bus, I had to call the resort and then a staff member located us immediately and escorted us to the waiting bus. So, a bit of confusion.... but no harm done.The bell hop service worked great upon check in, but we called for luggage pick up upon check out and nobody showed at the appointed time. We wheeled our luggage to the lobby by ourselves.We did not use room service and did not frequent any bars other than the pool bar.If you plan to travel there with children, I think the activity desk does a lot to keep the kids entertained. There were always games offered and other activities and we saw a lot of happy kids. In summation..... the resort is beautiful and the grounds very nice. Would we go there again? .. probably, but given all the other places in the Caribbean, we tend not to go to the same place every year. If you have any questions, please feel free to send me an email. I will be happy to give you my view.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Had a Blast My wife and I picked the Paradisus Puerto Rico, because we had stayed at Sol Melia All Inclusives before (Playa Conchal Costa Rica), and we were curious about seeing Puerto Rico. We also thought we could (and did) get a good deal in the off-season (last week of June). After we made the reservation, we had some difficulty getting answers to some of our emails, but were still excited to go. Then someone suggested checking out Trip Advisor. Wish we had not. The reviews were negative, and just made us anxious about the whole thing. As it turned out, we had a great time. The food, facility, service, area etc. were all wonderful. We play golf, and the Resorts nearby were excellent (Coco Beach and Rio Mar). If you play golf, you must play the Lakes and Mountain Courses at Coco Beach, and the River course at the Rio Mar. The hotel will take you to the Coco Beach course for free, and pick you up. We did not run into a single unhappy person at the hotel, and everyone was wondering what provoked those negative reviews. As for ourselves, we have nothing, but good things to say. As others have said, you should make your dinner reservations for the whole week as soon as possible. Also be advised that if you rent a car and drive there, the self-parking is $10.00 per day. The area and facility are beautiful. If you do go, plan ahead for checking out. We called three times to get our bill, so that we could do Express Check-out. We finally gave up and went to the front desk. Luckily no one was in line and we were immediately taken care of. We hated to leave, because we had a blast.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not very All Inclusive at all... I've stayed a couple of times this year (work-related). Here are my observations:* Rooms are gorgeous, perhaps the best thing the resort has, besides the lobby.* Room service takes almost an hour, with a $3 charge (all inclusive?). Still, we decided to keep using room service for the reason stated in the following bullet.* Restaurants are not open all the time. They open at 6 or 6:30AM and then they close at 11-11:30AM. Then, they open at 12:00 to close at 3PM, and then you have to wait until 6PM for dinner. So, if you just decided to go to bed late because you kept hanging out or watched movies until 3AM, then you have to adjust yourself to their schedule so you get to eat something. Unless, you use cold-food room service. Then, if you are at the pool and suddenly you realize it's 3:30PM, you're [----] because you have to wait until 6PM (that, of course, if you happen to have a reservation for that time!!!!). So, if you're hypoglycemic, don't ever come to this hotel! Or, leave the pool, go back to the room, and ask for cold-food room service... again.* Reservations: They sell you this hotel over the internet and ads as a top class resort with amazing restaurants blah blah blah. But, the restaurants are always full, and you have to make reservations the day you check in, not before. So, you may have to wait until 10PM to get to eat to at the Bamboo (Japanese restaurant), which is amazingly great, by the way, but always full. There's always buffet food at the Mirador and Caribe帽o, but believe me, the food is not very good. The restaurants close before midnight, and there's no such thing as midnight munch like in cruises. Either you starve, or go back to your room (even if you're supposed to be out enjoying the resort lobby and facilities) and, guess what, order room service.* Bamboo and Avocado are the best restaurants. However, I have observed that now they are serving much less in restaurants than before, and the quality of the buffet food in general (especially lunch and dinner) is declining.* The Pool is beautiful, kids will have a great time.* The Beach is probably the ugliest beach in Puerto Rico, by far. It's full of rocks, not much beach sand, and just ugly.* Bars/pubs: This is the must disgusting thing. There are only three bars at the resort, an ALL INCLUSIVE resort, and I will discuss each of them separately to send the message clear of what's wrong with this resort.- Pool bar: Pool bar is great, bartenders are great, drinks are great. Half of the bar is outside the pool and the other is inside (it is not very big, but nice). For some reason, at about 3 or 4PM they close the outside section of the bar, so if you are not inside the pool, the bartenders kindly tell you that you could keep ordering but by standing by the edge of the pool, screaming at the bartender, and finally bending over to get your drink; this is after having to compete with other people at the pool. I think this is outrageous. How could they just close one side of the bar when at least half the people at the pool are is outside!!! And they do this everytime, it is not that I stayed once, one day, and saw that...- Casino/Pub bar: This bar is OK. People can smoke inside and air circulation is horrible, so it stinks as bad as you could imagine. Furniture absorbs all the smoke smell, so even during the day the room stinks. Bartenders are great, they are not the problem (they are probably the only good thing - as far as service goes- the resort has), the problem is that at 1AM (or before), during the weekends, the bar is closed, as well as the lobby bar (the next in my review), so you, as a tourist in an ALL INCLUSIVE resort, have nowhere to go, but to your room??????- Lobby bar: Lobby bar is on a nice spot. Bartenders are great, as usual. The only bad thing about this bar is that they close it shorly after midnight! Yes, you're on vacation on a resort that they sold you as an ALL INCLUSIVE resort, and before 1AM you have nowhere to go besides your room. No restaurants, no gazebos with food or drinks, no bars!!! They even shut down the lights and the fans at the LOBBY!!!!!!!!!!! Could you, for just a second, imagine this!!!??? You can't even keep talking to your friends, wife, or whoever you met that day, because they shut down the lobby, the only thing left open in this All Inclusive resort??? These people want to save it all! The funniest thing is, and this is true, if you ask for leaving the bar open, or for at least get a couple of beers out, they kindly tell you that you could order beers guess where?, yes!, from your room!!, and they limit the amount of beers you could order. It's so pathetic you have to laugh.With all I have told you, it would be hard to believe that the hotel is paying for a woman to sing every night by the lobby bar, but they do, only that she thinks that she is singing to her mirror because she is just only singing for her pleasure; she does not ever connect with the people around. She has a great voice, and surely has the talent to entertain the people better, but what she is doing now is just a show for herself; she even sang the Titanic song the last time I went... With the stinky casino/pub bar as the other option, I have had to stay at the lobby bar at night and listen to the most annoying singer I've ever watched in my entire life. When she sings salsa or merengue, there's only a few people dancing, and the only could be her. I've been to the Paradisus in Dominican Republic, and the singer(s) over there put a show that has the entire lobby dancing all night long!, and what do they play?, salsa and merengue!, and bachata too!To finish, I know Puerto Rico very well and there are many other places to stay which are far prettier, better, and funnier. There are hotels of all types in all metropolitan areas (San Juan, Ponce, Mayaguez), and Paradores (BBs) on most towns, where you don't have to be stuck in an all-inclusive resort that does not allow you to eat what you want, when you want, and tells you when to go to sleep. In summary, think well before making your decision to come to this hotel, and consider other options if you want to visit the Island (check tripadvisor.com for reviews of other places).

The waiter asked me to hold my fork as he removed my salad dish as I would need the fork for the entree. We are 5 Star but please hold on to your only fork. As there was no Break Plate my only option was to hold on to the fork or to place it on the table. At least it gave me time to not pay attention to the Romper Room going on around me.Dinner on Day two was going to be at the Mirador Grill. We got to the grill but it was closed due to rain. When I checked with Royal Service I was told it was moved to Toscano and I should have been informend. I eventually found out that they had left a message for me but the light on the phone was not working.... 5 Star. The room was acceptable but by no means was it luxurious. The Jacuzzi was in fact a single jacuzzi tub that you would have in your home bathroom. I was very suprised by it as I expected it to be more of a two person Hot Tub. For some reason sitting in a single bathtub was not what i was envisioning when I booked the suite. I brought 5 movies that I had wanted to see for the past year but never could find time for and was told that the hotel could not provide a DVD player as it violated the contract with their in room Movie providor. The in room moview were $20.99 each and they were not the ones I wanted to see. I brought my favorite CD's to listen to but was told the they could not provide a CD player. As most hotels have CD players as part of the radio it never occured to me to bring my own. 5 Star. Royal Sevice Check in was a lengthy process and my room was not ready until 45 minutes after arriving. At 4pm when I did get my room key the housekeeper was still in the room cleaning. I waited on the Balcony for 15 minutes while she finished.I thought the staff was very very friendly and listened sympathically to my requests for a DVD or CD player. I even asked the one Royal Service person if someone could buy a TV and DVD player at a local store and I would pay for it but they never got back to me. It was beautiful, Serivce was incredible, Food was delicious, my Casitia overlooked the Sea and the Balcony was huge. If you have children Paradisus is a perfect place for your family. Lots of food, and very kid friendly. If you want a quiet weeks vacation go somewhere else. The royal service pool was the only place that was kid free. I heard that Romatico restaurant was kid free but never had the oppurtuninty to try it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Even with a few minor issues, we loved it! Like many others, after reading the negative reviews, I thought we were about to waste a whole lot of money and time on this resort, but not the case! I am 7 months pregnant and my husband and I wanted to take a last relaxing trip before I couldn't fly anymore and the Paradisius was a perfect spot for it. First, for anyone who's been pregnant, you can appreciate how important it is to have access to food at any time of day. And the huge pool provided plenty of exercise just swimming from one side to the other. It seems like all of the other reviews during the time we were there were all positive, and I think the main reason was because the resort was empty! The pool chairs and awesome little Bali huts were easy to get at any time during the day, check-in/out was a breeze, restaurants were fairly empty, and there were few enough people that we kept seeing the same people and met some very nice couples. I HIGHLY recommend going in off season and trying to hit a time where there are no conventions there - we were very aware of how different it would have been if there ware large and rowdy groups there. Even when people came in for the weekend, it started to get a bit more crowded and less peaceful (we stayed from Sun-Thurs, which was perfect).There were many families with small children and I was surprised at how well suited it seemed to be to them too.Food: We loved breakfast and lunch at the Carabeno and didn't bother going anywhere else. Great healthy salad bar and fruit options. If you don't like healthy food though, you probably won't be as happy - hot food wasn't all that good. But because it was so damn hot out, we loved all the fresh fruit and vegetable options. As for dinner, they can definitely use some help with the reservation service. The process is just screwy, but we were satisfied with all of our meals. And actually started asking for 9-9:30 reservations as it gave us plenty of time to nap/relax after the pool. We avoided the Mirador buffet as it didn't look all that appetizing.We did have an issue with the Concierge making some reservations for us, but turns out they were un/mis-informed so we weren't able to get to Vieques, which was our goal. They were supposed to send us to the Tour Desk to make any reservations (which we didn't even know existed). So just make sure to double-check plans and reservations and make sure you're working with the right people.All in all, we had a wonderful, relaxing stay, found the grounds and the rooms extremely comfortable and elegant (the lobby area is to die for), and the staff friendly, if occasionally underinformed. Provided you're not going when the place is packed, we would highly recommend the Paradisius.
