<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice grounds, high price includes Bed Bugs! This was easily the most expensive hotel I've ever stayed at, but I figured I would pamper myself for a few days. My vacation started off great. I thought this place was incredible. Compared to the Caribe Hilton, Paradisus was paradise. The grounds were beautifully maintained, gorgeous landscaping, huge pool, secluded beach (although no swimming or snorkling because of shallow rocky waters), nice rooms, friendly staff, nice bars and entertainment, and great plantation like relaxation areas. The food varied - breakfasts and lunches at Mirador were OK. Decent selection, certainly edible. The birds flying around the food and eating off people's plates when they got up to get drinks was a little gross, but tolerable. I ate dinner two nights at Avocado and one at Toscano. I was impressed. It was much better than I expected based on the reviews I read. I thought I was in heaven.However, I woke up after my second night with three dozen welts covering my arms and legs. I did not recall receiving one bug bite when I was awake. I remembered reading that bed bugs are an increasingly common problem. After a little internet research, I found out that the bites fit the classic pattern of bed bugs. When I complained to management, they sent a maid to the room who spent 30 seconds scanning the bed in the middle of the day and concluded that there were no bed bugs. I have NO DOUBT these were bed bug bites. What had been a great vacation was ruined! I felt extremely self conscious going out to the pool area covered in itchy welts which still, one week later, have not gone away. Try sleeping knowing that there are blood sucking bugs waiting to come out! I know these things can happen in even the poshest hotels. That's fine. What bothered me was management's response. They completely blew me off, did not apologize whatsoever, and refused to even refund a single dollar. When you are spending hundreds of dollars a night to be in paradise, you expect to be treated better!Paradisus was OK, but not worth the $. If you go, bring some potent bug spray and long sleeve sleeping attire.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Buyer beware I've stayed at numerous resorts with my family (wife and two kids) in Caribbean locations and have never felt the need to write a review on a resort. I read reviews on the Paradisus prior to going in April and was alarmed at some of the comments. I did my best to put them aside and hoped for the best. Having just returned back, I must say that I felt a sense of disappointment and that many of the comments were accurate. The facility is beautiful. It is clean, well kept up and I would consider it to be top notch. They have beautiful restaurants, a great huge pool, a fantastic gym and spa, etc. Now to the important stuff. When I first arrived, I wasn't used to waiting 15 minutes on a line waiting to check in. The check-in and check-out lines are all one and are short staffed. You have to wait on the same line to ask simple questions as well.My biggest complaints are with getting restaurant reservations and the quality of the food. Regarding reservations, they are hard to come by at the three a-la-cart restaurants. You have to constantly complain to management in order to get a seating. Their best restaurant, Bamboo, was initially offered to us on our last night at 9:45pm, much too late for kids. For the remaining three nights, it was suggested that we try one of the three buffet-style restaurants. We would never have chosen the resort if told this in advance of booking the trip. The core of the problem lies with them being the only all-inclusive restaurant on the island. Waiters, bartenders, etc. do not want to work there because they can make more income at resorts where tipping is allowed. This causes a shortage of staff and results in a limited numbers of seatings per hour. We were quite surprised to see the restaurant half full when told they were solidly booked. However, they can't accommodate all of the resort's guests in these three restaurants.As far as the buffet-styled restaurants are concerned, the food was mediocre at best. It tasted as if it was prepared much earlier in the day and sat in warming trays for hours. It didn't taste fresh and I had situations where portions were hot and the rest at room temperature. The a la cart restaurants were between 3 and 4 stars (good for an all-inclusive resort) and the buffet-styled restaurants were two stars -- at best. I would also say that the Paridisus doesn't have the most family friendly environment. Daily, there seemed to be very lively crew who took over the pool's volleyball section and were quite loud, cursing, smoking and spilling drinks into the pool -- not to mention under the influence before noon.I would not recommend this resort to anyone. The only way it will survive is to change the management team, no longer be an all-inclusive, change the food quality, and change the name in order to develop a better reputation.

<Author>STEVENSNY
<Content>Spectular Place! My girlfriend and I had a couple of days off and decided to take a quick trip to P.R. and selected Paradisus. I am a travel agent and had not visited this property before, so I will make this review quick and from a professional standpoint to help other travelers. The resort was very empty and that was uncalled for, so we opted to walk the grounds, which were amongst the most beautiful anywhere in P.R.Being that it was fairly empty, in our two days we ran across only two other couples along the vast beach and there were less than a dozen people in any of the lounges, etc. Now, the place can accommodate tons of people, and I don't know if we would have had such a great time if it was jampacked, but we truly felt it was our own resort. ALL of the staff was very friendly and helpful. FOOD: I love to eat, but also realize that inclusives usually consist of buffets which are mediocre. The food here was no exception. Not a great selection and 1/2 of it non-descript food which I couldnt even guess what it was! So, you're not going to get deluxe dining here. ROOMSERVICE ... Not matter how slow you talk or how you THINK you gave the order, three of 3 times roomservice screwed up the orders. They always made good on it within 15-20 minutes. Long story shortened: If you are looking for a truly beautiful place with attentive service, friendly faces and total relaxation, Paradisus is wonderful. If you are into a culinary trip, this is not your place. I also didn't see too much around the resort except for some BBQ roadside places, so I would venture that compared to those, the food at this resort is better and safer! We did have a fabulous time and I would go back in a flash.

<Author>LauraPh
<Content>Loved every minute of it This was our annual springbreak vacation for me and my teenage daughter. It was everything we wanted. This was our first experience at an all-inclusive resort, so I have nothing to compare it to. I read all the reviews before we went and decided to go anyway. It was unfortunate that many people had bad experiences, but they provided us with the information we needed to make sure we did not have the same problems.One thing I think that helped was the timing of our trip. We arrived the Saturday before Easter Sunday so there were no conventions. It was all families. A couple of conventions came Thursday, but we were not bothered (although I heard that many others had their reservations changed to accomdate the convention and were very upset).Here is the breakdown of our experience:Arrival: The shuttle was waiting for us when we arrived and the driver loaded the bags. It is supposed to leave every hour on the hour, but apparently we were the only two so it left at 20 minutes after the hour. We were offered refreshments. It was a long drive, but we just sat back and enjoyed the scenery.Check-in: our bags were unloaded and we headed to the check-in. (We got to the resort at 12:20 - the official check-in is at 3:00). We waited about 10 minutes in line to check-in. The process was quick and painless and the clerk was friendly and happy to answer questions. We were told our room would not be ready until 3:00, but were shown to the hospitality room where we could change into our swim suits. We were provided with the resort wristband and told to enjoy the facilities. Our luggage was held up front for us. At 3:00 we checked to make sure our room keys were activated, grabbed our lugguage and took the trolley to our room. (we learned from previous reviews that luggage takes awhile to get to the room so we took it ourselves - no problem).Grounds: Beautiful. The palm trees, various flowers and the buildings were all beautiful. Even though our room was in the last building we walked to the pool daily just to take in the sights.Pool: Extraordinary! Even thought the resort was apparently booked full, we did not ever feel crowded in the pool. On the first day we chose two chairs with an umbrella direclty across from the pool bar. We sat there everyday! The poolside chairs and cabanas do get snatched up early. However, we are early risers so everyday we got up, got our stuff together, walked down to the pool, put our stuff on our chairs and went to eat. We were usually done with breakfast by 7:00. We never wanted a cabana (we were there for tans!) but, I think the cabana people get up at 3:00AM to out their stuff out! My daughter and I practically had the the pool to ourselves until 10:00 most mornings. Our one complaint about the pool area is that the pool bathrooms were disgusting most of the day. Yes, there should be more staff to clean, etc., but the other guests caused the mess. It is hard to believe that people pay to stay at a beautiful resort like this and leave the bathrooms the way they do. I will not provide details, but by the end of the day the bathrooms smelled like an outhouse. Poolside activities: there is an activity hut by the pool. They play fun music all day. It is probably loud if you sit near that area, we couldn't hear it where we sat so we were able to relax. We played water volleyball and basketball, participated in the daily dance lessons, water aerobics, bingo, and pingpong. My daugher played beach voleyball. There was a ton more to do. The staff at the activity hut is amazing! Upbeat and energetic ALL the time. The dance lessons were surperb! Bars: all bars were great with excellent service. Liquor was top notch and they were not stingy. They knew how to make all types of drinks.Food: Breakfast and lunch were always buffet. Mirador and Caribeno were usually open at the same time although Caribeno was closed for a couple of days during the week. Caribeno is the place to eat breakfast and lunch if you have the choice. The breakfast is hotter and the fresh fruit selection is outstanding. Lunch always has an amazing salad bar. Service is fantastic. Mirador is so-so, food is not hot, there are birds flying around and service is lacking. The ONLY non-friendly person we found at the whole resort was the hostess at the Mirador.We had no problems at all getting reservations at all thesit-down restaurants. We went to the concierge the day we checked in. All of our meals were amazing at Bamboo, Avocado and Romantico. Reservations are also needed for the buffets at night. Maridor did surprise us with their evening meal and show... it was great. surprisingly, our least favorite was the Italian buffet at Tuscano. Service was good, but food was bland and oily.Rooms: really nice and cool. The maids did a great job everyday.Beach/Watersports: we went kayaking and paddle boating. It was fanatastic - I nice was to truely see how beatiful the water is. The beach is not good for swimming becuase of the seawead growth and it makes the water look brown. However, the water is crystal clear and wonderful. If you take time to paddle down the beach (or walk) you will find quiet little spots with nice areas to take a dip. Even on the busiest of days there were NO people at some of the most beautiful spots on the resort.Bottom line: we loved every minute of it and did not want to leave. We were treated like queens for a week.

<Author>cmarkell
<Content>Not Quite Up To Par I was at Paradisus Puerto Rico with my wife and two children for six days beginning April 13th. The resort is beautiful, but falls short in many ways. Immediately after check-in, we went to make our reservations at the restaurants. We were told all the full service restaurants were booked for the rest of the week and could only eat in the buffet style restaurants. What a way to start the vacation having to argue with this person and demand to see the manager. We eventually did get the bookings we wanted. What surprised me was that these fully booked restaurants were only 75% full when I was there. It became apparent that the hotel staff are instructed to push as many guests to the buffets instead of the full service restaurants. They'd rather you eat at the buffet because it costs them less. You won't find lambchops, sirloin steak or fresh fish at the buffets. You'll only find these at the full service restaurants. Additionally, just about any hot dish I had at the buffet was never hot. It sits there in a large metal tray on steaming water. This does not keep the food hot. It barely keeps it warm. The overall service from the waiters is shameful. Some try hard, but there's not enough to attend to the guests. I had to wait 30 minutes to get a cup of tea... 20 minutes to order a second drink. Need a spoon, forget about it... help yourself if you can. Overall, the place is beautiful, has plenty of activities, but the food situation, and overall service is hit or miss. One day my room was not even cleaned by the maid. Even after calling the front desk, nobody was sent. At 10pm after going to the front desk, someone was sent. They compensated us with a free massage. In speaking with other guests, I heard many similar complaints. I did enjoy my stay at the Paradisus, but should not have to have dealt with these problems for what I paid. I will not be returning anytime soon.

<Author>rqf
<Content>A pleasant five days REVIEW - PARADISUS PUERTO RICOI recently returned from a trip to this resort. I was at the resort from March 23 to March 27.GETTING TO/FROM THE RESORT - The hotel runs a shuttle bus from the airport to the resort and from the resort to the airport. The charge is $30 per person each way. It leaves every hour on the hour and the trip takes close to an hour. Shuttle is a modern air conditioned vehicle that can take at least 25 people. The hotel has a representative at the baggage retrieval area at the airport. The representative will escort you to the bus. He will give you a receipt and you will be told to save the receipt as it will be needed when you board the bus for the return to the airport. This system is well organized .ChecK IN - It was a relatively slow process but not because of inefficiency. People have questions and this is time consumingRESORT GROUNDS - Truly beautiful. It is, in effect, a botanical garden. On a scale of 1 to 10 this is definitely a 10.RESTAURANTS - There are six restaurants, three serve buffet style and three are sit and be served and these are open for dinner only. For these you must make a reservation and that poses a problem since there is no way the resort can accommodate all guests on a given day. I was told the three restaurants can only serve 400 people a day. For a hotel with a capacity of more than 1000 lots of people can not get reservations and that makes for a lot of unhappy campers. That issue is the source of most of the complaints made and rightfully so. FOOD - The buffets are open for breakfast, lunch and dinner. The buffets were adequate but not as good as the buffets you find on most cruise ships or at other hotels. The ambiance at the sit down restaurants was very good at all three but the quality of the food varied. The best was the Japanese restaurant. The other two can鈥檛 be rated much better than Fair. The service at all three was very good. POOL - The pool is large and there appears to be enough lounges for all. There are a number of huts that have thatched roofs and are open on all four sides that are available if you want to get out of the sun. Unless you get to the pool early you won鈥檛 find any vacant huts. There are about 20 of these placed around the pool. Other than the huts there is very little shade in the pool area. BEACH - This beach may be one of the worst in Puerto Rico. The beach is a narrow strip (15 to 20 feet at most) with poor quality sand and plenty of small rocks and pebbles that make walking, barefoot, painful. Further you have to go through sea grass to get out to where you can swim. I never saw more than four or five people swimming in the ocean at any given time. This is not the place to go if you want to swim in the ocean and refuse to go into a pool. They do have kayaks and paddle boats for guests. There is no charge for using this equipment. . ROOMS - The rooms are located in two story bungalows. The rooms are large, clean and well appointed. Each room has either two double beds or a king size bed. There is a sitting area with a sofa. Every room has a coffee maker and a refrigerator stocked with bottled water and cans of soda. You can get beer if requested. Each room has a terrace. A shuttle that operates all day is available to take you from your room to the lobby. There is a safe in the room and an ironing board but no ironROOM SERVICE - Room service is available 24 hours a day. There is a $3 charge each time you order from room service. I used room service once. It took 35 minutes from the time I ordered to the time it was delivered. I didn鈥檛 find that to be an excessive wait since the kitchen is located a fair distance from the rooms. SERVICE - General service was good. All those workers I can in contact with were very pleasant and it was apparent they wanted to be of service if needed. ENTERTAINMENT - There was a show every night that featured dancing. The same performers appeared every night. The shows were entertaining CONCLUSION - On the whole it was a pleasant, restful experience. I am not a finicky eater so someone more discriminating would probably take issue with the food served. I went there because the price was right. I would go back again should I get a good price.

<Author>luv2go2PR
<Content>We had the best time ever We stayed at the PARADISUS-PUERTO RICO for 8 days and I absolutely loved it! I was SCARED TO DEATH to go because of the previous negative reviews, but was pleasantly surprised when all the things we feared were NO PROBLEM at all. CHECK IN was a breeze. Everyone was courteous and happy to help us. When I got to the room I asked for extra towels,pillows and even an extra coffee maker for tea,and not only did I get them, but I was CALLED BACK to MAKE SURE I got them. I accidently left the keys to my suitcase home and they sent an engineer to open it, and also called to make sure that he arrived. They couldn't do enough to make our stay the best it could be. I didn't have the ROYAL SERVICE nor did I need it. I also got a wonderful rate and did not pay anything NEAR to $600/day people write about. The value I recieved was incredible. If you want to know who I booked with E-mail me. We did research before we left and knew it was going to rain so we rented a car so we would be able to shop or travel. We did do some sight seeing and shopping and it is not neccesary to have a rental car but when you can get one for less than $30 a day, why not splurge? We use Charlies whenever we are on the island. The Concierge, DAISY, who gave out dinner reservations was warm and sincere. We ate at all 6 restaurants and enjoyed them immensly. The best were the BAMBOO(the Japanese,) the AVOCADO(the Steak house,)and the ROMANTICO(French cuisine.) The service in these 3 restaurants was impeccable. The problem with the outside buffet, THE MIRADOR was being fixed the first few days we were there. They put up netting to keep away the birds. It opened on the weekend and the views of the ocean were incredible. The other 2 buffets were average but there was always plenty to eat and the food was fresh and plentiful. A few times I complained and when I brought it to their attention that something was missing they were very anxious to know of their shortcomings and take them into consideration because what they explained was that much of the staff were new and just learning the routine. AS part of a large corporation (Sol Melia) they want this property to be just as good or even better that the rest of their properties, all over the world. I ordered room service 3 times and they arrived in less than 30 minutes. The management is really taking these reviews into consideration and trying their very hardest to improve. The grounds are exquisite and I saw them spraying to keep insects away. The beach is very beautiful despite the rocks and vegetation. We took the Catamaran ride and used the kayaks and pedal boats. The staff at the pool keeps you busy with water aerobics, stretching and salsa lessons. We sat on the grassy area in between the pool and the sand and got beautiful ocean breezes. Make sure to bring 30 plus sunscreen. I am an avid sun worshipper and even I, got burned to a crisp! The drinks were plentiful and delicious. Get out to the pool early to reserve a good seat and if you want the shaded huts I think you have to get there at sunrise. I was never able to get one until the end of the day when someone left and it was worth the wait. The shows after dinner were very enjoyable and the dancers were talented as well as beautiful and handsome. There is a singer who comes on before and after the show and then a disco that opens at around 11p. It is true that locals can come in for a fee and either stay the day, have dinner or even stay the night. The only problem with the locals is that they are cliquey and stay only with each other. The casino IS TINY but a few people we met said they won there and had a great time. I am sure if you want casino action you can go to El Conquistador or El San Juan. I was too tired after being out in the sun and water all day to worry about what I needed to do at night. I am not a golfer but I heard from a few that the golf course is OK. He said Just OK. The trolleys that take you to your room are making constant rounds. Just start to walk and soon enough one will arrive for you to flag down. The safe is the room is free of charge and the cards for the towels are no problem at all. No shortage of towels and a few times we left the safe open and nothing was missing at all. By the way, I needed milk before bed time and my finacee had no problem at all getting it in the restaurants. To me it seems that what ever you want you can get, just ask for it and they are very eager to satisfy you. Please write to me if you have any questions. I would go back there in a snap. The only set back was the beach but we went to Luqillo Beach on the day we arrived. I am not really a beach person anyway. Oh! one last thing. Although the Paradisus is beautiful, do not get the idea that The Paradisus IS Puerto Rico. There is so much to see and do in Puerto Rico. You need to go to Puerto Rico a few times(at least) to see all the beauty and culture that this magnificent Island has to offer.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Stop complaining and enjoy I just returned from 4 days at the paradisus with my girlfriend and it is exactly what we wanted. We arrived to a beautiful hotel with helpful staff. I have read plenty of people complain that it took hours to have their bags delivered to their room, we were able to sidestep that problem by taking our own bags a whopping 5 minute walk to our room. The rooms were huge and fantastic with a great terrace. We heard people complain that there were not enough activities at the resort, but we wanted somehwere where we could sit by the pool and not be bothered. If you want someone to constantly entertain you, then this is not the place for you, but if you are looking to relax then it is perfect. Another complaint I have read is about the food. We had one bad meal over the course of 4 days. The reservation process is not a difficult one. Each day we went to the pool in the morning and stopped by the concierge to make a reservation for that night. If you do that there will be no problems. The only thing I would watch for is the Roulette dealers. They seemed to have a little difficulty counting the correct number of chips.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disorganized and disappointing My wife and I just returned from Puerto Rico. The company I work for flew us to the Paradisus for a corporate escape. The hotel is beautiful but unfortunately several things made the trip somewhat disappointing.1. A representative from the hotel did not meet us at the airport right away. We had to find our way to the pickup spot which was on a lower level of the airport. Unfortunately we had to carry our luggage down a set of stairs to get there. The buses took some time to arrive and when they did, several porters arranged our luggage while we were allowed to board. We were then counted and away we went.2. We arrived at the hotel around 1:30 PM. The porters unloaded our luggage in the lobby and started labelling them with the name of our company. The hotel representative told us our luggage would be transported to our rooms shortly.3. The staff greeted us nicely and wrapped an all inclusive band around our wrists. They told us our room was not ready but that they had a little snack waiting for us in the main lobby. We also had access to the bar while we waited. The first estimate they gave us was about an hour. This was bearable as our vacation was paid for by my company. However, when the hour passed their next estimate was 3:00 PM. The front desk manager told us, we are working with housekeeping to have your rooms ready but we have been running into delays due to some guests that have checked out late. This seemed somewhat reasonable since our group included about 400 people and the hotel only had 500 rooms. We kept drinking and checked back at 3PM. Still a no go and the manager was singing the same tune. My wife started to get irritated as she also works in the hotel industry. She argued with the manager that our rooms should have already been prebooked and arranged. The manager recanted her earlier statement like a script in her head. She suggested that we could use their hospitality suite to change so that we could go to the beach. She told us to go check with the concierge to find our luggage.4. We asked the concierge for our luggage. He pulled out a clipboard, found our names and told us our luggage had been transported to our room. He also told us that our room was ready.5. We went back to the front desk to get our room key. The front desk agent told us our room was still not ready and was being cleaned by housekeeping. We told her that the concierge had indicated our room was ready and that he had transported our luggage there. She replied, he has no right to tell you anything like that. I'm sorry, but your room is not ready yet. Luckily the hotel representative that had met us at the airport spotted us at the front desk - my wife was getting very frustrated. Magically, he handed us our room keys. The front desk agent looked dumbfounded.6. Happily we went to our room. When we go there, a musty smell pervaded the place. My wife used the word moldy to describe it. However, since it was 4 PM and we didn't want to wait or complain anymore, we changed and went to the beach.7. Although the manicured grounds of the hotel were beautiful and the pool well kept, the beach left something to be desired. Patches of seaweed blocked access to the waves and the sand was hard and spotty with pebbles. Also, an anonymous guest told us that they had spotted jelly fish which really turned us off. We went back to the pool to enjoy what remained of the day.8. Two restaurants offered a buffet breakfast - the Mirador Grill and the Avocado. The Grill offered scrambled eggs, bacon, hash browns, fruits, yogurt and several types of bread. Overall not particularly fantastic but edible. The Avocado added freshly made omelets to the array.9. Lunch and Dinner were very similar buffets at both places often repeating left overs from the previous day. The selection of sea food was excellent including shrimp, snapper, mussels, etc.10. The hotel also included plate service once per week by reservation only. The Avocado, the Mirador Grill, Romantico, etc. all had different themes. The food and the service was excellent. However, the bus staff were fairly inexperienced and had to be reminded to get water and coffee. 11. Nightly entertainment was subpar. A lounge singer churned out popular tunes in karaoke style with the assistance of a piano player and track sequencer. My wife commented that the entertainment was for seniors only - not suitable for anyone between 18 and 35.12. The hotel also featured nightly live performances with different themes. Only two of the ten performers were near professional quality. The rest seemed to be in learning mode, often out of sync with each other.13. The Casino was small and had few tables open simultaneously. Caribbean stud did not include a progressive or big jackpot.Overall, though, everyone was friendly and we had a decent time. I believe this place has a lot of potential. The staff needs training and the daily activities need development. Also, something has to be done about the beach.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>not a four star positives: great pools, rooms (on 2nd floor) , nice people, property, good location (near to San Juan and El Yunke rainforest), excellent Bar in main lobby.Negatives:Poor management, Short staffed, Tardy room service(if you order in meals), Beach (scary for kids ), Restaurants, no first aid kit at pools and only one lifeguard. No signs at the pools either (eg: no diving etc).We travelled with two kids (3 and 10) so we enjoyed the pool . The rooms were wonderful on the 2nd floor of two storied bunglows. We opted for royal service where a butler is assigned to you. Ours was great ( a tip does help) . Reservations are needed at the restaurants well in advance so please book them as soon as you arrive . There is one operating buffet where the food is okay but one gets tired of it after two days...there is an italian buffet which only operates on weekends.The other restaurants are reservations only. Nothing spectacular. There are tours availabel to various spots in PR and AVIS has a desk there but were out of cars. We rented one from nearby arranged by our butler and we visited San Juan and ElYunke rain forest ( avoid rushours between 2pm to 8pm) . Room service is a disaster if you order food in..ours took hour and half first time and 45 mins second time. Book your transport from airport and back before you arrive in PR by calling the hotel. Last day I fell into pool and was injured in my back by concrete stools near bar area in the pool. There was no first aid available. The security staff would call a doctor however that will cost you $150.00. In my case I opted for ambulance however they arrived after 20mins. So please carry first aid kit.The locals come in on weekends and there are local business events. Lobby is beautiful and Royal service lounge will spoil you.Overall we had a good time however I would rate this hotel a three and half star.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful and Relaxing My mother and I went to the Paradisus to celebrate our 40th and 60th birthdays. Great Facilities: We could not have asked for a more beautiful resort to stay in. Everything about the resort's grounds was first class. The best was the catamaran and snorkeling trip on the Traveler. You can book this at the hotel for about $70 per person and I recommend it.If you are looking for alot of action at night, I do not recommend this place. There are no bars close by and the night life at the Pardiadisus is mild. (One couple in thier 20's told me they spent $140 round trip for a cab to San Juan one night so they could party in the bars there.)Food:The drinks were plentiful, strong and filled with a smile. The food was good enough, but the staffing for the full service restaurants seem to be a problem. It took us three days to get a reservation before 9:00 p.m. and were dissappointed to see that they were only seating one third of the restaurant. A word to the wise--be prepared to eat at the buffets or eat late.Summary:This resort would be perfect for a relaxing vacation if they hired some more employees.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Relaxed and enjoyed the Paradisus We were apprehensive after reading the reviews. Our concerns were put to rest shortly after arriving. The staff who checked us in were friendly and warm. The lobby area is beautiful. Our room was very far away, but we enjoy walking and there were always golf carts available to drive you if you don't wish to walk. Our room was beautiful, an ocean view jr. suite. It was clean and comfortable. There was a bit of a musty smell, but that seems to be unavoidable in the Caribbean. The only challenge we encountered was in securing dinner reservations in the restaurants. The hotel needs to devise a better system. We were not allowed to make reservations before we arrived and when we arrived, the concierge was taking a lunch break. With some negotiation we were able to get reservations for each night we were there. (This was not the experience of most other guests we spoke to.) Oddly, each evening when we ate, approximately half of the tables were empty. This was odd because so many of the guests we spoke to told us they were not able to get reservations. I would rank the quality of the food as average to above-average. The servers and management were friendly and provided good service. Most of the hostesses, especially at the breakfast and lunch buffets were not very friendly or efficient. The pool area is beautiful and clean. There is plenty of room and plently of areas that you can sit if you prefer quiet to people watching and interacting. The bartenders were efficient and friendly. The beach is not ideal for swimming, but is beautiful and great for a walk. We enjoyed sitting on the grassy area overlooking the water and walking along the beach. We swam despite the rocks and seaweed and enjoyed ourselves. The spa was lovely and relaxing and we enjoyed massages. The hot tub and pool areas were very nice and virtually empty when we visited.  If you are looking for a five-star resort where your every whim is satisfied, you will be disappointed. However, if you are happy staying in a beautiful and clean resort with stunning views where you may have to negotiate for what you want, you will enjoy this resort. I will return if they offer a great rate again in the future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disappointment in Paradise We just returned from four days at the Paradisus, and we will not return. There are not many resorts as beautiful as this one, but there are many areas in need of improvement. The climate is wonderful, and the landscaping is well designed. Rooms are spacious and very clean. The pools offer everything one wants, but the beach is one area that does not encourage visitors. Housekeeping needs improvement. Often they do not get to your room until very late in the afternoon or early evening. There were no washcloths or hand towels after the first day. Repeated requests for these items were ignored. Room service was terrible; service was slow, trays were not picked up for days, and the food was poor. The restaurants were not open in the evening, and you were told there were no available reservations when you called. The only meals available were buffets in two restaurants. Food that was to be hot was barely warm, and the buffet tables were not refilled very often. You need to get there early to get any food. Casino is small, and you might want to forget the gift shop. The spa was excellent, and the staff professional. Perhaps Paradisus has a lot of problems because it is only a few years old.

If you can afford the few extra dollars, go for the Royal Service. Oh, and if you gon with your best friends thats a real plus! And make sure you try the Flan at the desert table!!!

<Author>Timmic
<Content>Much better than expected...I'd go back for the right price! My husband  I just returned from 5 days at the Paradisus and we were definitely not disappointed! We have done numerous all-inclusives through Apple Vacations and I would rate this resort a 5 Apple for appearance and a 4 Apple for food. The grounds were beautiful and the rooms large and clean -- it's probably the first time I did not try to change rooms. Yes, they have the same musty smell that many places in the Caribbean have -- some incense and scented candles cured that. I brought a can of Raid but did not see even ONE bug in our room. I normally hate first floor rooms for the privacy factor, but there is so much landscape between the room and walkway, no one was walking right past our room. We were with a very large group - 350 to 400 people - and I agree that large groups do get better service. No one I knew got any bug bites, yet I met a woman who had at least 100 bites on her legs - go figure! Food - typical all inclusive food but not at the standard you would expect for the price. I've eaten at a Secrets Resort and their food is up to par for the price you pay. We ate at Romantico and Avocado - enjoyed them both. I would avoid the outdoor restaurant as the birds have a habit of flying in and eating off the buffet along with you. The indoor breakfast/lunch buffets were fine. Plenty of fresh fruit, bagels, pastries, salad, etc along with fresh made omelettes. We had terrible luck with room service, yet another couple with us had great service. It's a lot of hit or miss so I would say their biggest problem is inconsistency. The Italian buffet was good -- pick your pasta, sauce, and additionals (mushrooms, shrimp, etc) and they make it fresh and hot.They are far from everything so I would consider renting a car if you are going for a week or more. We were there for 3 full days and did excursions for 2 of them but another couple had a car and said it was no problem driving there.Having done enough all-inclusive vacation packages through Apple (Playa del Carmen, Antigua, Punta Cana, Hualtuco, Ixtapa, etc), I would say this would be worth about $1200-$1500 from Chicago for one week including airfare and all taxes. I can totally understand the poor reviews for those that paid for it. Definitely not worth the money they charge, but totally worth it for the right price. My husband and I would go back in a heartbeat if the price was within our range and we would rent a car for a couple days. The pool was beautiful and we never had a problem getting chairs. I don't agree with the towel card thing so I'd suggest bringing your own. Not worth the money if someone else accidently takes yours.The grounds are large so if you're going with other people I'd suggest bringing a set of walkie-talkies.(Don't forget extra batteries!) If you are going on a company trip, you will probably enjoy it more. Either way, relax and enjoy it.I'm usually only on Trip Advisor when planning a trip and since I don't have any more coming up, please feel free to contact me directly at timmic0516@comcast.net if you have any questions.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Paradise at Paradisus We stayed at the Paradisus hotel the week of January 22nd, and found it to be a very rewarding and relaxing experience. The hotel staff was accomdating and friendly, and the service was good throughout. We were thoroughly happy with the hotel. The horizontal layout of the hotel is a bit sprawling, but taxi service is provided to vacationers' bungaloes, and this service is more than adequate as waiting is kept to a minimum. The food is excellent across the board, be it breakfast, lunch or dinner, and the selections are varied. There are several different types of restaurants for discriminating tastes, including oriental, italian, and continental. We preferred the buffets, and the Italian restaurant was particularly good. The pool is vast and winding, and interestingly contoured. The scenery at poolside along the ocean is a thing of beauty, and comfortably laid out. The only problem we had is that we found that we had quite a few mosquitoe bites when we arrived home, so we would recommend protection. As for tours, we enjoyed the rainforest and its myriad types of birds, insects, vegetation and plants. However, our favorite jaunt was to the fortress at El Morro fronting the town of Od San Juan. The fortress was constructed in the mid 1500s to repel invaders, and you can almost feel the battles while walking through this massive, multi-storied structure. And don't forget to take a walk through Old San Juan, which has character and diversity, as well as good buys for interested shoppers. All in all, we had a great time. If you like a relaxed and relatively tranquil vacation, the Paradisus is ideal, as it is tucked away on a remote peninsula, away from the maddening crowd.

<Author>Rachael-Dublin
<Content>Would not recommend! (particularly for couples) We stayed at the Paradissus from 26-30 December 2005. I have never written a hotel review before but feel I have to in this case. We stay in 5 star hotels around the world and usually spend Christmas in one in Mauritius. We are a young couple and joined family there for three nights. The location is nice except it is very far from any town etc. if you wanted to try and escape to a local restaurant. The rooms were fine, large but not luxurious as one would normally expect with a five star. We were paying $1000 a night and for that it was a very average room. The (free) mini bar only contained water and soft drinks. While the water was welcome we would prefer a full bar and the option to decide paying for a bottle of wine. Our first introduction to the hotel was at a slow check in where we were told we would have to wear a wrist band for our stay and given cards which would allow us to get a pool towel each. If the pool towel was not returned at the end of each day one has to pay $30. I have never stayed in a 5 star (or any hotel for that matter) which didn't hand out towels at the pool. We felt like we were in boarding school! The next day we met the rest of our family who had already been there a week who confirmed it was really dreadful. In particular they complained about the food, the wine, the incredible system of having to queue to make restaurant reservations and the lack of a supervised childrens club. The had four children under 8 with them and the 'supervisor' just walked off one day and left them on a beach with other children. We decided to make the best of it and found the adult only pool which is part of a royal service package. For $25 each extra per day we could use it and avail of its relatively civilised atmosphere and its more relaxed towel regime - they gave you two towels! The pool staff here were very friendly and regularly brought around water etc. On the food all I can say is that it wasn't good. Breakfast was the best of the lot as there was plenty of fresh fruit. We avoided lunch after the first day. The salad bar looked as if everything had come out of tins. We ordered a bottle of wine and it came long after we had finished eating. With tips being included in staff's wages they have no incentive to be that attentive. Saying that we did meet some very pleasant staff. We tried three of the restaurants - Bamboo (ok), Avocado (bad) and Tuscana (very average pasta bar). There was loud entertainment in all three and constantly in the main bar area. The hotel is aimed towards large families with plenty of children where costs can be controlled with the all inclusive system and people aren't that interested in good food. It seemed ideal for teenage children and the main pool was full of life. It is not designed for couples at all. We were forunately only staying for three nights on a stopover before we headed on to another Caribbean island. The rest of our family checked out a week early and moved to the Ritz-Carlton in San Juan which they found very good - their main reasons for leaving being the food and the lack of fully supervised child care facilities. I am giving the hotel two stars as the spa was really magnificant. We used it every day. The massages were among some of the best we have ever had worldwide and we travel alot. The staff there were also excellent. The adjacent gym is well equipped but tiny for the number of guests in the hotel and was full at peak times. The casino was also well equipped and seemed to be well run. Finally the bugs - I should mention I got about 40 little bites in the 3 days we were there. Although I should also mention that my husband didn't get any. Safe to say that next year we are all returning to the luxury and fantastic food of Mauritius!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Just got back I too just got back from a nice holiday vacation in Puerto Rico at the Paradisus. I am surprised at a lot of the comments as we did not experience a lot of the negatives that others have experienced. Hopefully I won't bore you with the details but I will go into our entire experience there.First of all, due to research on the internet, we booked the Royal Service which was probably worth it in the long run but also the source of the few negatives we experienced. We arrived the day after Christmas around 1:00 PM (at airport) and had originally planned on taking a taxi to the resort which we figured would be faster than waiting for a shuttle at about the same price. when we got off the plane, a Paradisus representative was there waiting for other guests. We were able to take the shuttle which was $120.00 round trip. It did take an hour to get to the resort from the airport - seemed forever - but anything would have seemed forever after a 4hour plus flight from Chicago. When we got to the resort, we were asked our names as soon as we got off the shuttle and when they saw that we were 'Royal Service', we were immediately escorted to a special lounge where we were checked in. So, Royal Service saved us the longer check in at the front desk.While checking in we asked about different aspects of the resort and royal service and it was suggested that before our 'butler' (I use the term very loosely) would give us a tour of the resort and take us to our rooms that we should immediatly book our reservations for our restaurants. The butler took us to the restaurant line (one person was in front of us) and we were told that due to a computer problem and cancellations, we could only book that night and the next. I really didn't feel like coming back and while she stepped away to get a reservation book, I asked our butler about it and told him I would prefer to book our entire week. When she came back he spoke to her in spanish and lo and behold, we booked our entire week, got reasonable times (all around 7PM) and tried out almost all of the restaurants - Bamboo is the absolute best. This resulted in a nice 'extra' tip for our butler (since all tips and gratuities are included).Room -Absolutely gorgeous and no musty smell like some people have mentioned. Huge towels, robes, unbrella, mini rifrigerator stocked each night - just softdrinks water and beer. Balcony - ours looked out toward the mountain/rain forest. The four royal service buildings are very close to beech and to the main resort. And, they have there own private adults only pool around maybe 16 or so cabanas that can be reserved by the day. Do that immediately too ... the first couple days you may be on a wait list - they give them away if you don't claim them by 10AM. Basically we beached in in the AM and Cabana'd it in the PM other than the one day we took a tour of the rain forest which is absolutely phenomenal.The main pool was definitely filled with a lot of kids, but the beach was not nor was the private pool.The beach - Due to research on the internet we brought aqua socks which were a must if you wanted to use the beach as opposed to the pools. From what I understand, the beach is a 'natural' beach and can't be groomed. The beach itself and the views were fantastic. There is really two beach areas .. the first being the natural beach which is from the water to boulders that stretch out along the whole beachfron ... this beach was around 10 to 15 feet wide I would say. Then there are the boulders and behind the bolders, between the beach and the resort is what seems to be a man made beach area where a lot of people sunned and played volleyball, etc. The water is absolutely calm, as there is a sandbar maybe 200 yards out where the waves crash. The beach is rocky but with aqua socks, absolutely no problem. the other problem with the beach is the water where there is muich vegetation. However, with aqua socks and good vision (you can see where the vegetation is) you can find good places to swim and I was in the ocean every day having a ball. If we had our kids (now adults) they would have wanted some motorized fun (jet skis) but for us, it was nice and calm and beautiful. We kayaked some days we paddle boated others and just vegetated the rest. We felt no reason to take a cab to any other beach. BRING AQUA SOCKS!Restaurants and food - Breakfast and lunch were buffet - the 'outdoor restaurant was primarily for people who were at the pool and didn't want to put on shorts and shirt.. the indoor restaurants were for everyone else (including a few who didn't care to listen to the rules and came in barefoot and in swimming suit). Buffet was average. Breakfast, if you are an egg eater, have them make you fresh eggs... the scrambled in the buffet were atrocious. Also, I couldn't wait to hit O'hare airport on the way back to get a cup of coffee as there isn't a good cup in Puerto Rico! All in all, breakfast and lunch were good ... only real complaint was lack of fruit which I found surprising. Some days the fruit was out other days it wasn't. Dinner was for the most part above average. Bamboo great - this is the japanese style restaurant where 12 people sit around a table and they prepare the food in front of you. Nice way to meet people and food was great. Romantica was very good but service was slow and slower. Toscano is Italian but buffet style .. they will make whatever kind of pizza you want, or the pasta dish will be made in front of you with whatever ingrediants you want. Wasn't thrilled about a buffet for dinner but I found the food very good here. Avocado is the 'California' style restaurant and we were warned that the food sucked. We were there two nights and the first night the food was very very good - we had fish of the day and second night it was just ok. We did not try the Mexican nor the Caribbean.Royal Service - Helped us out at check in. Helped us out getting reservations to the restaurants. Didn't know where to get ice (machines are not in your building0 so we called and asked where the machines were .. they told us not to worry , that was part of royal service - they would bring us ice. 45 minutes later - no ice. called again... 45 minutes later we left for dinner, still no ice ... never got it. Next day called again ... no ice... called agian and was promised it in 15 minutes... 30 minutes later got a phone call making sure we got it and told them no. finally two differentpeople came with ice. They have robes in the room and if you want to buy one you call and they will send over a new one. On New Years eve, our last night, I decided that I would get one as a souvenier. Called thenumber and no answer. Went to dinner and stopped at royal service lounge .. they told me they would have one sent to room. Never got it... wasn't billed for it either. (By the way - check the tv account summary every now and then ... they charged me $400 by mistake and corrected it by crediting me $300.00. I didn't like their math and called - no problem getting it corrected. Part of royal service was getting a daily newspaper .. despite calls and a personal visit to royal service lounge, I never got it. New Years eve we called and told them what time we needed them to come get our luggage and take it to the shuttle (5:45 AM for a 6AM shuttle) and no one showedup. Finally after two calls, someone came. Neither did the shuttle. Finally at 6:30 they were able to scrounge one up for us and the other family going to the airport. By the way, return trip to airport on New Years day at 6:30 AM was only 30 minutes - no traffic.So, royal service was for the most part frustrating whenever we had to rely on someone to do something.Casino - Yes it is small - but dealers are very friendly and this was our entertainment. Basically the table games they had were roulette, caribbean stud, three card poker, several blackjack tables, late at night they opened a texas holdem table and then there were slots. We knew ging in it was a small casino and didn't have a problem with it although I would have loved it if they had a craps table. Entertainment - Lounge as nice in early evening - a duet with a piano player and a singer. Later a band that could get quite loud. And each night at 10:00 entertainment in the ballroom. We go on a loto f cruises and love going to the shows. We went the second night and lasted 20 minutes... never went back. If you are going for the entertainment - this is not the place to go.All in all, we had an absolutely fantastic time ending with the champaign and fireworks they provided for New Years. Would we go back - in a second. I would get royal service again but knowing now how they act, would stay on them a lot more about getting what I paid for. I would also book another excursion because I was getting antsy by the end. I am not used to totally vegetating and would haveliked another getaway.I forgot about the spa/gym. I can't tell you about the spa, but tthey had a very nice gym which was very busy. Around 6 treadmills, one eliptical, about three exer4ciswe bikes and a lot of weight machines. I should have used the gym more than I did because it definitely wasn't a break even in terms of working out and relaxing with a rum drink - but what the heck - it was vacation!!I have listed my email address and would be glad to answer any questions regarding my experience. Happy New Year!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice sized rooms, but ............ All-inclusives usually are a red flag for me, so our family went to the Paradisus with low expectations. Check-in was painless, and our luggage was delivered to our rooms promptly. We were pleasantly surprised at the nice sized rooms, not royal service but we were an upper floor which I think have larger rooms. It was warm  humid late in November in Puerto Rico, and maybe it's always humid here since the rooms have a slightly moldy smell. All the surfaces  fabrics felt a little sticky  damp from all the moisture in the air. The shower/tub in our room had a slow drain, meaning by the time you got finished with a 10 minute shower you were standing in a foot of water and after you got dressed left the bathroom 5 minutes later the tub still had not drained yet. This problem was made somewhat somewhat better after we complained, instead of 12 inches of water you stood in 2 inches of water.We were a large group so all of our dinner reservations were made months in advance. Bamboo, the japanese hibachi style restaurant was decent. Very limited menu. Toscano - is as horrible as everyone else says it is. Italian buffet without even one decent italian dish. Only edible food item here was the cookies  cream ice cream which - thank goodness came ready to eat from Breyer's. The service was the worst here. Avocado buffets for breakfast  lunch were good bets. Did not have dinner here, but I think it's always buffet style regardless of the meal. Romantico has an ambitious menu, and the menu descriptions raise your expectations for the food. The food was decent but certainly does not deserve a rating much above Bamboo. Ask about the policy for young children at Romantico, this restautant is supposed to be Paradisus' premiere dining place so they discourage very young children from eating there. Most alcoholic beverages are included in the stay rate, but there are premium liquors  wines that can be obtained for an extra cost. I personally did not eat at the Mirador Grill buffet by the pool, the children in our group were ok with it since they had burgers, but the adults in our group catergorized the food at the grill as slop.Silly one towel per guest policy at the pool, and you had to remember to bring your towel card with you to the pool in order to receive a towel. Many lounge chairs had black mold on them. Invisible biting sand flies or something in great abundance by the pool areas and in the grass by the beach. I have been back from Puerto Rico over a week and am still scratching at 75 -100 bites. Front desk management/service was great. Support staff service, ex. waiters, housekeeping, bartenders, etc...., were not so good, we suppose because of the nature of all-inclusives there isn't any incentive for the staff to put in any more effort than is absolutely necessary.All in all, we had a nice time because of the company we were with. On a scale of 1-10 to rate the resort itself on everything from food, to service, to amenities for the price we paid, I would give Paradisus-Puerto Rico a 5. If the rooms were a little less spacious I would give the resort a 4.

There are three pools at this property. At the main pool, one must present a towel card in order to get a towel which is a major inconvenience, and irritating music is played from a large speaker. <Content>I have had fun everywhere in the world except..... <Content>Overpriced for an average resort..more like a 4 star This review is kinda longer but worth the read. I am an avid recreational vacationer who usually stays at 4-5 star properties that are AI. I'm not super-picky, all I ask is that I get my $$$ worth. I stayed at the Paradisus during July 2005. We went as a family of 6 and went with the Royal Service. For a vacation that cost us $15K, it definitely wasn't worth it. I saw NO difference between the usual guest and the Royal guest (besides the use of a lounge and a pool that my 8 year old couldn't use anyway). The food was just OK...not gourmet. The restaurants seem to be understaffed. When you ask someone a question, you'll get 6 different answers. I had to make several calls to housekeeping, and Royal Service just to get enough towels. I was on the phone at the least twice a day asking for something (the minbar was never refilled and I never had enough bath towels). The rooms were absolutely beautiful and the grounds are amazing. The staff at the Royal Lounge tried their best to help you out but senior management seemed unresponsive to guest problems. When I checked in, I was told that one of the oceanview royal suites I booked was not available and they insisted that I never booked an oceanview to begin with. After proving my case with documentation from my travel agent, they believed me but couldn't get me the room. I opted for a refund for the difference b/w the rooms and was told that I'd get a letter of refund at the end of my stay to show my travel agent. As if that letter was ready for me upon departure! I had TO WAIT for the letter to be drafted while my airport transfer waited for me! The butler service was OK and it seemed like I'd get problems resolved faster by making the calls myself. What did I pay extra for? As for reservations at the restaurants, I really didn't have much of problem (the resort was fairly empty for the most part of my stay). On the weekends, they allow locals to use the pool area (which is totally inappropriate). If you want to go into town, open your wallet! It cost almost $30pp to get into town via shuttle. And if you want to go to the rainforest (which you can see from the resort...that's how close it is) is $50pp. Speaking of being ripped off, the cherry on the cake of this vacation was when I received my cell bill when I got home I found unauthorized calls to Dominican Republic on my phone while I was there! Apparently someone in housekeeping helped themselves to my hidden cell phone to call their family! HIDE YOUR CELL PHONES IN THE SAFE OR TAKE THEM WITH YOU! This resort has much room for improvement. Perhaps I'll go back when they get their act together. If you get a good deal on this resort, I'd try it. Otherwise, it's not worth the $$$$$$$$$

<Content>Overpriced and underserviced I recently stayed at the San Juan Paradisus on a business related trip and overall I would have to say I was extremely disappointed with the experience. I found the service lacking, the food unexciting and the entertainment boring and unprofessional. For the prices they charge, they should be delivering more of a 4 star experience.Details:- Check in- Although I had to wait about 45 minutes for my room (I arrived before check in time), the Royal Services receptionists were very nice and accommodating. My butler took me by trolley to my room and was attentive. However, I did not see him again for the rest of my stay. - Rooms- The rooms were nice with the usual upscale hotel room accommodations. Nothing particularly special. Pools- Very nice, particularly the Royal Service pool. I was there in the middle of the week and the pools (and the resort in general) seemed to be only about 20% full. I鈥檓 told that weekends bring a lot of locals and the pools can get quite crowded. The Royal Service pool attendant gave the best service we experienced. - Restaurants- For an all-inclusive, there was a profound lack of selection and the food was average at best. Buffets were not particular large and selection was very limited. The stir-fry or pasta station was 15 people deep with a 20 minute for a cooked to order dish. In a waited restaurant this would be acceptable but not at a buffet. Much of the buffet food was cold and some did not seem fresh. My group of 10 requested a 7PM reservation at Romantico and was told they could only accommodate us at 6:40. Fine, we arrived at 6:40 to and empty restaurant that wasn鈥檛 near half full at 7:00. Why couldn鈥檛 they have just honored our 7PM request? The food at Romantico was good but there just wasn鈥檛 enough of it. Portions were ridiculously small. (2 escargot appetizer, 4 very small lamb chops, a sliver of cake.) I was hungry after dinner. There is no food option on the beach like the sandwich shack you find in other all- inclusives. Room service is a joke. Very limited menu with tiny portions. Three of four in my party told me they ordered room service when they got back to their rooms (still hungry after dinner) and after 45 minutes their orders were delivered incorrectly.Service- While they seem to try, my impression was they just don鈥檛 really know what good service is. (i.e.- staff going above and beyond to exceed your needs and ensure you have a memorable stay). They do the minimum amount possible to deal with you or your situation and then move you on. Sometimes we weren鈥檛 even told the truth in their attempt to move us on. My impression is that the service is fine until there is a problem or a challenge and then they simply don鈥檛 want to deal with it. I found this with the concierge, front desk, bellmen, bars and in the restaurants. For the rates they charge, they should have a better attitude. They should drown you in service and go out of their way to make you feel special.Entertainment- Other than a cheesy lounge singer and the casino, there is none. Overall: a disappointment. For these rates at a supposed 4-star hotel you should get the feeling that they want to make you happy. The food should be abundant and higher quality. I will not be returning.

The staff was without a clue, asking 5 of them what restaurant was opened on any given day resulted in 5 different answers (sadly all wrong). Spa-Overpriced for the service which was ho hum, nothing to write home about but certainly nothing to complain about. Again tips were defintely expectedCar rental- we reserved a car week before we arrived, we checked once at the resort on Monday she confirmed that she indeed had our reservation for the Thursday returning to the airport. On the Wednesday we went to the Avis counter to check on our car (we had nothing to do) only to find out that they had no cars for us becasue they were short in SJU airport so they took all the vehicles. Now we were stranded! the only suggestion teh woman had was that she could refer us to a local rental agency but they only had one location so we would have to bring it back to them! so what good was this doing us! upon bringing this to the attention of Royal Service staff i was told that for $60 they could have the shuttle bring us to the airport to pick up a car. So now we have to pay $60 on top of the $60 per day the car was costing us just to leave this place! the least the should have done was to comp us the shuttle to the Avis counter at the airport. My biggest complaint? It is so surprising to me that a hotel general manager would ask to hear their guests' comments and even take the time to respond to these Tripadvisor reviews but when presented with the opportunity to resolve a valid issue first hand before it gets to a review point; can be so totally clueless. Had Mr Lapp taken the ten minutes or to speak with us and listen to what we had to say I am sure he would have felt as did his other management personnel (who did attempt to to resolve these issues to no avail) that this was not acceptable anywhere in the world but even less in an alleged 5* resort. We paid good money to stay here, we were asking for nothing more than what we paid for, the quality were were promised and the quantity were were promised; 6 restaurants, clean robes non threadbare towels and sheets with no holes. We were not looking to get more than we paid for, but we were certainly looking to get what we were promised! Beware if you choose to stay here, bring lots of $$ for tip and your own robes/towels.

<Content>Had potential, but certainly not there yet. My husband and I just returned from a four-night stay at the Paradisus. When we first arrived, we were very pleased. The resort is beatifully decorated and the pool is lovely. However, our excitement was short-lived! Our sheets had stains on them and the bed was not very comfortable at all.After spending about 30 minutes at the pool, we had had enough! The hotel overbooked the rooms due to a convention that weekend (we were told by a staff member that there were more than 4 people staying in a lot of rooms). The pool was extremely crowded and got dirty quickly - the guests were leaving plastic cups and straws throughout the pool area and they were floating around the water. The staff did try to clean it up but there was just way too many people for them to keep up. It was also impossible to get a drink at the bar, and when you were finally waited on, they were often out of whatever it was you wanted. The bartenders also seemed put out to take your drink orders. If the beach was beautiful, I would have been just as happy to spend the day there, but as another guest had said, it was non-existent. What little sand they had was covered in broken rocks, making it impossible to walk along and shallow water was covered in patches of sea-weed, making it impossible to swim in.The restaurants were mediocre at best. Romantico was the best food by far, however they classify themselves as fine dining and fancy with their dress code. They will not, under any circumstance, allow a male to dine in their restaurant with shorts on. My husband and I went to dinner, he was dressed in pressed khaki shorts and a button-down shirt and they would not allow him in the dining room until he put long pants on. This would be fine if this was their rule, however, they classified ripped, baggy jeans as long pants. While they would not let us in, they were allowing guests in baggy, ripped jeans, white tank tops and sneakers to eat in their dining room - fancy restaurant, I think not! One of the better nights we had was spent ordering cheeseburgers from room service to avoid the noisy crowds in the lobby and restaurants. This, too, was short lived, as the cable for the second night in a row was not working. After we complained and suggested they allow us to order a free movie they did, which was the right way to handle the situation. However, we got about half way through the film and that shut off, and was out for the rest of the evening.As I said, the resort itself was beautiful, but they need to improve their hospitality skills. There is no way this resort is a five-star, I would like to meet the person that rated it and find out how stained sheets, mediocre service, dirty pools and mildew stained lounge chairs can ever be classified as five star.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Some good points - some not so good I spent June 5 - 11 with my wife and 4 year old daughter at Paradisus and this is the second all-inclusive we've been to (the first was Iberostar Tucan in Playa del Carmen, Mexico - a true 4 -5 star resort). What really needs to be done is break down the categories and rate them. Price - 3 out of 5 stars - We were very satisfied with the cost even after upgrading to the Royal Service - which is a must.Service - 4 out of 5 starsWe upgraded to the Royal Service. If you are are not a Royal Service guest, the service will be poor. We were mistaken for non-RS guests and had to wait 45 minutes for someone to come to our room and get our luggage. Most employees were very nice - especially those assigned to RS guests. The resort was fairly empty so we were moved to a ocean front suite immediately.Food - 1 out of 5 stars The website states 5 star cuisine - not even close. You must make reservations to avoid the toscana and carribean grill. Avacado was only open 1 night ( we were there 6 nights) - The Bamboo the japanese fusion (which is really just a hibachi steak house) was open, but the staff never told us there was an appetizer menu with sushi and sashimi on it. Pretty lame not to do that. The Italian buffet style Toscana was horrible and the carribean buffet was only a little better. This place is not kid friendly in terms of food. The outdoor grill and eating area was never open when we were there so it was either eat inside after having to change your wet swimsuit, or eat lunch outside in 90 degree heat/100 percent humidity away from the shore with no breeze. Also there are no kids allowed in Romantico the French restaurant - thus eliminating another choice for our family. So for 5 of 6 nights, there were only 2 restaurants available to us.Beverages were plentiful and readily available - house wines were drinkable. There really was no afternoon snacks - all deep fried food.Beach - NONE no starsA dead reef surrounds the swimming area and although quite beautiful in a natural sort of way...the water is not what you would expect from Puerto Rico. Swimmable and clean, but not pleasant. No snorkeling. Catamaran, kayaking and paddle boats were fun though. Ground and Pool - Pool is great - grounds excellent 4 out of 5 starsKid friendly - 0 out of 5 starsThe Kids club is a small playground. There is no staff to organize any activities - except adult aquarobics - There is a baby sitter available if you need it.Activity packages - 0 out of 5 starsSince Paradisus is 50 minutes - 1 hour from San Juan with no traffic (and not the 35 minutes the website boasts) Most excursions outside the resort cost $60 - $100 per person. We rented a car for $60 and went on our own. Driving is no problem. The only kiosk is an AVIS rental (which is funny - because the resort package we purchased included a large discount for HERTZ - so if you took the resorts shuttle - you couldn't rent-a-hertz! ) Definitely do the rain forest and old san juan. If you rent a car an need to park it over night, you get charged $15 to park your car at the resort you're staying at! That was unbelieveable. The Spa is way over priced - even for a resortRoom - 4 out of 5 stars - Room was beautiful with a jacuzzi on the balcony - though there are no doors or any separation between the 2 rooms of the suite. View was lovely from the balcony.Oh by the way, we left an old worthless SLR automatic camera at the restaurant one night...never to be seen again - no one turned it in...good thing I didn't leave our digital camera.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Must visit Paradise, I mean, Paradisus My wife and I just came back from 4 nights at Paradisus Puerto Rico and had an amazing time. We have travelled and stayed at luxury resorts in the past, and we had a great experience here. I was certainly concerned before going after reading some of the earlier reviews, but for the most part was pleased.Pros: The resort setting is gorgeous. The grounds were well kept with plants and flowers. It was clean.The main pool was fantastic. Despite many people in the pool, it was large enough were you could find your own quiet corner. Swim up bar and partially submerged lounge chairs were a plus.The covered cabanas were great and provided some needed shade from the HOT SUN. The food was very good. Breakfast and lunches were mostly buffets, but the quality of the food was great. Dinners were very good. Service was a bit weak (see cons below).The beach was actually great. Not the best for actual swimming, but nice to sit out and use the kayaks and paddleboats (included).Royal Service was a must. Nicer rooms. Made a jacuzzi on your balcony for you each night if you wanted. Access to private pool.Cons:A bit of a drive from the airport.The service in the restaurants was still a bit slow and not as responsive as one would expect at such a resort. They didn't fill water glasses promptly. When asked, they would say ok and not come back. You would have to ask several people (often the manager) to fill the glass. When you went up for seconds (or thirds, fourths, fifths) of food, they didn't take away the dirty plates. It became a bit comical after a while.The reservation system for dinners still doesn't quite work. I had heard that they improved it by allowing you to call before you arrive. When I did (the day before arrival) I was told they would hold the time slot and to call when I arrived with my room number. I did, but was told that the reservation time wasn't available and had to chose different times (not the ideal ones, but oh well, we were on vacation). However, when we did arrive for our 8:30 reservation at Bamboo (had called and asked for 7) they told us that it would be at least 30 minutes more. We ended up not staying and just going to one of the restaurants that didn't need reservations.The only other con would be that in the evening there isn't too much to do. They close the pools at 6pm (seemed kinda early) and at 10pm had a typical resort show. The lounges are open but aside from that there was alot of activity. We ended up sitting on our jacuzzi on our balcony, cetainly not a bad thing....Overall, we had a great time and would certainly recomend Paradisus. I would hope with time and more training in the restaurants, the service would improve and this would be a perfect place. That being said, it certainly was close to paradise...

The concierge pool is quiet and relaxing and has private pre reserved cabanas. We weren't in the Royal Service level, but I found the staff to be very friendly and accommodating. The main pool is beautiful and has many private cabanas, , more cabanas than I have seen at other resorts. When the property is full they are somewhat difficult to obtain, early bird gets the worm. Within a week this happened maybe 3-4 times, big deal we were on vacation and had lots of time and weren't in a hurry to go anywhere. We were at the resort when they were filming the Sports Invitational for Fox TV, there were about 50 celebrities there such as Kevin Costner, Chevy Chase, Kelsey Grammer, Matt Dillion... if it's good enough for them than it should be good enough for you!Beach- ok so you know that the beach isn't white sand, the water isn't a tourquise blue other than this the resort is beautiful. I have been to many other worldwide resorts that offer better beaches, but I knew about the beach prior to arriving and was perfectly content with the beach. I personally think it is hard to find every single aspect of a resort, property, destination that has 100 % of everything that you might be looking for. Sure I could find a few petty things that could be taken care of, but they are petty and not worth my time getting upset over.I found the Paradisus to be a true paradise and gorgeous resort and can recommend it highly to others.

<Content>Relaxing and Romantic We went to Paradisus May 3rd-8th - and, having traveled quite a bit (including 5 star all-inclusives), my expectations are always VERY, VERY high - and, I'm usually disappointed. But, this time I was pleasantly surprised! First off, let me echo what countless others have said in their reviews... the grounds are AMAZINGLY beautiful.
