Our favorite part of the room was the sunken jacuzzi tub (for two!) outside ON the balcony. I've never had that experience before... and, drinking a glass of wine overlooking the ocean in a tub of bubbles is the BEST - especially after a day of baking in the sun. (Oh, by the way, they CHANGED ALL THE BEDS in the early Spring, 2005. So, we went expecting HARD mattresses due to other people's comments and instead had a week of TERRIFIC sleep on the new, perfect mattresses!!)Ahhh... baking in the sun. The main pool was glorious. Since we came on a week that wasn't very booked, we felt like the resort was our own private plantation. There were only about 4-6 other people around this HUGE pool at any given time of the day Tuesday - Friday. The built-in chairs made laying in the sun a dream because you could stay cool, covered by an inch of water from the pool on your legs and feet. It was an amazing, relaxing experience on those days... (I'll save all my negative comments for the end of this review!)Another great part of the resort is the top notch spa and workout area. Although we didn't have any spa treatments on this trip, we did take a complete tour of the spa area and everything was very relaxing and pristine - including the indoor and outdoor massage tables. (You can get a massage in the tropical garden area by the spa pool - or even at the edge of the ocean if you choose!) We did use the exercise equipment on three of our vacation days - and it was great! (Air-conditioned and aromas from the attached spa made it smell fantastic!)THE NEGATIVES:1- The food was just ok. Typically, we go out to eat quite a bit - to a variety of top restaurants. Going out to eat for me needs to be an experience - not just about the food. (great atmosphere, good wine selection, excellent service!) So, I was really looking forward to both the Japanese steak house on the property as well as the French restaurant that everyone raved about. But, this is where is was disappointed... Our first night at the Japanese steakhouse was pretty good but the second time the food had little flavor. (It all depends on the cook you get that night. The second night our cook was new.) As for the French restaurant (Romantico) - not so romantico... very boring actually. The place was EMPTY!! And, we were seated at a 2-top in the center of the restaurant with no one else really in the room we were in. There was no background noise so we felt like all ears were on us and we talked very little. As for the food at Romantico - I think they're favorite ingredient is Nutmeg. The Lobster Bisque that came highly recommended from our waiter was really creme de Nutmeg (I think they may have dipped a Lobster claw in the broth at some point but there wasn't really any Lobster to speak of in the soup.) As for the Filet Mignon main course - dry and tasteless. (I'm spoiled with Midwestern Beef.)2- Be prepared to age 10 years waiting for a drink. Now, I know what you're thinking... she's so impatient - she should just get used to the Carribean pace. NO WAY. I have been to Sandals in the Bahamas and other resorts in the Carribean several times and I have never experienced bar service like this. Let me break it down... There are about 4-5 bars around the resort (not including the restaurant bars) and NONE of them stock the same inventory. If you find one that knows how to make a drink you like, the next bar will say they don't carry that liquor. It's crazy! I wanted a Vanilla Stoli and Diet Coke and the waiter from Romantico had to walk out to the main lobby bar to borrow their stash of Vanilla Stoli. But, MORE importantly, the service itself is very bad at the bars. There were two guys at the main lobby bar that had drinks in front of them and were deep in conversation with the bartender when we showed up. (Other than those two guys we were the only ones there.) We sat patiently for at least 5 mins - ignored completely. Finally, I got up and walked around the bar right in front of the bartender and asked him, Is this bar open? Oh yes, miss... and then he took our order. The pool bar is another story... none of the bartenders had any drink suggestions whatsoever. So, if you didn't already know the tropical concoction you wanted top of mind - you were out of luck. And, not surprising, they were just as slow and unattentive as the main lobby bartenders. (To contrast, the bartenders at Sandals were FANTASTIC! Not only was there a HUGE menu hanging around every bar with 10-20 different drink suggestions, but the bartenders had their own specialties that they would reveal to swim-up bar regulars.) Personality is KEY to staffing great bartenders... and, they still have a ways to go there.3- The beach is filled with broken shells and sharp stones. So what? It didn't really matter that much to me, since I'm a pool person anyway. It was still beautiful to look at out of our balcony every morning and every night from our JACUZZI!! But, if you are a beach person this would probably be a drawback for you.4- ... and, then there was SATURDAY. Remember how I wrote that Tuesday through Friday at the main pool were fantastic?? Well, on Saturdays, they open up the resort to locals. AAAAAAAAAAAAAAHHHHHHH!!! Saturday was a nightmare at the main pool - total chaos. Seemingly thousands of screaming, running children and salsa music so loud it only inspired the kids to scream louder. After 15 mins at the main pool on Saturday, we retreated to the Royal Services pool area for some quiet cocktails and romantic pooltime. That is one of the reasons you should DEFINITELY choose Royal Service if you go to Paradisus.... the option to use that private pool area as well as other niceties.Now, go plan your vacation and stop reading these reviews!! :)

<Content>Beautiful resort We were looking for a resort where there would be a variety of activities and yet plenty of relaxing. The Paradisus was wonderful for our family get-a-way. Since the resort is so new, I am sure it will continue to fine tune it's services....but we enjoyed ourselves and would love to go back.

<Author>larchdoc
<Content>Paradisus Skeptic As a true skeptic, I was very tentative concerning my trip to Paradisus, especially after reading the reviews from this site. I considered changing my plans to the Ritz Carlton if the reviews were correct and indeed had booked the Ritz tentatively if I decided to leave the Paradisus.Much to my surprise, the resort was extremely pleasurable. Specifically:1. The hotel's appearance and cleanliness were terrific.2. The staff was extremely attentive and polite.3. The food was quite good. I never experienced any long lines. (even though the resort was full) Especially notable were the restaurants Romantico and Bamboo. If you are flexible about your dinner times it is quite easy to obtain entrance into them. The Avocado was excellent for my perpetual diet. Indeed, there is an abundance of great fruit which allowed me to only gain one pound during the week. 4. The gym was sufficient and clean.5. Spa was excellent.6. Pools were great. Indeed at times I did have concern about the level of music but this was rectified simply by asking the attendant to turn down the volume.7. THE BEACH Directly in front of the main pool it is certainly almost non existant. If you decide to walk approximately 200 feet to the right there is sufficient beach with an abundance of lounges. 8. The beds. They have all been replaced with very comfortable soft mattresses.9. The lounge chair problem has been resolved with the purchase of many more.10. SUMMARY Overall, it appears that many of the problems noted on this board has been addressed by management. Indeed, I did speak to management and they do review these boards in order to improve their facility. It is still a fairly new resort and certain problems will always occur as with any resort. Not every employee responds as desired and unfortunately can cause a problem. I did have to call room service twice on one occasion but management was very attentive to my complaint. That is basically what we all want---somebody who will listen and resolve the issue-- the resort does this. The resort is particularly excellent for family groups, small conventions or small groups who need to spend time together without wondering where they will eat or meet at nite. It keeps people together. It is certainly infinitely better than any other place in Puerto Rico! I do have one compaint though, and that was with the price of a round of golf which I thought was excessive. I did price other courses in the area and they were all about the same. Maybe the resort can have a golf package price. In essence, I , the Skeptic, would return.

<Author>CompressedChi
<Content>Lost in Paradisus As other have written, this is a beautiful, well maintained property that is all-inclusive and a member of the Leading Hotels of the World. We just returned from a long weekend and found much of what has been said (both good and bad) to be true.We had several choices of hotels in San Juan and decided to try the Paradisus on the strength of its reviews. Based on the suggestions of others who found it difficult to get into certain restaurants, I decided to call the day before to try to make arrangements prior to our arrival. I was told that reservations can only be made if you know your room number, which unfortunately is not revealled until you check in. I also asked for driving directions from the airport and was emailed them promptly.The property, while it may be only 20 miles away from the airport, took about an hour to drive to in bumper to bumper traffic. We decided to rent a car based on the fact that the hotel shuttle charged $30/per person one way, so for the two of us it would have been $120 round trip. The driving directions are somewhat confusing, and we had a few wrong turns that only delayed our arrival. We also found out that they charge guests $10/day to park (not mentioned anywhere), which is crazy since the lot is huge and very underutilized. Since we were there for 3 days, the $30 added onto the cost of the rental car came out a little over $120--no wonder the hotel priced it's shuttle that way!Upon arrival, there were a lot of bellmen, none of which offered us any assistance with our bags. Check if was very efficient, but as was noted by other, we were left on our own to find our room. When we went back to the bellhops to ask about transport to our room, they said that no one was available to bring our bags, so we should take the trolley since the room was very far away. We went back to the front desk to inquire about closer rooms and the woman at the front desk was very apologetic and reassured us the room was not that far away and even walked us to the trolley (which is located at the back end of the lobby), and we rode to our room from there.I must say that the property is spectacular and well kept. The employees are polite, but do not go out of their way to be helpful. Rather than ask the concierge to make dinner arrangements for us (since there was only one concierge and a line of about 10 people needing assistance), we walked directly to the restaurant and asked about tables. We found Bamboo to be difficult to get into and the surly hostess did not make things easy. The host at Romantico was much more accomodating. Bamboo is a down market version of Benihana, but entertaining and they offer you a lot of food. The atmosphere at Romantico is very nice and the service good. They also offer a surcharge wine list, which has very good wines at New York restaurant prices (about twice retail) -- but it beats what they pour for free.We went to the gym daily, which is virtually always empty, and very clean. The attendant was friendly, and it turns out that he will teach aerobics, but only if enough people show up. He also told us that there were pilates classes at the Activities Center that did not exist. The Activities Center is poolside and there is a list of daily activities posted. Unfortunately, no one seemed to know what activities would occur the next day, so it was difficult to plan things. The pool is great. There are a lot of areas to sit around and plenty of chaise chairs and cabanas on a first come first serve basis. The cabanas are definitely the way to go as the sun can be fierce. Poolside salsa lessons in the afternoon were a lot of fun! Beware that the drinks at the poolside bar are very weak, and one should always ask for an extra shot!The rooms are very spacious and the oceanview rooms offer a wonderful, romantic setting to watch the sunset off your balcony. One thing we found lacking in the amenities were hair conditioner and a sewing kit (you only figure out what you forgot to bring when you need it most!). It turns out that there is something called Royal Service which functions like a Club Level Room in other hotels. They have personal butlers and a private pool and check in service. It is significantly more expensive than the already pricey rooms, and I'm not sure it is worth it.All in all, the place is beautiful. The food was good for an all inclusive, but not great. My overall impression is that this five star hotel would match up with a middling three star place in Asia or Europe and a four star hotel in the US. They really need to improve their service, especially since it isn't cheap. I think that there are numerous other options to consider when choosing a San Juan hotel that (technically) isn't in San Juan.

<Author>gsmarko
<Content>Stay Away - no beach, no service, not much at all The Positives1. The hotel鈥檚 appearance and the grounds are absolutely beautiful.2. The beachfront dining at Mirador provided spectacular views of the ocean. A wonderful, tranquil dining experience.3. The tennis pro was excellent.4. The spa, though small, was very pleasant. My wife loved it.5. Dinner at Bamboo was very enjoyable. That said, this restaurant should not be described as 鈥淎sian fusion with Thai influence鈥? It is, quite simply, a Japanese Hibachi style restaurant with a very limited menu of sushi.6. The swim-up bar in the pool was great. It was one of the few areas in the resort which was properly staffed.The Negatives1. ABSOLUTELY ZERO BEACH. The beach is about 12 feet wide from the grass to the water. The limited space is filled with rocks and broken shells. There is no sand to sit on and no place for children to play. The resort was full when we were there but no one at all was on the beach. Also, the water sports are extremely limited.2. The pool is large and nice, but could be cleaner. Since there is no real beach and little available activities, I would think the resort would put more effort into keeping the pool clean and in tip-top shape. The water at times was cloudy and often contained drinking cups and debris. Furthermore, for our entire stay, the hotel was full but there was never more than 1 lifeguard on duty covering a massive pool that often contained  150 people. I was astonished. 3. Seating by the pool was inadequate. At one point, this lead to a shouting match between guests over seating space. If the pool is the main attraction of the resort, should seating be inadequate?4. The restaurants were booked from the time of check-in and many guests could only get into the buffet restaurants. This was ridiculous since the restaurants were only about 60% occupied when you went inside. The only explanation I can think of is that the resort was inadequately staffed. This is shameful considering the expensive price of the resort and the large # of guests. If you can not get into 1 of the 3 non-buffet restaurants for dinner, you are stuck at one of the 3 buffets. The quality of food at the buffet restaurants was sub-par. My dinner at Toscano is best described as a bad night at Macaroni Grill (not even a good night at Macaroni Grill). Not a great deal for $750/night.5. Even at the buffet restaurants there was a long wait to be seated. We waited 30 minutes to be seated at Toscano. Once seated, we found that 60% of the tables were empty. When we asked why we waited 30 minutes to get into a largely vacant restaurant, we were told that they did not haven enough staff to clear the tables. This is shameful.6. The concierge desk is woefully inadequate. There was never more than 1 person working. You often had to wait 20 minutes to speak to someone. You could not call the concierge desk since they were too busy to answer the phone.7. Service is extremely slow throughout the resort. Room service is particularly bad, often taking  1 hour.8. The beds are as hard as a rock. This is a frequent complaint among customers. It appears that the resort is trying to purchase new mattresses to address this problem. Negatives that really messed up our trip1. We arrived late at night with a 3 year old. We needed bedding for the couch. We had to call housekeeping 5 times. It took 1 hour and 20 minutes to get a blanket. The good news was that hotel manager wanted to appease us afterwards and suddenly the restaurants with no available dinner reservations had a spot for our family. 2. Room service consistently took too long and brought not only cold food but the wrong food.3. The porters were not careful with our luggage. They arrived late to pick up our luggage, drove their little truck recklessly, and our luggage went flying out of the truck onto the road.4. MOST IMPORTANTLY, our son got sick and required a doctor. The concierge desk, which was probably the single worst aspect of the resort, took 4 hours to pick up the medicine from the local pharmacy. This was clearly due to the fact that they were understaffed and they were prioritizing 鈥渘ew business鈥?over a sick, young child. This was disgraceful.Overall, I would strongly discourage anyone from staying at Paradisus Puerto Rico. The resort may look beautiful, but the terrible service, understaffing, and lack of a beach front are significant problems. This is not a 5 star resort, not a 4 star resort, and maybe not even a 3 star resort. Of note, many people we met on the island (away from the resort) were well aware of the many problems at the resort. This undoubtedly explains why the occupancy has been low and the cost of staying at the resort has dropped precipitously over the past year.

Kids camps at other resorts are much better, Hyatt, Ritz and other all inclusives. They play loud, loud music and make announcements at the pool all day, if you want peace you have to go to the pebbly beach, which is ok too, but it could be better. The rooms are far from the main facilities, ours did smell a bit musty and there are very few ocean view rooms, if you are not guaranteed, you won't get one. The restaurants requiring reservations were all full, we wondered whether it was a scam to have them, but not let anyone in, they didn't seem crowded at all. If you complain loudly they may help you get in at a time they select. This is ridiculous. The hotel is 1 hour from the airport NOT 35 mins, except by helicopter.HINT - The Royal Service is very, very nice (we didn't get it, but wish we did) there is a beautiful adult pool, preference at restaurants, ocean view, special services, if your kids are over 5 or you are just adults visiting, this would be key to a relaxing, pampered vacation. I would not go back with my husband alone unless we had Royal Service accomodations.If you go ENJOY - don't be nervous this is a nice place, they care about their guests and you will have a good time! I was reluctant because of some of the bashing I saw here, which is exaggerated. No its not the Four Seasons, Paris, but if you booked here that is not what you are expecting!

<Author>KatefromCT
<Content>An Enjoyable Long Weekend My husband and I spent 4 nights (March 17-21) at the Paradisus. While there were a couple of snafus, all in all, we were satisfied with our stay. We are in our mid-forties, travel frequently for business, live in a metropolitan area and have vacationed internationally.I would recommend that you book the Royal Service. This allows you benefits that are not included in the standard room. Close proximity to the pools, butler service, concierge lounge, assistance with difficult dinner reservations, turndown, bathrobes, daily newspaper, etc.We arrived in the late morning at the airport to find a guide with a Paradisus sign to direct us to the shuttle. We were relieved to see her in such a prominent place only to find that we were not on the shuttle list. Unfortunately, my husband had called a couple of times to confirm that we were on the shuttle so this was annoying. They quickly told us that they had plenty of room for us on the shuttle, cool drinks welcomed us aboard. The shuttle driver was an absolute maniac driver. Having spent a lot of time in NYCity cabs, we thought we had seen it all. He was friendly and engaging, but he was a complete maniac behind the wheel. We probably should have reported him to the management. We joked that he was probably Chevy Chase in the Vacation movies, but I could not get off fast enough. The ride is a solid 45 minutes without traffic. There are two routes, along the coast (beautiful, but two lanes) or through the commercial districts. Both take approximately the same amount of time. The cost for the shuttle is $60/pp round trip. A cab may be a better idea. If you are adventerous, they have car rentals although we never needed to leave the resort.Upon arrival, you are greeted by a very friendly staff. Lots of smiles and very welcoming. When we checked in, they didn't have us registered or any note that we had booked the Royal Service. Within seconds, it was literally the blink of an eye, a VERY astute front desk person, Omayra, wisked us off to the Royal Service area and had us completely booked into the hotel. I can't stress enough what a difference the RS makes. The check-in area is comfortable as well as air-conditioned. For this resort, it's very personalized service. One of the butlers offered us something to drink (alcoholic or not), along with a selection of appetizers and fruit. After a long flight, we thought it was nice to be offered Mimosas. On the spot, Omayra booked our dinner reservations for the next four evenings. I have read that people are able to make them before arrival, but we were unable to get them to budge on that when we called. I would highly recommend that you make the reservations immediately upon arrival. The reservation system is completely out of whack and there were guests that were rightfully miffed that they couldn't get a dinner reservation before 9pm. (some could not get them at all) All of the nights there seemed to be open tables and lots of staff so I'm not sure where the problems lie.The restaurants are cruise-like. The reservation-only restaurants, Romantico, Avacado and Bamboo were good. They weren't great, but they were good. These are in no way five star restaurants. We had two dinners at Romantico and if you eat meat, I would recommend the beef. I am a seafood lover and had a seafood dish that I thought was marginal at best. I didn't quite figure out if luke warm was to the local liking, but most of the food was not hot. The staff, however, is totally first rate. They literally bend over backwards to make sure that you are enjoying yourself. They do this without seeming to be forced. We did give some of the staff tips, which they gladly accepted, but it is not necessary. It's difficult to see the housing around the resort and not think that the staff could use the extra income.Our butler took us on a tour of the facility, told us a little history of the resort and actually pointed out that they were replacing all of the mattresses. We saw large tractor trailers full of mattresses because of all of the complaints about the original hard mattresses. Our mattress must have been a replacement as it was very comfortable and not at all hard.Royal Service also has an adult-only pool. We weren't traveling with children and this perk was absolute perfection. We basically camped out in one of the sheltered huts (Palapas) while having two incredibly large, comfortable and padded lounge chairs directly in front of us at poolside. The huts can be reserved so each morning we arrived to a reserved covered, lounge area with large, lush towels waiting for us. The inside diameter of the covered area is approximately 9x9' square. It's a giantic cushion with side rolls to lean against. We could very comfortably lay down and the Palapa gets you out of the strong sun.The staff at the pool deserves the highest marks. They were so incredibly attentive that we could not have asked for more. Felix was an all-star staff-member that we really enjoyed. He came around with citrus water (chilled) and asked if he could spray us down. It was about 85 degrees and very sunny so we certainly appreciated it. Later in the day, he offered us scented, water soaked hand towels that had been refrigerated. We did tip him at the end of the day, as did most of the other guests. The pool was clean and comfortable, the water temperature was just right. The music was background music only, it certainly didn't disrupt any of the atmosphere. The rapper, Usher, was a guest a couple of weeks earlier and at some points, they were playing the Usher CD, perhaps in his honor. The beach is beautiful to look at and a nice walk with the right footwear. We brought along beach shoes, mesh, and walked all around the property with ease. From the postings that I had read, I thought we were literally going to be on a rocky coast. It's actually very small pieces of coral and shells that make up the beach. It's not a resort that you would go to for the beach, but it did make for a nice morning walk. I did not see anyone swimming, but there were a couple of guests wading about 4 feet from shore. I can't stress enough that if you want waves, powdery sand and a day in the ocean, this is not the place for you. There are water bikes, kayaks (1, 2, 3 person) and Hobie cats which are available. We took two separate Hobie cat rides with the same captain, a very nice high school senior who told us that this was his weekend job. I have sailed a lot and I was very comfortable with his skill level. My husband and I were alone with the captain on both trips, one in the bay and one along the coast out past the coral reef. The scenery is beautiful and it's difficult to find fault looking onshore. I would highly recommend that you bring appropriate footwear for the beach, it will make it a lot more pleasant and enjoyable. It would be VERY easy to cut your feet on the coral in the water if you do not take the appropriate precautions. They do sell these beach shoes in the boutique if you forget yours at home.The restaurants on the whole were good. It's difficult to find a buffet with fresh and hot out of the oven food so they have a lot of food that can be kept warm. I had a fabulous lunch one day at Avacado, grilled rock lobster tail thrown in with cooked-to-order fettucini alfredo with shrimp. Unfortunately, they only had one chef making the pasta and I noticed that there were probably 20 people in back of me. The dinner at Avacado was good (by good, I'm talking about a restaurant where they charge $12-$25/entree and the expectation is not high). Always an offer for wine and a suggestion to accompany your dinner. Nice service, friendly smiles. Avacado also has breakfast which you can eat outside under a covered area. Made to order omelettes, but only one person making them. We did comment that our experience was probably overstated because the resort was not close to capacity. We estimate that the hotel was probably 30% full with a couple of groups in attendance. They were expecting 1,000 more guests during Easter week and we were happy that we weren't guests during that time.There is a casino and it was not crowded at all. Drinks flow freely everywhere at the hotel so the casino could be lively. In the hotel lobby, there was entertainment every night and although I read that it was very loud, we did not experience that at all. There was a piano player along with one singer and she sang in a moderately loud tone. It was not disturbing at all more of a background music. There is also nightly entertainment at 10pm. We didn't take advantage of that but heard that it was fun. We did think the area around the main pool was loud. During our times on the Hobie cat, we could hear how loud the music and entertainment sounded. They do have dance lessons and a very, very large pool so if you were on the periphery of the pool, you might be able to get around the music. We did not actually sit by that pool so our experience is limited. It certainly was very large and there were chairs everywhere so the seating seemed adequate. There were also probably 400 additional lounge chairs on the area between the rooms and the beach. Some were in the sun, some were shaded by palm trees. We did not even see one person sitting there but some of the people did drag the chairs into the ocean.I personally thoughts the grounds were tropical. The staff seemed meticulous about their groundskeeping yet you never really saw or heard any of it going on. Lots of palm trees.We were probably a 6 minute walk to the main building and were continually asked if we wanted a ride on the shuttle. The shuttle is like a giant golf cart that holdsabout 20 people. I'm sure that there were shuttle stops, but the drivers always nodded and asked us if we wanted a ride. We declined, it was warm and balmy and we were on vacation. Relaxation was what we were striving for. There were a couple of groups at the resort during our stay and in no way did that interrupt or effect our stay. Our room was a Royal Service Garden View, more like distant mountain view and the view was spectacular. I'm sure that there are guests that probably could find something wrong everywhere, but the reality is if the sliding glass door is open and you are 3 miles from a rainforest that gets 1,000,000,000 (yes, a billion) gallons of water a year dumped on it, you will probably have a little bit of dampness or odor. They would have to require guests not to open the door in order for it to stay completely dry. The humidity level in Puerto Rico is 85%. Our room did not have one problem and when we got to the room, the attendant had the bed pulled away from the wall and was cleaning under it. The in-room refrigerator is stocked with plenty of beverages, Coke, Diet Coke, Sprite, Madalla, OJ and bottled water. The beds were comfortable and were turned down each evening along with the towels being restocked. The RS bathrobes were placed on the beds waiting our return. In the morning, we enjoyed coffee out on the lenai.All in all, we had a fabulous time. We did discuss, however, that we would most likely not return and that our assessment was based on a very low occupancy. We commented on how having only 8 people at a private pool with absolutely perfect service could skew your opinion of a resort. It is a bonus that because of our bracelets (RS were gold and red) that we were given upon check-in, we were easily identified by the butlers and sought out for service. With a full house, we can see where problems might not be as quickly resolved. Also, when it's very sunny and hot, it's mandatory to have a hut. We commented that there were only 15 huts in the RS pool area and that we couldn't imagine not having one at our convenience. We probably couldn't have stayed at the pool all day without it.Enjoy. If you have any questions, feel free to email me.

<Content>A fantastic trip to paradise We just returned from a 5 night stay in the oceanfront Villa's. We travel a great deal and some were all-inclusive. The Paradisus Puerto Rico is now at the top of our list of fabulous places to stay. Excellent restaurants and food, service, attention to detail, 2 personal butlers on call 24/7, excellent rooms and the list goes on. This is a new resort (a bit less than a year old) so there were a couple of kinks here and there, but nothing that would detract from a marvelous vacation! Book your restaurant reservations UPON ARRIVAL. Particularly good was the Romantico. A few of the others are buffet but quite good. Our only bad experience was the Italian restuarant (buffet). Our biggest problem was having to explore and figure the place out pretty much on our own. We received some very helpful information when we arrived, but if you are not part of a group, you will not receive the guided tour. The beach is not worthy of being called a beach due to the very rocky conditions. This is, by the way, a condition that cannot be helped by the Paradisus. The government owns the beach and nothing can be done to make for better footing, etc. The pools are excellent and we had a great time anyhow. Overall, we were extremely pleased. The attitude of EVERYBODY was ALWAYS..what can I do to make your stay with us even better? except for the waiter at the Italian restaurant of course. We rate The Paradisus a true 4.75 star facility.

<Author>kings54
<Content>Royal Services A+ My husband  I just returned from a 6 night stay at the Paradisus. I noticed lots of mixed reviews, so thought I would write my own to help out anyone that is planning a trip. Royal Services-I'd like to start by suggesting to everyone to book a Royal Service room. I was unsure if this room category would be worth the extra cost. IT WAS!!! It is especially worth it if you want a quiet, pampered stay. You will be provided with rooms that are in closest proximity to the beach and pools (although still very private and far from any loud activitiy). Butler service is a phone call away - the butlers were fantastic - they gave us a thorough tour of the resort with tips and ideas for things to do. They set up our ocean front deck (which had a nice jacuzzi) with a champagne sunset including a bottle of champagne and a set up bubble-filled jacuzzi to relax in. They also were able to squeeze us in to a restuarant of choice although it was booked on my birthday, and when we returned to our room there was a birthday cake for me! These are just a few the the perks of this Royal Service. There is also a private lounge area which has free internet acess, breakfast, snacks and drinks throughout the day. It was a nice place to grab coffee in the morning and read the paper. There is an adults only pool which had plush teak lounge chairs and palapas surrounding the pool. The music was quiet and relaxing, the bartenders there were fantastic. One tip - grab a chair early, although the bartenders will bring up regular beach lounge chairs when the plush ones run out - I just like to be spoiled. Royal Service also reserved an ocean front palapa (bed-type cushioned lounge under a thatched roof) each day, where we took our 5:30 naps). Staff-Okay - moving on to the rest of the resort. Everyone in the staff was terrific - and very helpful. There was a mess up when we first arrived, mostly because of the hour that we arrived (4:30 am). Although we were supposed to have a Royal Services room, the front desk had sent us to Suite which was not in this category. When the bellman brought this to our attention, we went back to the front desk, where they were not able to do anything until the morning. So, we had to stay for the night in one room, then move to another the next day. Because of this mix up, the hotel quickly upgraded us from a Garden View Royal Services Suite to and Ocean View Suite, which I thought was a great way to handle the mix up! Restaurants - Make your reservations upon arrival! Make sure to go to Romantico - it was the best there. If for some reason you can't get in, stop by the restaurant at 6:00 (opening time) and they can sometimes squeeze you in. Bamboo was good - a typical hibachi restaurant. Avocado was best for lunch, and dinner was okay, but service at dinner was slow. My husband  I are not big fans of buffets, but thought that Avocado's lunch buffet  Toscano's dinner buffet were both great. Please realize that all restaurants have lunch buffets! Mirador is on the beach/large pool, but has very casual food, and seemed to have poor service anytime we went there. All-Inclusive-We have only been to one other all-inclusive resort (Sandals St. Lucia) and that didn't compare. The brands of liquor at the bar are great for an all-inclusive (although with royal services you can get just about anything you want - just ask). The food is very good quality and the grounds are spectacular!Property-The Paradisus is beautiful! The open-air lobby area is georgous at night - lit by hundreds of candles and lanterns. The main pool area is huge. This area is expecially fantastic for families with children (try to grab a palapa to hang out in - many families used this as a shady escape). There is also a swim up bar in this area and lively music. It is true, the beach is not a clear-blue swimmable beach. However, for someone like me who loves the ambience of the ocean surrounding you while you enjoy the pool - it is perfect! It is lagoon-like (the waves break far out over a reef) so many people are out on paddle boats and hobie cats. It is still beautiful - don't let this stop you from coming to the Paradisus! There is a very large sand beach area with many, many lounge chairs, so there is always somewhere to lay around.Our experience overall was excellent (and I am a tough critic when it comes to resorts). Go - enjoy! And - try out that royal service (Travelocity gave us a good deal on this - look there!) Email me with any questions!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fine experience overall but you're naive if you're expecting the Four Seasons or Peninsula stay. My wife and I returned from a five-night stay at this lovely all-inclusive resort in January, and, like any new property (opened 3/04), it has kinks that have to be ironed out. I preface this posting by saying that my wife and I both work in the hotel/ hospitality industry for large hotel companies, and i must say that the Paradisus passes the test. The positives severly outweigh the negatives, and by reading many of these December postings, I have to believe that the Paradisus took the criticism to heart and fixed most of these bugs.This is an all-inclusive resort where tips/ charges are taken care of by your daily rate. But I must say, the staff treated us like royalty from the moment we stepped out of our taxi. The door/bell staff are very cheerful and make an effort to please. They socialize with you and offer assistance before you even have to ask. In the hospiatlity industry, we are expected to anticipate our guest's needs, and at the Paradisus, they do that. From the bellmen down to the maids, they make a sincere effort to make you happy. I happen to believe that, despite it being all-inclusive, it's Ok to tip a couple of bucks. There were times I didn't have change and did not leave a tip, and it was fine with their staff. They didn't seeme bothered or slowed their service because of this. Believe me, this happens at many resorts (Cancun and Domomican rep. come to mind). I received terrific service on my first day through to the fifth day. My wife was there for a conference and I just tagged along and had fun. The lobby bars are very good. You get top of the line liquor and you get your drink refreshed before you're even finished with the one y0ou have in your hand. There was a waiter, which I cannot remember his name, who must have swerved around 50 people in this one area. He was efficient and very friendly. I watched as he filled everyone's order (correctly) and quickly. No one tipped him. Not one. But he came back and gave the 100% service time and time again. I live in Chicago and let me tell you, I can go 15 minutes without having my drink refreshed or even have trouble getting the waiters attention. But at Paradisus, you almost never have to wave a waiter/ waitress over to you because they're already there. I disagree with the assertion that the pool bar/ waitresses sucked. The days varied as far as occupancy ( ranged from 40-75%), but I received great service in the pool. I had a waitress ask me at least every 15-20 minutes if i wanted something. Yes, she did her rounds. Best of all, when i was just snoozing, she didn't bother me like some resorts do.Enough has been said about the restaurants. They're all good, even the buffet ones. Romantico, Bamboo and Avaocado were very good to good. You got to make reservations for them. Do so at concierge as soon as you get there. The Carribeno, Toscano and Madoro Grill were good. What can you say about buffet-style joints? The'ye are not going to be first-class al lof the time. If anyone can tell me a 5-star buffet exists, please tell me. All of the outlets had freindly hostesses and waitstaff. Again, we never had to wait for drinks or requests. Food was hot and fresh. The desserts were good as well.Yes, the beach is not much to look at. I love poweder-sugared beaches like everyone else, but it's relaxing. The sea is dark because it's winter time, so that's not the resort's fault. Also, the sea is cold. It's January for Gods sake. That's how it is. You can Kayak, windsail, paddleboat, etc. It's all included and the staff was very cool. The beach is empty--no other guests around.The entertainment was a bit corny but what do you expect, Vegas? The music was loud but not overwhelming, but I guess that'll be up to you to decide. They have nightly shows that are of decent quality and they have the casino, which i believe is adequately proportiioned for the resort. I won some cash, so maybe that's why I liked it. There are at least 50 slots, a roulette table, 4 Black Jack tables, Carribean Stud, 3-card Poker, Keno and Limit Texas Hold'Em. Again, if you're expecting Vegas, then you'll be disappointed. but the casino is big enough and is never crowded or packed. The dealers are very friendly and love to converse -- unlike many casinos where the dealers are robotic and not very personable.The spa and gym are OK. They could be better for a facility this large. I did not try the spa, but I hear it's expensive, but again...what do you expect? The gym has free weights, treadmills, etc. All the things you need to work out. Fresh fruit, water and towels are provided. There is also a spa private pool for use if you wish.They have two business centers on the property. One is for all guests to use while the other is a VIP/ Premeir Member class facility that has all of you bc needs plus comforts such as leather sofas, wide screen TV and a waitress to offer you cigars and drinks while you check your e-mail. nice touch.I have two small children but I did not bring them on this trip. They are 4 and 2 years old and I believe they would have had fun. They have a large kiddie pool and play area, and there were kid activites throughout the day. I guess it depends on whether there are lots of kids around the pool area for the activities to occur. There were board games available to use for the kids, pool toys, all sorts of balls to play with. Ping Pong and Billiards, Chess also available by the pool. And best of all, if you're hanging out by yourself like I was while the wife was attending her conference, the entertainment staff would play with you.Gift shop was adequate -- had everything you needed. You get fresh fruit/ wine in your room on a daily basis. Newspaper to your door. Shuttle guy driving around asking if you want a lift. I had a room close to the facilites so I didn't utilize him. He always offered and was courteous.Rent a car if you can. Taxis are outrageously priced. Aiport shuttle is expensive as well. One way cab is $66-75 and shuttles run $30 one-way. Rip off.All in all, this property should get better with time. I paid a group rate so, for me, it was definitely worth it. I easily consumed $200 worth of food and drink per day. But for $469 a night...I don't know about that. Not yet, anyway.

<Author>yahootie
<Content>Great vacation! Overall I was very pleased with my recent trip to Paradisus. The resort is beautiful! My two major dislikes were that the bed was very hard and that the water in the pool was very cold. It is also true that there is not much of a beach (but I'm a pool person, so this did not bother me). Service ranged from average to good, but all of the staff was very friendly and aimed to please. Anyone traveling to the Carribean must remember that there is a thing called Carribean time, and not to expect instantaneous service. That is just the way of life there. So, if you go in knowing that, you will not be too disappointed. The two restaurants, Bamboo and Romantico are excellent, though hard to get into. Otherwise, the food at the buffets (especially Avacado)is good (sometimes cold, but that is true at any buffet). The drinks were wonderful, especially the Mojitos prepared at the Lobby Bar.I would recommend this resort and would happily return!

<Author>Luv2TravelOften
<Content>Not deserving of "Leading Hotels of the World" rating POSITIVES: 1. Beautiful grounds, lobby and room2. Bamboo and Romantico restaurants (two that need reservations) extremely nice3. With some exceptions, buffet restaurants very good4. Most of staff was very pleasant. Beds were great, but we like firm mattresses.6. Showers in rooms had great water pressure.7. Drinks were great. You don't get beer on tap in plastic cups everywhere. Medalla (local beer) is great. Also have Corona and Coors Light. Booze isn't well quality (i.e., they had Absolute vodka, Dewers scotch, etc.)8. The built-in lounge chairs around the edge of the pool in a couple of spots are great. They're hard b/c they're concrete, but they keep you cool because they're a couple of inches beneath the water level.9. We were with a corporate group, and alll of the activities and services associated with our seminars were great.NEGATIVES:1. This is our biggest complaint. The open-air lobby is beautiful, with seating areas all over. The problem comes in with volume of the music and the activities. (My husband is 39 and I am 44, so we're not crabby old people.) A lobby should have background music, not loud speakers that make it impossible to talk. In the evening, a female singer and a piano player perform right next to the lobby bar, and the decibel level is deafening because of the amplification system. Even if you go to the farthest seating area in the lobby, you still have to scream to be heard by the person sitting in the chair next to yours. They say that part of the problem is that the hotel is struggling (40+% occupancy when we were there the first week of December, which is the high season). As a result, they supposedly allow locals to use the hotel facilities. I'm assuming that it was local people who were dancing in the aisles of the lobby to the singer's music, encouraging her. There is another bar next to the casino, 50 steps from the lobby, called the Fun Bar. It has a stage, couches, disco lights, etc. We think this is where the live entertainment should occur. During one rainy day, a game of bingo was conducted in the lobby. Again, even though the players were all seated within 20 feet of the caller, she used the amplification equipment, so anyone else trying to enjoy the lobby in peace was subjected to her obnoxious screaming. Even going to the farthest point in the lobby didn't help that day. We left.At the pool, there are two stereo systems, one near the bar and one near the activities hut where you pick up towels, etc. They play different music, but you can hear both from almost all parts of the pool area. The girls in the activities hut constantly change the volume, stop and restart songs, etc. It's just obnoxious.2. After the fact, we learned that each room is supposed to come equipped with two umbrellas. Ours had none. On the morning it rained, we sprinted to the shuttle stop hut, and waited over 1/2 hour for the shuttle to come. It never did. (It's supposed to make the rounds every 5 minutes.) When the rain subsided a bit, we ran to the lobby. When we told the porter that the shuttle hadn't come, he said he hadn't seen it in over an hour. He told us to complain at the front desk, which we did. 3. Staff at pool bar were lazy. Not very attentive to female patrons, if unescorted. Waitress one day sat on stool at bar, talking to bartenders and lifeguard and didn't even make rounds of pool area to take drink orders.4. Much of staff seem young and immature. They play around with each other a lot, instead of tending to the guests. Probably has a lot to do with negatives 1. and 3. above.5. There really is no beach. I thought it would be small, but people weren't even venturing into it. The sand is riddled with large rocks and broken shells.6. This is slightly minor, but the stools in the swim up bar are too high.7. There were mites running around the ice cream container in the Avacado restaurant one afternoon at lunch.CONCLUSION:While it was a very nice hotel, I wouldn't rate it a 5-star or give it membership in the Leading Hotels because it's just not elegant enough for the price ($600 per night). It's ambience is slightly forced and amateurish. At $300 a night, I'd stay there again, but, without that reduction, we'd try the El Conquistador next time.

<Rating>5	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Know What to Expect and Prepare Accordingly Just returned from a quick weekend getaway here with my wife. We were a little worried after some of the reviews, but decided to act on some previous tips left on this board and in some ways, altered our expectations.The property itself is beautiful. The lobby and common areas, restaurants and rooms were very nice. The beds, however, are rock hard. If you have trouble sleeping on a hard bed, don't stay here. The property is also very large, thus, request in advance a bungalow nearer the service areas if you don't want to have long walks to the restaurants and pools. The resort shuttles run regularly, but are not always there when you're ready.The restaurants were good. Before you arrive (5-7 days), call and speak with the concierge and insist on making reservations at the reservation only restaurants prior to arrival, otherwise, you will be eating at the buffet restaurants. Breakfast and lunch are buffets, food is okay, but not great. The reservation restaurants were really good. Drinks were non-stop at a variety of bars, but a little slow when seated at a table. At dinner, a variety of wine options were offered and all sampled were good. The pool area is great, very expansive. If you want to avoid music, the activities crowd and kids, you will want to reserve your room with Service Royale, which has a private pool and bar w/ no kids. The beach has water sports (kayaks, sail boats) for use, but it's not a swim/snorkel beach. The resort has a one towel per person rule as well that works through a card trade-in system, which for a high-end resort was a little disappointing.Nightime activity is a little slow. A cruise style entertainment show is offered each night around 10. There is a small casino. The lobby bar area has live music nightly and many guests mingle in this area. We rented a car since it was the same cost as the shuttle provided by the resort ($60 per person round trip). It's about a 30 minute drive from the airport. Rule of the road in PR seems to be that traffic lanes and lights are merely suggestions...drive carefully. The car was nice as the resort is about a 10 minute drive to the El Yunque rainforest, which makes for a nice day trip and we didn't have to book a package through the resort. The resort charges $10 a day for parking, which I thought was a little odd given there was ample parking available throughout the resort. I think locals use the casino and also the convention meeting area for private events, thus the charge. The spa onsite is very well equipped, but also very expensive. Take what you expect to pay at a normal resort spa and add about 50%.We enjoyed our weekend for what it was...a quick getaway. The staff is friendly, but not always attentive...they definetly run on island time. I did find that a well placed $5 tip at the bar or to a cocktail waiter would keep you in good drink more quickly...otherwise, all gratuities are included. For me, the food variety was wearing thin by night 3, so I could not imagine a week-long stay. For the price we paid ($435 room rate secured through lhw website) we felt it was an excellent value for comparable services and what would have been spent had the resort not been all-inclusive. If you do go, a few tips: - Make Restaurant Reservations for Romantico and Bamboo before you go. Politely insist via phone call to concierge. - If you want to avoid children and noise, book w/ Service Royale. - If you are wanting to enjoy the pool bar portion of the all-inclusive, seek lounge chairs near the bar. You're going to be walking to the bar quite often...the pool bar cocktail waitress is non-existent. - Footwear is a good idea for walking on the beach. The area is ideal for watersports, but not for swimming or snorkeling. If you're looking for those activities, this resort is not for you. - Don't expect Ritz or Four Season service, do expect courteous employees and a very scenic property

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Getaway for the Family We just returned from four days with our two girls (ages 4 and 6) at the Paradisus Resort in Puerto Rico where we had a terrific time. We found the location, atmosphere, amenities and accommodations completely to our satisfaction for a quick getaway in the carribean. The resort is very attractive with beautiful decorative pools, parrots and lovely open air sitting areas in the main building with comfortable, well appointed and modern sitting areas and decor. THe bathrooms are immaculate and quite impressive looking. The staff for the most part was extremely friendly and provided good service. We did the Royal Service level which from what I could tell allowed us to check in within a separate area furnished comfortably, an offer of a fresh towel, television and refreshments. Also our room faced the ocean and included a tub with jets (jacuzzi like) on the open patio which the kids loved after being at the pool all day. The turndown service and chocolates on the pillows were a nice treat. (one minor complaint - when I asked the butler about the gratuity situation he responded that it was included but we were welcome to tip whoever we wanted - I would have preferred he said it's all included and that's it.)WE stayed in one room which had a big king size bed (a little hard but comfortable) and pullout couch which was fine since we did not spend much time there. It was very comfortable and clean.. and included a small refrigerator stocked with juice, water and soda at all times. The bathroom had a huge walk in shower and enormous towels and nice bathrobes. The pool layout was our absolutely favorite part... big and inviting with a small baby pool attached and 3 and 4 foot deep areas for swimming. (The beach was okay.. kind of rocky and mucky in the water but the kids loved scavenging for hermit crabs). I loved the big covered canopy beds around the pool area for lounging as well as the lounge seating in the pool itself. We all loved swimming over to the pool side bar and sitting in the water to order drinks. My four year old became a big fan of virgin strawberry daiquiris and highly recommend the mojitos! THere is also poolside drink service but it was kind of sporadic and if you want something to munch in you do have to walk back to one of the restaurants.The activity hut was a center of things happening all day long for adults and kids. Music plays constantly and they announce different scheduled events including water aerobics, pool volleyball and basketball.. there's a ping pong table, pool tabel and oversized chess game as well as lots of different fun board games, float boards and noodles to borrow. They will watch children ages five to twelve also and have salsa lessons poolside in the afternoon. There is also a small playground area right by the pool with a table that had occasional craft projects in the afternoon. The only slight downside for small kids was the evening after dinner there was usually a show of some sort but not until 10 pm. I found out after a couple of days that they also had a fun kids disco and games at 9:30 each night but this was not well publicized. The staff were great with kids. Also one night we were told there would be crafts and activities before the show and it never materialized.Food-wise we were very pleased with the choice of six restaurants. We ate breakfast and lunch every day in the open air patio restaurant by the beach which is a buffet with lots of good healthy and not so healthy choices! Our favorite restaurant was Bamboo for a delicious beni-hana type meal. Make your reservations because it's worth it and they have a kids menu for an alternative. WE never ate at Romantico because children must be twelve or older but heard from many it was fabulous for french food, atmosphere and service. We were pleased by the other restaurants (all buffets), found pizza and an Olive Garden type menu at the Italian place and did okay at the Puerto Rican and California restaurant.WE also utilized the babysitting service which was reasonable ( $12 per hour for two children and a $15 transportation fee) to get away and play nine holes of golf which was also very nice. The woman was very friendly and loved children (Evelyn) and brought a bag of toys and games to play with!All in all a great getaway and change of scenery for people with our without children!

Especially good was a guitarist named Juan Carlos--he is extremely talented as a guitar player (flamenco, classical, and contemporary) and had a magnificent voice. The rest of the entertainment was up to cruise ship standards. The casino was petite and it was clear that nobody was winning.It didn't really matter that there was a special pool for Royal Service clientele, because there was no sun or reason to go to the pool the entire time we were there.Do yourselves a favor and rent a car at the airport and you'll save money. Car rental at the hotel is more expensive and their shuttle service is costly. Even when the weather is good, you'll at least want to visit El Yunque, the rainforest (bring your National Park Service Golden Eagle Pass and you won't have to pay the entrance fee at the Visitor's Center). You should also see Old San Juan, with lovely shops, great Spanish Colonial architecture and a fabulous Indian restaurant--called Tantra (the chef previously was head chef at the defunct Hyatt Cerromar). We've eaten Indian food all over the world, and this restaurant ranks in the top 3.Parking costs $10/day and there are not enough spaces. The system for payment is stupid and archaic. There seem to be more local conventions going on at Paradisus, than couples or families visiting from off-island, so that is why we think the parking lot situation was always dire. While the rain kept pouring we had nothing better to do, so we drove just to look over the Westin and the Wyndham (mentioned above). They both were more established and lusher, obviously more upscale looking than Paradisus. The El Conquistador was hard to find, but looked spectacular from the little we saw. On the way to the airline terminal we met a couple who had spent a few days there, and they confirmed the attitude problem with the service there, but were not too put out by the food prices.I think that next time I go on a tropical vacation I won't be so put off by spending the entire arrival and departure days travelling with connecting flights, and we'll go someplace that I've always longed to go--like Virgin Gorda or St. Lucia.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The good and the bad After waiting for all of the opening kinks to work themselves out I finally visited the Paradisus 11/06-09 with some female friends, all in our early 40's. I am 20 year plustravel agent and searched out a great rate of $350.00 per night on Sol Melia's website for each room.The Positives:Absolutely beautiful property despite the lack of a swimmable or attractive beach.The public areas come close to any Ritz Carlton or Four Seasons, great decor in all of the restaurants and lounges, extremely clean and well kept, stunning bathrooms, obviously money well spent in building this property. The rooms were lovely although mine had a mustly odor and they are a touch dark. The hard beds do growon you after a night or two. The grounds are very nice and the landscaping is filling in all around. The food was very good except for Toscano, the Italian buffet which the staff tends to push you towards. Avocados has an excellent buffet for all 3 meals. Both Romantico and Bamboo were worth the visit, great food and service. Even though they say they will not take reservations before you arrive for either, insist on it, otherwise you will be dissapointed when you arrive if you're only there for a short stay. We had to jump thru hoops to get reservations at each once we arrived, but it was worth it. What the hotel is lacking in is available snacks with your drinks poolside during the day. The Royal Service Pool was a pleasure and the covered king beds around the pool were heaven, but many times during the day we kept saying some chips and salsa would be nice or some type of snack without having to take the long walk back to one of the restaurants.Service was spotty. The bar staff all around was excellent as were most of the restaurant staff but you found at least a couple of lazy workers in each restaurant.We made a habit of tipping the better bartenders and wait staff and found them to then be even more attentive, it's worth the $5 or $10 here and there.The spa was wonderful. I had two seperate treatments and found the facilities to be very nice and the therapists well trained, although their 50 minute treatments are more like 45 minutes.The Negatives:If you are 3 or more people don't bother with the Paradisus shuttle when you arrive at the airport. It runs $30.00 per person each way. We were 6 and the rep tried to put the 6 of us in a delapidated taxi-van at the Paradisus cost of $180.00 total. The taxi driver didn't speak the best English and was confused by the Paradisus rep's voucher. I asked what the actual cost was and found it was $66.50 plus tip. We sent the rep on his way with a tip for his trouble and paid the taxi driver directly. We did use the shuttle on the return as some of us had different flights and knew it would be difficult to get a taxi from the hotel.The beach is an unfortunate failure and from what I can see is unredeemable. The water is murky as far out as you can see and the sand is quite muddy. They do have lounge chairs spread around the higher level of sand which is still mostly dirt with broken shells spread throughout but there is never anyone in them or in the water unless they are taking a kayak or sunfish sailboat ride. The hotel is best marketed not as a beach resort and I think they are learning to take the focus off the beach.We were upgraded from the standard room to Royal Service rooms and were very grateful. However, checkin was very confusing, first I was told my 3 rooms was actually 1 for 6 people yet 6 could not stay in one room, obviously! After 1 hour of waiting in the lounge we were given our 3 rooms at 4pm but they weren't ready. We were shuffled off to lunch and at 5pm the rooms were ready but it took another 25 minutes to get our luggage. There were 2 large groups in-house and the hotel was sold out that evening, it showed. When I asked about dinner reservations for our 3 evenings I was told Romantico and Bamboo were sold out and we should go to Toscano. I had called the day prior to arrival and refused reservation and told we would have no problem when we arrived. When I informed the girl of this she got us dinner in Romantico for our 3rd night.Toscano is a beautiful restaurant but the food was mediocre at best. In addition, you wait 10-15 minutes to be seated in a half empty restaurant. People are lined out the door with many available tables inside. It's buffet service, no reason to keep you waiting for a table. After dinner I stopped back in the RS Lounge to insist on reservations for Bamboo the next night and after describing out unsatisfactory meal at Toscano I was told they would see what they could do. Later that night I had a message confirming Romantico for the next night also but still no Bamboo. It was not until an incident the next day that they finally obtained a 930pm reservation ourlast night and Romantico the second night.Watch your valuables. Put everything in the room safe. One of my traveling companions came in off her balcony to find a staff member going through the purse of her roomate who was at the gym. He lied to excuse himself and apologized but he unfortunately tried to cover for himself with management with a different story and in the end was not believed. The incident was reported and the management took the information and assured us it was a very serious issue but in the end the man was just suspended for 4 days, so we heard thru another employee. There was no further contact from management after the incident and it did not leave a very good taste in our mouth's. Fortunately nothing was actually stolen.Conclusion:For the rate we paid, it was a very good value. I did advise management that they have a long way to go before they can command the type of prices they are asking during the high season. There are still a number of issues with the property that need to be worked out. I think though despite the beach, this will eventually be a top resort for those just looking for a relaxing getaway in nice surroundings.

<Content>Paradisus Is As Nice As The Brochure Returned yesterday from 5 days at the Paradisus. It is absolutely beautiful. They boast six restaurants, but 3 are together in adjacent rooms. There was some overcharging the first day due to the employee at Cabrera not speaking English. Evidently she lied to Cabrera about speaking English. When I returned the 2nd day for the rainforest car, Cabrera reduced the overcharges and satisfied me. What the employee did not tell us is there is a $25 charge if Cabrera must pick up the car at the hotel. They were very fair in that regard after I told the 2nd day employee about the pick up charge. The concierge will arrange your hotel sponsored trips and/or the rental cars.Rooms were beautiful. All are suites. The royal upgrade we did not participate in. I do not think you have to unless you want to have an direct ocean view. A slightly obstructed ocean view is what you get otherwise.Bathrooms are granite (marble?). Towels are huge - maybe 5 feet long. Great for the women wrapping around themselves.Had a great time. I would go again.

My only question is why on all these websites do they say that Paradisus is in San Juan?? It's not! It's in Rio Grande, which is about a 45 minute drive East of San Juan....right on Coco Beach. That we found to be very confusing because we didn't realize that it was almost an hour to the hotel...but I'm glad that we rented a car so we could explore on our own!We had a wonderful time and Paradisus Puerto Rico is an amazing resort and we hope to go back real soon!

The staff was very friendly, but the service was very inconsistent. The bars were short staffed most of the time and it took a long time to get a drink. On 3 occasions in a 5 day period, the bars ran out of Coconut Rum! The food was average. Breakfast at the poolside cafe offers a buffet that most of the items were cold. Avocado's also offers a breakfast that was much better. The lunch was decent, the highlight being steak and lobster (which they conveniently were in short supply of each day). Dinner at Bamboo was horrible one evening and great a few days later. A lot of this had to do with the inexperienced chief we had the first time. The French restaurant was not very good. The steak meal offered was cold and tasted like pot roast Room service was quick with a limited menu. The evening entertainment provided was good. The beds in the rooms were very hard and the rooms did have high speed internet that was very inconsistent. If you like a beach vacation, this is not the place to go. There is no sandy beach available at this resort you can lay out at. The pool was very nice. The lobby area was very nice with lots of marble but BE CAREFUL- It gets very slippery when it rains. We saw several adults and children fall. I would wait a while before considering to vacation at this resort. The reviews we read on trip advisor were very helpful preparing us for this vacation. I would want to see more positive reviews before booking a trip at the Paradisus Puerto Rico.   
<Date>May 23, 2004
<Rating>2	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>BGJohnson
<Content>Give it a year... We visited the Paradisus as part of a large group in early May. When (if?) this resort works out all its kinks, it will be a top-notch world-class resort.Most of the resort is open-air. Whoever decorated this property spared no expense when it came to architecture. Polished marble and koi ponds abound, along with hundreds of cozy nooks with plush sofas and leather chairs and candles aplenty. Absolutely stunning is the only way to describe the atmosphere.That said, the staff seems to run on their own time, not guests' time. Be prepared to wait for everything. It took two hours after check-in for our bags to be delivered to our room. Our group's welcome reception was set by the pool, but the resort hadn't made arrangments for any lighting, and we mingled and ate in pitch dark.Make your dinner reservations for every night the very day you arrive because reservations are hard to come by. The Bamboo restaurant was tops (asian-themed, with 12 to a table and a grill as the main attraction), but Romantico was our favorite. Elegant fare like lobster bisque and seafood crepes, candles and a stroling violinist help set the stage for a romantic evening. There is also an Italian buffet, Toscano, that was scrumptious. The poolside grill offered mediocre daytime fare but was best in the morning because it featured cooked-to-order omelets that were mouth-watering. Don't bother with room service because we ordered several times and the results were always the same - it took 1 1/2 hour to arrive and when it did the food was cold.The resort offers rental car arrangements, but the rentals are not on-property. We ordered a car for 9AM one day and it didn't arrive until noon. $65/day for a compact car. It's 45 minutes to San Juan, so if you plan on seeing Puerto Rico you WILL need a way to get around. Daily excursions were expensive, averaging $70/pp for a 1/2 day excursion to the rainforest (10 minutes from the resort) to $92/pp for an arranged horseback morning excursion.Nightly entertainment was, for the most part, pretty average cruise ship style stage shows. The adjacent casino was mediocre. The beach was small, though pristine and well-maintained. The pool was fabulous. Don't count on swimming in the ocean, though. The entire perimeter of the waterfront is surrounded by coral reefs, and almost everyone who ventured in the water in our group ended up with wounds to their hands, legs, and feet. Catamarans and kayaks are free to guests, but because of the coral the property doesn't offer any motorized water crafts for rent.The Kids Club offered few activities, though the pool cabana was stocked with board games. The brochure boasted nightly karaoke and a dance club, in addition to aerobics, yoga, and salsa dance classes, but those things were not available during our visit. Souvenirs with the resorts name on them (namely t-shirts, etc) were not available, either, which disappointed our kids.Even if they were slow, the staff was SO friendly it was difficult to be upset about it. The architecture of the majority of the resort was SO stunning that in and of itself it made up for many of the downsides. Still, they have a long way to go. They need a minimum of a year to get their act together before they live up to their hype. I wouldn't go back before that...  
<Date>May 15, 2004
<Rating>2	4	5	-1	3	-1	2	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Getting Better I have just returned from a 5 day stay at the Paradisus Puerto Rico. I stayed there as a part of a large group (about 80 people). Our stay was wonderful, but the resort still has a way to go before I would think of returning. I echo the comments made about the beach, it is pretty much non-existent, the water was very shallow and hard to swim in. The pool area was, by far, it's best feature! The staff was very attentive and assisted us in every way they could, even as far as playing our groups own CD's at the pool bar. We loved the Bamboo resturant, but make your reservations early! One of the most common complaint from our group was the stiffness of the beds. They were the hardest beds we had every felt. After a long night enjoying the entertainment on site, though, the hardness of the bed did not matter much! There were still the problems I have read about previously re: some of our group had difficulty initially getting into their hotel rooms as the electronic key did not work, plumbing problems, the landscaping not being completed, the mini bar was not refilled everyday, our room was not made up until after 5PM one of the days...but all in all, this will be a wonderful resort when all the little kinks are worked out.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Paradisus was great Hi I am a travel agent that just returned with a group of travel agents that did a site inspection of the Paradisus. My impressions were that yes, it does still need some work, but if you stayed there, you will not be disappointed. There are not a lot of people staying there yet, due to the fact that they are still finishing up all the rooms and that it is a new resort, so there is not a lot of action going on yet. However, if you want to play games at the pool, have a good time, the staff was more than willing to help. I am sure in time there will be an excellent kids program when more kids are staying there. Typically, there are not usually any structured programs for teenagers at all inclusives anyway, but when there are more people there, they will be able to meet them and make friends.The resort is absolutely lovely, and for an all inclusive resort, they have excellent food, even on the buffets. They have a great variety of food and it is not the same every day either. The dinner restaurants, Bamboo and Romantico, where you have to make reservations, were really really good. The service was excellent, if a little slow, but please remember that it takes time after a hotel opens to get the staff trained and coordinated. It will be fine. I think it was nice that most of the restaurants were air conditioned, and you don't often find that at all inclusive resorts.The entertainment at night was top-notch, and much better than what I have seen at other all inclusives. The casino was very nice, and a fairly large size. They have lots of meeting and banquet rooms and will be able to accomodate groups very nicely.I thought the rooms, all junior suites, were a very good size. The maid service was ok, there were a few things missing the 1st night, like no soap, but they were very accomodating and brought it right away. There were also a few construction things in the rooms, like they need to get the bathtubs to drain properly, that they are still working on. The beach is nice, a few pebbles here and there, not the most gorgeous beach in the world. So if you are looking for miles and miles of white sand beach, it is not here, not yet. We spoke to the hotel manager, and they said they were working on the situation and they may be able to work on the beach, but they are constrained by the Puerto Rico natural resource department, that wants to preserve the environment as much as possible. So within a few months, hopefully they will be able to spread some more sand on the beach. Some people from our group went in the water, and said it was really nice, not too deep (great for small kids), and very warm. But, I tell you, the pools make up for the beach-they are awesome!So, to me the hotel will be fine-just give it a little more time to mature. We as Americans are so demanding, we want things now, what they have now is absolutely fine, with more to come. The greatest treasure the Paradisus has is the staff-they were the friendliest I have ever met, everyone was very eager to please, and the concierge desk, which was always very busy, was excellent and very patient with the guests.

<Content>not what they advertise Went to the Paradisus PR for spring break with my husband and 2 sons, ages 11 and 15. I agree with other reviewers during this time period. The property just opened and had a lot of glitches. As time went on, there were more clients and the children had more friends. However, there was little for the teenagers to do. The game room was just for videogames. They could certainly have used a pool table or two. The rooms were just okay, spacious, but certainly not 5 star. The housekeeping was terrible. The grounds were not lush and the garden view was very sad-looking. The service was fairly poor in the restaurants and rooms, though everyone was very friendly. Basically, this property will take about 3 years to get up to the level of a true 5 star, Leading Hotel of the World standard.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not too bad We booked the Paradisus over the summer with much anticipation. The first all-inclusive resort in Puerto Rico had much appeal. But, when it didn't open in December, January or February, we booked the Westin as a back-up. At the last minute, we decided to take the plunge and stay at the Paradisus for our spring break vacation - April 3-April 8. Positives - beautiful property in spite of the fact that it's not complete. Lovely pool area, a beautiful and welcoming lobby, spacious rooms (we stayed comfortably in a junior suite with our two children ages 11 and 13, excellent fitness center, 4 barely used tennis courts, a good choice of restaurants, excellent service. The staff just wanted to please. Concerns - a very disappointing beach; instead of a wide, white sand beach, it was narrow and full of gravel. I don't know if improvement plans are underway, but I do hope so. The food was adequate, nothing special, but satisfactory for an all-inclusive resort. Bamboo was actually very good and we're dining at Romantico tomorrow night which other guests have said is wonderful. There was still quite a bit of work going but it never felt instrusive. The grounds are still being landscaped so it didn't have that lush feeling of other, more mature resorts. Our experience here is certainly atypical. A large section of rooms are still incomplete so it felt quite empty. There was getting up early to claim chairs or umbrellas, no lines at the buffet for the bar, no difficulty with dinner reservations. It's difficult to know how the staff will handle the crowds once it's totally complete and filled to capacity. I would recommend the resort now and believe it will be really terrific by Christmas vacation!
